Special Telecommunications Issue

The Voice of the Telecommunications Industry

New Year's Greetings

— Lü Bing

Time flies like an arrow; in the blink of an eye, we have reached the new year of the Republic of China, year twenty-four. Leaving behind the old and ushering in the new, this time of year naturally brings a new atmosphere to society, and the people of the nation hold new hopes. This publication is no exception, and as the new year begins, we would like to express what we wish to say.

The progress of the telecommunications industry comes with the needs of society. The more society needs telecommunications, the faster telecommunications will develop. Therefore, the prosperity of society greatly affects the telecommunications industry. In recent years, foreign aggression has brought economic decline, many rural areas have gone bankrupt, and the business world is in a slump. Under such circumstances, even if the telecommunications sector itself does its best to reorganize and build, the increase in business may not meet the authorities' expectations. Therefore, the development of telecommunications truly depends on the improvement of the domestic situation. The past is already history, but we hope that starting this year, the entire nation will cooperate further, society will become more stable, and all industries will gradually become more prosperous. In this way, the telecommunications industry will also see greater expansion. This is our first hope.

In the past year, the various facilities of the telecommunications authorities have been reported in the news, so there is no need to repeat them. Time flies, and there is no end to telecommunications. Measures that have already been determined and began in the past, if they do not need to be continued, should be completed this year. New initiatives for improvement should observe the needs of the industry and aim for active development this year. In particular, it is hoped that the entire telecommunications industry will share the same goals and work together. This is our second hope.

This publication has been in circulation for over a year. Although it has been able to meet readers' expectations to a certain extent, it cannot be said to be completely satisfactory. As the new year arrives, our desire for innovation is even stronger. We hope that those outside and within the telecommunications industry will send us new works on telecommunications, striving for them to be insightful and original, not falling into old ways, so that the content of this publication will be more substantial and精彩. This is our third hope.

New Year, New Year, filled with many new hopes. To realize these hopes, continuous effort is essential. The year has begun, and the scenery is greatly renewed. We respectfully wish progress to all sectors and look forward to their efforts in the new year!

The New Spirit of the Telecommunications Industry

— Zhen

Years pass quickly, and the New Year's Day of the twenty-fourth year is upon us again. New Year's Day is the happiest day of life and the most exciting day of life. Why is it the happiest day? Because we work diligently throughout the year, with no spare time. Some toil physically, engaging in personal careers, while others fret mentally, serving the country. On this New Year's holiday, everyone enjoys themselves, raising glasses to celebrate the year, filled with joy. Why is it the most exciting day? Because our lives are limited, but our careers are endless. In the fleeting decades, besides childhood, old age, and illness, how many days can we work? How many things can we accomplish? Considering the days we can be productive and the bodies we can use, how can we not concentrate our spirits and act swiftly? New Year's Day is the starting point for a year filled with this new spirit, so it is the most exciting day. If individuals can implement this new spirit, what cannot be accomplished? If the nation can implement this new spirit, what enemy cannot be defeated?

Among the Western material civilizations imitated in our country, telegraphy was the earliest, starting with Li Hongzhang's memorial on handling foreign affairs in the fifth year of the Guangxu reign. Over fifty years have passed. Why have we not only failed to keep pace with Europe and America but also become known for corruption? Although it is said to be influenced by the times, it is also due to poor planning. What is poor planning? It is the lack of a new spirit to aid it. Given China's vast area and large population, it is unreasonable to say that there is no need for a telecommunications industry! With the power of the national government above and the economic power of the people below, it is also unbelievable that the telecommunications industry cannot be developed! However, those in charge of telecommunications are either stuck in the past and do not know how to advance, or they fear difficulties and seek only to maintain the status quo, or they rely on politicians and military figures and do not publicly reveal their needs and realities to society, seeking their sympathy and assistance. As for those who use telecommunications as a means to get promoted or get rich, they are even more contemptible. Due to these factors, China's telecommunications industry has stagnated for fifty years, following old ways and declining. "Decades are like one day."

From now on, if there is no new spirit to aid it, who knows if fifty years later, we will not be as we are today?

What is the new spirit? It is the spirit of not avoiding hardship, not minding grievances, having meticulous thinking, and great courage, with career as the premise and service as the goal. The achievements of telecommunications administration in the past year are clearly visible: regarding international communication, there is the opening of the China-UK and China-Japan wireless circuits; regarding domestic communication, there is the construction of remote radio stations such as Kangding and Lhasa, the establishment of fifty-one telegraph offices such as Jiangling and Tai'ning, the organization of combined telegraph and telephone business offices and agencies, the merger of wireless radio, and the success of postal and telecommunications integration. In addition, regarding the determination of organizational systems, the improvement of business regulations, the unification of financial revenue and expenditure, the implementation of engineering plans, the consolidation of telecommunications businesses run by the ministry, provinces, and private enterprises, the recovery of external sovereign interests, the diligence of telecommunications personnel, and the credibility of society, this publication has repeatedly recorded. Society has its own evaluation, so there is no need to elaborate. Some say that the changes in China's telecommunications industry in the past year almost exceed the accumulation of reforms over the past fifty years, which is no exaggeration. How was this achieved? The new spirit, that's it.

The principle of reversal after extremity is clearly stated in ancient teachings. The revival from decline is a common occurrence. However, it also depends on the spirit of those in charge. If they believe that the career is at its most extreme point of decline and do not think about how to save it, merely pacing back and forth in the courtyard, sighing in the room, then the career will inevitably decline and never recover. If someone emerges, observes the cause of the illness, seeks the way to diagnose it, enthusiastically does it, and resolutely implements it, then its effect will often exceed our expectations. Looking at China's telecommunications in the past two years or several years ago, it was bound by unequal treaties externally and ravaged by natural disasters and bandits internally, with accumulated causes of corruption and a fragmented situation. Who would not be infinitely pessimistic and believe that it was beyond salvation? However, the telecommunications industry in the past year, after the authorities' combing, weeding, supporting, and reorganizing, has proven to be a complete success. This is the power of the new spirit.

However, if it is said that the telecommunications industry has done its best in reorganization in the past year and has reached the peak of development, who would dare to believe it? Not only is it unable to compare with Europe and America, but it is also inferior to Japan. Not only has Director-General's plan to build wired and wireless circuits not been realized, but the improvement of existing局　　　must also be doubled. Moreover, the international situation is often tense, the national economy is in dire straits, politics still needs to be clarified, and the communist bandits have long been condemned by Heaven. All these facts are indirectly and directly related to telecommunications. Fortunately, the transportation authorities will never be satisfied with the status quo and will never be afraid of the adverse environment. The past has become history, and there must be new initiatives in the new year. Let us wait and see.

At this New Year's Day, we should have an extremely happy view, make the greatest determination, have unlimited hope, implement the new spirit of the individual, and serve the country and society. At the same time, we should support the government's new spirit, develop state-owned enterprises, not be pessimistic, not be impetuous, always persevere, and be resolute in dealing with things. The final victory belongs to us. As the ancients said, "The plan for the year lies in spring." Please start from now.

International Radio Stations in the Coming Year

— Zhang Chenghu

In the New Year's Day supplement last year, there was an article titled "A Glimpse of International Radio Stations," which detailed the construction of international radio stations by the transportation authorities, as well as the existing equipment and business conditions. Time passes easily, and another year has passed. The efforts of our transportation authorities in construction have not slackened at all during this year. Therefore, the development process of our country's only external　　　speaking international radio station during the year should also be a concern for all interested parties. Therefore, I will describe its equipment, business, and other items separately as follows:

(A) Expanding Equipment

To achieve the development of wireless telecommunications business, it depends on accurate and fast communication. The accuracy and speed of communication depend on complete and thorough equipment. "Good tools make good work" is an ancient saying. The International Radio Station has been established for four years, and its scale is roughly complete. In order to improve business and meet needs, the equipment has been expanded every year. The following were completed within the past year:

(Marconi Machine) This machine began to be installed in January of the 22nd year of the Republic of China and was completed in February of the 23rd year. It includes two 20-kilowatt shortwave transmitters, with two sets of beam antennas for Europe and one set of beam antennas for the United States. There are also four shortwave receivers, with three sets of beam antennas for Europe and two sets of beam antennas for the United States. Since the completion of the machine, the machine distribution and wavelength changes of the European and American communication lines can be easily handled.

(Armored Underground Cable) The transmitting station of the International Radio Station is located in Zhenru, Shanghai, the receiving station is located in Liuhang, Baoshan, and the central control is located in the Sassoon Building on Renji Road, Public Concession, Shanghai. The connection between the three locations depends on remote control lines. The original remote control lines of the station were overhead cables and copper bare wires, which were prone to theft, insect bites, wind damage, and fire damage, causing many obstacles. For the purpose of fundamental relief, a 50-pair armored underground cable was added, starting from the wiring room south of Hengfeng Bridge. It passes through Hengfeng Road, Datong Road, Jiaotong Road, and Taopu West Road in Zhabei, and reaches the Zhenru transmitting station; then from the transmitting station through Zhenda Road, Hutai Road, and Baoshan County Road, it reaches the Liuhang by-reporting station. The entire line is 42.87 li long, and five test line boxes are set up along the line. It began to be used in January of the 23rd year. The original overhead cables are still reserved for occasional needs, so the remote control lines of the International Station are in no danger of being interrupted.

(Zhenru Power Plant) The power supply for the Zhenru transmitting station was supplied by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company. Its power supply lines were very long and prone to obstruction. For the sake of safety, a standby power plant was self-equipped in the station, with a 600-horsepower diesel engine as the prime mover, and a power generation capacity of 400 kilowatts, which was sufficient for the entire station. The project was completed in February of the 23rd year. Since then, whenever the city power is cut off, the machine can be started for power supply immediately, so there is no need to worry about affecting the telegraph service.

(Liuhang Transformer Station) The Liuhang receiving station was originally located in a remote rural area and could not purchase city power, so it set up its own power plant to meet its needs. In the spring of the 23rd year, the Dachang Dayao Electric Company purchased power from the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to supply residents in the area. The station took the opportunity to contact the company, borrowed capital, extended the power supply line to the Liuhang receiving station, and installed a 50-kilowatt, 6,600-volt to 380-volt, three-transformer station in the station. It was completed and commissioned in July, and Liuhang Electric Economy also has the dual protection of city power and self-provided power.

(Repair Shop) The International Station was still in its initial stage of establishment, and there were no factory equipment. The repair and replacement of machine parts was very inconvenient. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications decided to attach a repair shop to the Zhenru transmitting station of the station, equipped with lathes, drilling machines, planers, and all hand tools. It was installed and completed in March of the 23rd year. If the transmitting and receiving machine parts of the station are damaged, they will be repaired immediately, and the necessary replacement parts will be fully prepared; and in their spare time, they will engage in the manufacture of wireless machine parts for the use of radio stations throughout the country.

(Dedicated Line Exchange) For merchants and people to use telegraphs, speed is the first need, and the financial industry is even more so. The International Radio Station has dedicated lines connected to various banks and stockbrokers. Their telegraphs are sent and received through this dedicated line, using telephones or teletypewriters to transmit to each other. The delivery rate is doubled, and merchants and people are happy to use this dedicated line more and more. In order to meet the needs, the station successively installed two dedicated line exchanges in September and November of the 22nd year, which can accommodate 50 dedicated lines for telephones and teletypewriters each. Shanghai merchants who wish to send and receive telegraphs particularly quickly can contact the station to lease them.

(Relay Fast Machine) Relay refers to domestic telegrams being relayed through Shanghai to foreign countries, or foreign telegrams being relayed through Shanghai to the interior. The domestic part of handling this telegram is the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, and the foreign part is the International Radio Station. Therefore, there should be close and fast communication between the International and Shanghai Telegraph Bureaus. In view of this, the Ministry of Communications has specially prepared a Creed automatic sending and receiving fast machine for the bureau to handle relay reporting, which was also put into use in September of the 23rd year.

The above items are the new constructions completed by the International Radio Station in the 23rd year of the Republic of China. There are also noteworthy expansion equipment under construction as follows:

(Expansion of Central Control Room) The central control room is the central hub for sending and receiving telecommunications, and its responsibility is respectful and important. It should naturally expand with business needs. The central room of the International Station, located in the Sassoon Building, occupies about 2,000 square feet. Recently, due to the increasing number of reports, it is not enough to apply, so it was decided to expand the location by one time, adding sending and receiving tables, and dividing them into east and west parts with the original ones. The current report table has been arranged, and the application machine parts, such as automatic transmitters, wave wringing machines, paper pulling machines,　孔 machines, amplifiers, and time printing machines. They are purchased by the Ministry of Communications from the station itself or purchased by the material procurement committee. After completion, it can form 15 receiving positions and 9 sending positions, and allocate the American and European communication lines to the east and west parts, and the receiving and sending efficiency can be doubled.

(Adding Transmitters) The Zhenru transmitting station has added a 20 to 40 kilowatt shortwave transmitter. The internal installation has already　, but the antenna has not been completed yet. It can be tested around the middle of this month.

(Expanding Receiving Station) A new battery room has been built in the Liuhang receiving station, and the relocation of new and old batteries and charging boards is underway. The original battery location was converted into a receiver room, adding a diversity receiver and two sets of antennas for Europe and the United States, so that the diversity receiving method can be used to eliminate the drawbacks of shortwave fading. This project is expected to be completed around February of this year.

(Adding Wireless Telephone Equipment) Wireless telephones have made special progress in recent years, and European and American countries have successively adopted them as international communication weapons. My country's International Radio Station is catching up and is also proceeding to add wireless telephone equipment. The Ministry of Communications ordered receiving, transmitting, and control machines from the British Standard Electric Company in the autumn of the 22nd year of the Republic of China and allocated them to the International Radio Station for application. Although the machines have not yet arrived at the station, the machine installation location and antenna foundation have been surveyed and determined. As soon as the machines arrive, they can be installed and used.

(Purchase Standard Wave Meters) The wireless radio business is becoming more and more developed, the space electromagnetic waves are becoming more and more numerous, and mutual interference is also becoming more and more serious. The previous Madrid International Telecommunications Conference decided that the frequency of the electromagnetic waves emitted by each radio station should not differ by more than five ten-thousandths from the specified one and enforce it. International communication agencies must purchase extremely accurate standard wave meters. To test the frequency of the electromagnetic waves they emit and correct them from time to time. The International Radio Station has never had this equipment. Whenever electromagnetic waves interfere, it does not know which is right and wrong. Even if others falsely claim that the electromagnetic waves emitted by the International Radio Station are inaccurate, there is no way to test and defend it, so it can only swallow its anger and default. The Ministry of Communications has purchased a standard wave meter from the United States and ordered it to be allocated to the station, which will be installed in the Liuhang receiving station immediately, so that it can receive any electromagnetic waves from around the world and test them. It is not only for measuring the electromagnetic waves emitted by the station itself. (To be continued)

Telegraphs and the New Year

— Baozhen

The wheels of time are constantly moving forward, and the annual New Year has come to the world. People are driven by life and inevitably leave their hometowns to live in other places. Therefore, people in their hometowns, when they encounter the New Year festival, cannot help but miss their relatives and friends who are far away from their hometowns. Of course, travelers living in other places also miss their elders or other relatives and friends in their hometowns. Therefore, social customs often involve sending New Year greeting cards during the New Year season, partly to reciprocate politeness and partly to communicate. However, my country has a vast territory, and it takes more than a day or two for mail to reach its destination in distant places. Suppose a New Year greeting card is sent from Shanghai to a friend in Beiping on New Year's Day. It may take four or five days to reach the destination. After receiving the greeting card, the friend in Beiping, even if he replies immediately, will take another four or five days to reach Shanghai. This back and forth will take at least eight or nine days, and the New Year season is almost over. There are direct trains between Shanghai and Beiping, and transportation cannot be considered inconvenient. Then, in places where transportation is inconvenient, wouldn't it be ineffective to exchange greeting cards? How can we remedy this shortcoming? I dare to responsibly introduce only one method of using social telegraphs. No matter what place in the country, it can be sent and received immediately, and it will never delay your affairs. When relatives and friends receive a beautiful New Year telegram, they will of course reply with a telegram immediately, and they can receive it on the same day. Thousands of miles away, it is no different from meeting face to face. Therefore, if we use telegrams to wish our relatives and friends a Happy New Year, we will surely make them feel happy in spirit.

Every time the political and military circles of our country send telegrams to superiors or colleagues during the New Year, they often abuse official telegrams with printed telegram paper because they do not understand the regulations of the telegraph bureau. However, since New Year telegrams are of a private social nature, according to the revised regulations on charging and restricting official military telegrams, they cannot be sent as official telegrams. When the telegraph bureau encounters such official telegrams that do not comply with the regulations, they will be treated as official telegrams for private matters and detained. Moreover, recently, the responsible leaders of political and military agencies have expressed their deep sympathy for the Ministry of Communications' measures to crack down on official telegrams for private matters. It is reported that a staff member of the Political Training Office of a certain division, Li, was dismissed by the Military Commission for using the division's printed telegram paper to send private telegrams. Therefore, if public officials of political and military agencies want to send telegrams to their superiors or colleagues to congratulate them on the New Year or promotion, do not violate the regulations and send official telegrams, which may be detained in the middle, or even dismissed for this reason. You can send social telegrams in accordance with the regulations, which is not only legal but also avoids the risk of being detained. Isn't it killing two birds with one stone? Moreover, the price of social telegrams is low. No matter where in the country, whether in the same province or another province, each Chinese character costs only two cents, which is three cents less than the five cents per character for official telegrams. Isn't it even cheaper?

If the name of the recipient of a Chinese social telegram is within two characters and the name of the receiving location is within 15 characters, it can also be calculated as five characters according to the new provincial fee regulations. For example, the telegram "Wang Junnian, No. 1087, Yian Lane, Albert Road, Shanghai - I sincerely wish my brother a prosperous future in the New Year" is charged only for 20 characters, which only needs to pay 40 cents, which can be said to be extremely low. During this New Year festival, for ladies and gentlemen from all walks of life who want to send New Year greetings to relatives and friends in distant places, only this cheap and good-quality social telegram can satisfy you.

Explanation of Telegraph Terminology (Continued)

— Qinghua

Various telegraph regulations and articles in this publication often use telegraph terminology. Those in the know can understand it at a glance, without any difficulty. However, those outside the industry often find the meaning unclear and difficult to understand. Therefore, I will continue to annotate the commonly used terms below:

Telecommunications: The abbreviation for telegraph is "telegram," and the abbreviation for telephone is "telephone." The term "telecommunications" is a collective term for telegraphs and telephones. Whether wired or wireless telegraphs, local or long-distance telephones, as well as facsimile telegrams, broadcasting, and wireless radio, all refer to "telecommunications." When we say telecommunications industry, it includes all the above-mentioned electrical communication businesses.

Incoming Telegram: It is the telegram sent, that is, the telegram received by the recipient.

Outgoing Telegram: It is the telegram sent out, that is, the telegram delivered by the sender.

Relay Telegram: It is the telegram relayed by the intermediate telegraph bureau.

Telegram Base: It is the telegram paper with the telegram text written on it. The outgoing telegram base is the telegram base originally written by the sender, the incoming telegram base is the telegram base sent by the receiving bureau to the recipient, and the relay telegram base is the telegram base copied by the telegraph bureau when relaying. Telegram bases are also divided into original telegram bases and copied telegram bases. The original telegram base is the original telegram base, and the copied telegram base is the telegram base copied according to the original base, only for reference.

Telegram Fee: It is the telegraph fee.

Telephone Fee: Telephone fees are divided into monthly rent (or quarterly rent) and long-distance. The telephone fee paid monthly for local telephones is called the monthly rent telephone fee, and the call fee for each long-distance telephone call is called the long-distance telephone fee.

Connection Fee: If a long-distance telephone call is connected to another company or telephone bureau's local telephone, a connection fee must be charged separately. For example, in the past, when Shanghai's Chinese boundary connected with the concession, the concession telephone company had to charge a connection fee of five cents each time. (Note: It is now free of charge, and the Ministry of Communications provides subsidies).

Line Fee: If a long-distance telephone call passes through the telephone lines of more than two telephone bureaus or companies, in addition to the call fee for the line of the local bureau, the line fee of other companies must also be paid, which is briefly referred to as the line fee. The price of ordinary long-distance telephone calls is calculated by combining various fees and is not collected separately.

Copying Fee: If there are more than two recipients of a telegram in the same location, only one telegram needs to be sent, with the additional payment mark of "distributed copy" or "TMX." When the telegraph bureau receives the telegram, it will copy several copies and send them to each recipient. For this additional copying procedure, for each telegram that does not exceed 50 characters, each additional copy (that is, there are two recipients) will be charged a "copying fee" of 20 cents. For those exceeding 50 but not exceeding 100 characters, the fee will be doubled, and so on. (The distributed copying fee for social telegrams is only 10 cents for every 50 characters.)

Translation Fee: For outgoing Chinese clear text telegrams that are translated into code by the telegraph bureau, an additional "translation fee" of one cent per character will be charged. There is no translation fee for incoming telegrams.

Special Labor Fee: If the recipient lives in a township or on a ship with no telegraph bureau, and the telegraph bureau must send a special messenger to deliver the telegram, a "special labor fee" should be charged. (To be continued)

The Modernization of Telegraph New Year Greetings

— Zhongming

Today is New Year's Day of the twenty-fourth year. On this New Year's Day, people from all walks of life are busy celebrating the New Year and wishing each other well. Speaking of the methods of New Year greetings, they are also changing with each passing day, following the evolution of the times. The various New Year greeting methods that were popular in the past have gradually become outdated and are not suitable for this modern trend. The giant wave of the times has dispersed all the old and promoted the new, and New Year greeting telegrams are the latest social communication tool promoted by this giant wave.

Telegraph New Year greetings have long been popular in European and American countries. Its scope is not limited to relatives and friends. Even if an ordinary person does not know the head of state or local officials, they often send telegrams to congratulate them on Christmas or New Year's Day. This is a kind of salute from the European and American people to the head of state or officials. In the past, telegraph bureaus in various places in our country also opened New Year greeting telegrams at the end of the year, but because the telegram fees were not very low, they could not be promoted. Since the implementation of the social telegram method last year, the telegram fees have been greatly reduced, and the price per character in Chinese only costs two cents. Therefore, the public enthusiastically used this brand new modern New Year greeting method. It is said that last year, the income from social telegrams in various telegraph bureaus was considerable, and most of them were of a New Year greeting nature. This shows the public's welcome of New Year greeting telegrams!

However, the public's welcome did not come by chance. There are two major meanings between them: First, in recent years, everything has been about modernization and economization. Anything that can meet these conditions can　be welcomed and become popular. People are tired of the old-fashioned New Year greeting methods and always want to change their taste, but they don't want to spend too much money and the method is new. Under this circumstance, telegraph New Year greetings have undoubtedly become popular for a while!

Secondly! Anything that is too common is often not valued. The same is true of New Year greetings. If the method we use is too common, it will naturally not attract the attention of relatives and friends, or even be considered lacking in sincerity and respect. Of course, we want our New Year greetings to be sincere and respectful so that the other party has a deep impression and achieves the practical effect of contacting friendship. Among all the New Year greeting methods, the most sincere and respectful, and the most attractive, I think nothing is better than telegrams!

Regarding New Year greeting telegrams, there are two more points worth noting to everyone: I heard that this year, in order to reward the social people for using telegrams to celebrate the New Year, each telegraph bureau has specially prepared a large number of colorful and exquisitely printed New Year telegram envelopes, printed with beautiful pictures drawn by artists. In this way, when your relatives and friends receive the New Year telegram, they will be very happy to see this beautiful picture. As for the delivery time of New Year greeting telegrams, there are also restrictions. They are not delivered before 8:00 am and after 8:00 pm to avoid disturbing your relatives and friends. The giant wheels of the times are constantly moving forward. It is expected that this year, the number of New Year greeting telegrams will be more enthusiastic than last year!

Summary of China's Economy in 1934

— Feng Weiqi

The Chinese economy in 1934 continued the decline of 1933 and even deepened it. In the world, because of the imperialists' frenzied war preparations, military industries expanded extremely, and related industries recovered to some extent, creating a false prosperity. However, in China, even this false prosperity was absent. Agriculture, industry, and commerce all showed extreme decline.

Now, we will briefly list and describe the important facts that characterized the Chinese economy this year:

1. Rural Economy Further Declines Due to Disasters

Since the invasion of imperialist forces, China's rural economy has been in a process of collapse and decay. Combined with years of war, famine, banditry, heavy taxes, the seizure of territory, and the shrinking domestic market, this has accelerated the process of collapse and decay. Although there were successive good harvests last year and the year before, these occurred during the deepening of the global economic depression, coupled with China's inconvenient transportation and the exploitation and monopoly of high-interest loans in urban and rural areas. Consequently, not only could the peasants' distress not be alleviated and the rural economy not be revived, but the harmful phenomenon of low grain prices hurting farmers occurred. This year, because more than ten provinces and regions across the country suffered from drought and flood, agricultural yields were sharply reduced. According to estimates by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station of the Ministry of Industry, the national average yield of summer crops this year was only 60% to 65% of the normal annual yield. Specifically, early indica rice was 60%, glutinous rice 58%, millet 64%, proso millet 62%, corn 61%, soybeans 56%, sweet potatoes 63%, peanuts 62%, sesame 59%, and tobacco 62%. The value of the losses, according to the same institute's survey, in the ten provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hebei, Shandong, Hunan, Shaanxi, Henan, Hubei, and Jiangxi alone reached 1.445 billion yuan, and this does not include indirect losses. The institute's already published figures for the disaster-affected fields and total value of crop losses in the six provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hebei, Shandong, and Hunan are listed below:

Disaster-Affected Fields　Total Value of Crop Losses

Jiangsu　　49,455,000 mu　　218,000,000 yuan

Zhejiang　　21,790,000 mu　　164,000,000 yuan

Anhui　　37,027,000 mu　　346,000,000 yuan

Hebei　　57,361,579 mu　　239,548,791 yuan

Shandong　　48,094,477 mu　　150,615,695 yuan

Hunan　　22,389,000 mu　　182,521,892 yuan

Total　　236,117,056 mu　　1,300,686,378 yuan

From the above table, it can be seen that the most severely affected provinces were Anhui, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, and Hunan, which are the most productive rice-growing regions. In recent years, Chinese farmers have been hovering on the brink of starvation due to the long-standing bankruptcy of the rural economy. Even the good harvests of last year and the year before still saw the import of large quantities of grain. How much more serious is this year's drought, which is the worst in sixty years? Therefore, as soon as the disaster struck, calls for relief echoed across the country, and grain prices in various places rose in unison. In Shanghai, for example, the weekly price of japonica rice rose from a high of 9.75 yuan between October 16th and 22nd last year to a high of 14.10 yuan between August 16th and 23rd this year, a difference of nearly 4.50 yuan. Even after the new rice came on the market, it remained around 13 yuan. The weekly rice prices in mid-August of this year and the same period last year are listed below for comparison.

The high price of grain has left disaster victims with no means of livelihood, leading to a wave of rice riots. According to incomplete statistics from various newspapers, the following table shows just the incidents that occurred in July and August:

Location　　　Date　　　Number of Participants

With poor harvests, insufficient grain, and high grain prices, it goes without saying that large quantities of foreign wheat flour must be imported to make up the difference. The figures for the fourth quarter of this year are naturally unknown because they have not yet been published. However, the third quarter saw a sharp increase compared to the first and second quarters, which explains this situation. However, if we look at the total import value for the three quarters, 4,163,711 yuan, it is still 74,600,099 yuan lower than last year, about 59% (of which the quantity of rice decreased by 40.6% and the value decreased by 60%, while the quantity and value of wheat decreased by 63.9%). What is the reason for this? Regarding this point, it is impossible to explain if we ignore the sharp decline in the purchasing power of farmers after the disaster, or even their inability to purchase anything, and the nominal nature of relief efforts.

Amidst the widespread reports of drought and flood damage to crops and resulting poor harvests, the only somewhat satisfactory news is that, according to the second estimate by the China Cotton Industry Statistics Association, the lint cotton production is 11,172,553 dan, an increase of 1,398,346 dan compared to last year's final revised estimate of 9,774,207 dan. Although this year's cotton field area of 44,807,579 mu is an increase of 4,353,556 mu compared to last year's final revised estimate of 40,454,023 mu, the percentage increase in cotton field area is only 10.74%, while the percentage increase in lint cotton production is 14.32%, so the average yield per mu has actually increased (0.7 jin). If there had been no drought and flood, the yield would undoubtedly have increased even more.

In addition to the aforementioned drought and flood disasters, the main factors contributing to the collapse of China's rural economy this year include the deepening of the global economic depression, which has led to the continued exclusion of Chinese agricultural products from the world market (such as Chinese tea being squeezed out by Indian, Sri Lankan, and Japanese tea, Chinese silk being squeezed out by Japanese silk and rayon, and the repeated increases in tariffs by countries such as the UK, the US, and France to prevent the import of Chinese egg products), and the US implementation of the Silver Purchase Act, which has absorbed Chinese silver reserves and further dried up rural finance. Also, the large-scale import and dumping of agricultural products from various countries, the intensified exploitation by local gentry, landlords, and moneylenders, and the heavy burden of miscellaneous taxes cannot be ignored.

2. Weak Rural Purchasing Power Leads to Further Industrial Decline

Needless to say, China's industry is also in decline, like agriculture, and its decline has a long history. The reasons for this decline are nothing more than the following: (1) dumping of foreign goods, making domestic goods unable to compete, and domestic and foreign markets almost completely seized; (2) bankruptcy of the rural economy, resulting in weak purchasing power of the people; (3) domestic politics not yet on the right track, and insufficient government protection; (4) too little capital, lack of cooperation from the financial sector, backward technology, difficulty in development, and ease of bankruptcy.

In recent years, although various sectors have emulated Europe and the United States by adopting economic nationalism and making every effort to promote domestic goods, the results have been limited. Therefore, China's industry in 1934 continued the decline of the previous year and even worsened. Here are some of the main types of industries discussed separately:

Cotton Yarn Industry The decline of the cotton yarn industry can be seen from the suspension of work, reduction of work hours, decline in production, sluggish yarn sales, and low yarn prices. According to reports, in the first half of this year, 11 factories with 340,000 spindles completely stopped production, and 3 factories with 100,000 spindles stopped night shifts, totaling 440,000 spindles, accounting for about 15% of the total number of spindles in Chinese factories. This does not include those who shortened working hours (working five or six days per pay period). Therefore, even if the national yarn factory's reduction rate in the first half of this year was not as high as the well-known 23% reduction in the first half of last year (last year, 12 factories with 426,688 spindles completely stopped production in the first half of the year, and 4 factories with 97,288 spindles completely stopped night shifts, totaling about 23% of the national reduction rate, with the number of spindles stopped exceeding half of the total), it is likely not far off. Although factories such as Hankou Zhenhuan Minsheng Yuhua and Zhengzhou Yufeng have successively resumed production in the second half of the year, the number of spindles stopped is certainly no less than one million. The increase in the number of spindles that have stopped production and the reduction in production are undeniable. As for the sluggish yarn sales and low yarn prices, we can get a glimpse from factory-stored cotton yarn and yarn price changes. Shanghai is home to the best-performing yarn factories in the country, but in May 1934, there were still 97,021 bales of yarn stored in factories. Even after the peak sales season of autumn in August, there were still 89,644 bales in stock. Compared to 123,855 bales in June of last year and 123,240 bales in December, there was a slight decrease, but this is the result of years of reduced work and reduced production, and by no means indicates robust yarn sales. Compared to 71,820 bales in December 1932, there is still a difference of more than 17,000 to 25,000 bales. What is happening in Shanghai is indicative of what is happening elsewhere. As for the changes in yarn prices, the following table shows the figures (using 1930 as the base year):

Category　　1932　　1933　　1934 (Three Months in Spring)

42 count Highest price 88 Lowest price 53 57 49 50 49

32 count Highest price 99 Lowest price 71 76 65 66 64

20 count Highest price 98 Lowest price 75 80 67 69 66

16 count Highest price 95 Lowest price 74 78 68 69 66

10 count Highest price 94 Lowest price 81 82 72 70 68

From the above, it can be seen that although yarn prices have been falling in a straight line, the decrease in stored yarn is minimal. This illustrates that the fall in yarn prices has not helped to shrink the inventory. Therefore, Mr. Li Chongdian, section chief of the Industrial Division of the Ministry of Industry, once said after investigating the three industries of flour, yarn, and silk in Shanghai: "There are more than 30 yarn factories in Shanghai, and each factory is maintaining operations by reducing work hours. Although yarn sales have recently shown slight improvement, and factories that reduced work hours have resumed production one after another, this is temporary in nature, and it is still difficult to profit from the spun yarn." (See Shanghai Zhonghua Daily, October 13).

In addition, we can cite many other facts, such as the grounding of Shenxin and other factories founded by Rong Zongjing, known as the "Cotton Yarn Industry Trust" of China, to prove this, but the above is already quite sufficient, so it is not necessary to do so.

Silk Industry The decline of the silk industry in 1934 was even more severe than that of the cotton yarn industry. According to statistics from the International Trade Bureau, silk sales this year not only showed no improvement, but declined even further. The number of raw silk exports in the three quarters was less than 5,000 piculs, worth only more than 20.5 million yuan, a decrease of more than 50% compared to the same period last year, amounting to 20 million yuan. Silk prices fell from a high standard of over 1,600 taels per picul for Shanghai factories in 1929 to about 400 yuan this year (over 900 yuan per picul in May and June last year, and 500 to 600 yuan per picul in August and September). As a result, silk factories in various places have had to close down one after another. As reported in the Shanghai Zhonghua Daily on October 1, "In the past, there were more than 180 silk factories and more than 40,000 silk reeling machines in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Now, due to the impact of economic decline, only more than 70 factories are operating, with only more than 18,000 silk reeling machines." Furthermore, Shanghai originally had 113 single and double cocoon reeling factories. After the destruction of five factories during the January 28th Shanghai Incident, there were still 108. Last spring, 68 factories勉强 were operating, but this spring that number has further decreased to 33 factories, with a total of over 7,200 reeling machines, and a portion of these are temporary, processing cocoons for customers. But now, even these 30 silk factories that are struggling to operate cannot be sustained, and that number has been reduced to 14. In Shunde, Guangdong, only three factories are operating, and fourteen have closed down. Moreover, most of these silk factories that are struggling to operate only do so intermittently. From this, one can get a glimpse of the decline of the silk industry this year.

Flour Industry The flour industry is also one of China's important industries. Currently, there are 83 flour factories in the country, excluding the Northeast. There are 38 in Jiangsu, 6 in Shandong, 9 each in Hebei and Hubei, 4 in Henan, 3 each in Anhui and Shanxi, and 1 in Hunan. Shanghai in the south, Tianjin in the north, and Wuhan in Hubei are the most prosperous. The annual national output reaches more than 82 million bags.

This industry was also on the verge of collapse in the first half of this year, like other industries, but it improved somewhat in the second half of the year. The reason for this is, as Mr. Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Shanghai Banking Association, said: "This is because this year's floods and droughts in various places have been unusually severe,

Page 8

and there has been a crop failure, with disaster victims all over the country. As the saying goes, things are valued when they are scarce. Therefore, the flour industry has seized the opportunity to rise. Now flour prices are rising, and sales are also quite strong, so this year, amid the economic downturn of all industries at the end of the year, only the flour industry can get through it safely." (See Shanghai Zhonghua Daily, December 9)

Match Industry Although the match industry is not as important as the cotton yarn, silk, and flour industries in Chinese industry, it is also a developing industry. However, in the past year, due to foreign goods stifling the industry, sluggish sales, stockpiles of inventory, and plummeting prices, many companies have declared bankruptcy. In addition to the eight factories in the four provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Hubei merging into the China National Match Co., Ltd. to control operations in an effort to save themselves, there has recently been a widespread restriction on production to weather the difficulties.

Rubber Industry According to the Shanghai Rubber Trade Association: "Recently, after overseas Chinese failed in operating rubber businesses, Shanghai rubber factories have also suffered due to the fall in overseas rubber prices, the dumping of Japanese goods, and the fierce competition among companies. Supply exceeds demand, causing prices to plummet, and manufacturers are losing money. Recently, among the 37 existing companies in Shanghai, 25 have closed down one after another, and although the remaining 12 are able to maintain operations with difficulty, they are also in dire straits during the closing account period." (See Shanghai Zhonghua Daily, December 3)

In addition, industries such as cement, enamel, thermos bottles, wool textiles, hat making, umbrellas, cosmetics, glass manufacturing, oil manufacturing, and electrical appliances have all shown decline due to the rural economic downturn, the dumping of foreign goods, and the drying up of finance.

In summary, generally speaking, China's industry in 1934 can be said to have reached the end of the road.

3. Massive Outflow of Silver Leads to Financial Depletion in Urban and Rural Areas

In recent years, due to the decline of rural areas, political instability in the interior, funds from all over the country have concentrated in cities, with banks as their final destination. This has created the abnormal phenomenon of financial depletion in rural areas and financial expansion in cities. Although this is not a situation unique to this year, it is particularly serious this year. Taking Shanghai as an example, the reserves of Chinese and foreign banks increased from 547,447,000 yuan at the end of last year to 594,065,000 yuan at the end of May this year. Although it decreased gradually after that, as of December 6, it has sharply decreased to 334,104,000 yuan. However, this sharp decrease is definitely not flowing into the interior, but is the result of the U.S. President Roosevelt signing the Silver Purchase Act on June 21 and signing the Nationalization of Silver Order on August 9, which caused the price of silver abroad to skyrocket and led to a rapid outflow. This outflow did not stop even after the imposition of export taxes and balancing taxes on silver starting from September 15. According to reports, several batches of silver have recently been transported to the interior, such as Xiamen and Shantou in the south and Tianjin and Qinhuangdao in the north. However, not all of these inflows of silver into the interior are for the purpose of relieving the depleted rural finance and purchasing agricultural products. At least a large part of it is being smuggled out of the country after passing through the interior in order to avoid customs taxes. For example, the Hong Kong Industrial and Commercial Daily reported on November 12 that news had spread in the local banking community that more than 20 million yuan worth of silver had been smuggled into Hong Kong, which is one example. The massive outflow of silver has a significant impact on China's national economy, and its impact on the financial industry is first and foremost to create a crisis in the current Chinese financial system built on the basis of silver reserves. Because silver is flowing out and silver reserves are sharply reduced, the issuance of currency must be restricted. As a result, in the context of a shortage of hard currency, it is even more impossible to increase the amount of paper currency, leading to insufficient currency, credit contraction, tight money supply, and a lack of smooth flow of domestic capital. Although it has not yet reached such a serious point, the fact that Shanghai's interbank lending rate has risen from a normal, extremely loose 1-2% to a recent 2-3% tells us that if this continues, the crisis will eventually intensify. Secondly, after the massive outflow of silver, credit contracts, money becomes tight, and industry and commerce decline, making it difficult for banks and pawnshops to recover the extended term accounts, leading to turnover problems and even bankruptcy.

Over the past year, the monetary policies of imperialist powers, especially American imperialism, have not only caused silver prices to rise, leading to a massive outflow of Chinese silver reserves and inflicting a major blow on the Chinese financial industry, but also caused silver prices to fluctuate constantly, leading to unstable exchange rates and losses for many Chinese banks and pawnshops. According to statistics, in just two weeks from September 19 to October 2, more than a dozen companies in Shanghai, such as De Kang Gold Shop, and in Tianjin, such as Hongyuan Silver Shop, Yiju Silver Shop, Yisheng Silver Shop, Yuju Silver Shop, Enqingyong Silver Shop, Enqinghou Silver Shop, Chengming Silver Shop, and in Ningbo, such as Yukang Flower Shop, Chunyu Pawnshop, Hengxin Bamboo Shoot Factory, and Nianfeng Rice Factory, went bankrupt one after another. Although there is now an organization called the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee and the settlement of accounts is now done through customs gold units, with the government explicitly banning speculation, the successive bankruptcies of the aforementioned gold shops, silver shops, and pawnshops, and the hollowness of the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee, prove how weak such relief and prevention efforts are. In short, China's financial industry over the past year can be said to have been completely defenseless, subjected to the oppressive economic policies of imperialist aggression, and experiencing days of turmoil and insecurity.

In addition, we can also observe China's financial industry over the past year from the perspective of issuance and business trends.

Regarding issuance, the following table shows the figures:

The total amount in November, 393,359,203 yuan, also increased by more than 49.495 million yuan compared to 343,863,311 yuan at the end of last year. As for business operations, in addition to expanding speculation, reducing loans to industry and commerce, and continuing other non-core businesses this year, there have been continued attempts to extend loans to rural areas, vigorous promotion of small loans, and competition for investment in railways and highways.

4. Commercial Slump and Shrinking International Trade

China's commerce over the past year has continued its previous slump and has become even more萎縮 (atrophied/shrunken). For example, in Shanghai, known as China's largest commercial port, hundreds of stores have closed down in the prosperous areas such as Nanjing Road and Shilu due to poor turnover. The Special Zone and the South City Court are handling more than double the number of lawsuits of this kind than in previous years, and the court is executing the closure of several stores every day. Dozens of civilian financial institutions such as pawnshops such as Tongyuan and Yucheng have closed down because they only accept items and have no money to lend out. Hangzhou's commerce has not been slightly remedied by the completion of the Hangjiang Road and the highway network. In Jiujiang, in addition to munitions, general commodities are subject to the collection of production and sales taxes, and exports have decreased two to three times compared to previous years. In Hankou, the market is very quiet because the government controls the special goods trade. According to a report by the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau, compared with the same period last year, exports in July this year have decreased significantly in cotton, tea oil, cowhide, and egg products, except for a few items such as black tea, green tea, and tung oil. Imports from January to September were about 21 million yuan, a decrease of 6 million yuan compared to the same period last year. The desolation of the only major city in Central China is evident from this.

The situation in the Yangtze River Basin, the richest area in the country, is already like this, then it goes without saying that the situation in North China, which is under the iron hooves and tightened control of Japanese imperialism, is even worse. In Kaifeng, Henan, since the collapse of Xinchang Company this spring, the business of the entire city's financial sector has been unusually sluggish. Transportation, sundries, silk, raw oil, and other categories are all deserted, especially raw oil merchants, more than a dozen of whom have gone bankrupt. In Tianjin, the market is also extremely desolate due to the sharp decline in exports of agricultural products and fur from the interior. In Shanxi, various businesses have closed down due to social poverty and the collection of business tax and income tax. According to reports from 35 cities and counties including Taiyuan, Datong, Qi, Jie, Fenyang, etc., there were 6,757 old businesses in 42 industries such as silver and money. There were 153 new businesses this year, while 1,838 businesses closed down. Currently, there are about 4,000 businesses that have closed down in the 106 counties of the province. Except for Rehe, the main cities in Inner Mongolia are extremely depressed. Zhangjiakou's market is slightly more stable than it was during the chaotic times of war last year. No one cares about the transportation of grain into Baotou, and the entire city is extremely deserted. In the Northwest provinces, such as the Xi'an-Lanzhou Highway, the number of cars has been reduced from 100 to half due to the small number of passengers and goods, and the revenue is not enough to cover the cost of fuel, which shows the decline of the market. In Pingliang, Gansu, eight stores closed down within a month.

Commerce in South China is affected by the decrease in remittances from overseas Chinese, in addition to the generally unfavorable conditions. Various industries in Guangzhou are competing to sell to survive. According to the Hong Kong Industrial and Commercial Daily: "The sluggishness of Guangzhou's business this year is unprecedented, and the entire line is in danger of collapsing." Shantou, a major trading town in eastern Guangdong, has been in extreme financial turmoil. Since the discovery of a large number of commercial warehouse receipts in September of this year, almost all trade in the market has been suspended. In addition, provinces such as Fujian and Guangxi are even more depressed than Guangdong.

Under these circumstances, although imperialists are making every effort to dump goods, imports this year have still decreased sharply. According to customs reports, the cumulative number of imports from January to October was 874,114,029 yuan, a decrease of 283,809,861 yuan compared to 1,157,923,890 yuan in the same period last year. Exports also decreased from 506,954,698 yuan from January to October last year to 441,865,850 yuan from January to October this year, a decrease of 65,088,839 yuan. As a result, the trade deficit also decreased from 650,969,201 yuan from January to October last year to 432,248,179 yuan from January to October this year, a decrease of 218,621,022 yuan.

In short, China's economy in 1934 can be said to have further declined under the multiple oppressions of imperialism, natural disasters, and man-made disasters.

Semi-Monthly News

— Staff Contributor

Guangdong-Guangxi International Telegrams to be Charged in National Currency

Telegrams sent abroad from Guangdong and Guangxi provinces have previously been charged according to Hong Kong dollar rates. The Ministry of Communications, in order to unify the charging methods of telegraph bureaus nationwide, has ordered the telegraph bureaus and stations in Guangdong and Guangxi provinces to change to charging according to national currency rates starting from December. As for the practice in various parts of Guangdong Province of using silver dollars with "hao" markings, it is specifically stipulated that the exchange rate will be in accordance with the post office's conversion rate, with one national currency dollar equivalent to one dollar and three dimes in silver dollars with "hao" markings. If Hong Kong dollars are used for payment, they will be accepted at 93% of the national currency rate, meaning 93 Hong Kong cents equals one national currency dollar. This exchange rate will be determined based on market fluctuations, and any changes will be announced by the telegraph bureaus.

Supplementary Measures for Calculating Charges for Chinese Telegrams

Chinese telegrams are primarily sent by our Chinese citizens, so the Ministry of Communications is providing as much convenience as possible regarding charging restrictions. The latest supplementary points are noted below:

(1) House numbers composed of Roman letters and Arabic numerals, such as A7, J45, etc., are allowed to be calculated as one word.

(2) Telegrams containing only Arabic numerals and unit words, without context, such as (734) number, (687) yuan, etc., are allowed to be sent.

(3) If the name and address of the recipient include words such as "residence," "mansion," "villa," "at home," "official residence," etc., such as "Shen Guohua residence," "Shen mansion," "Jingan villa," "Yang Fu at home," "Datong official residence," etc., because their nature is similar to the names of organizations, businesses, hotels, etc., they are all allowed to be included in the address calculation.

(4) If the recipient's name includes titles, such as Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, President Dai Jitao, Principal Wang Yiming, Lawyer Jiang, Accountant Pan, etc., the names of these titles will be included in the recipient's name and address calculation. Also, if "Mrs. Zhang," "Miss Li," etc., are used without adding the given name, the words "Mrs." and "Miss" are also allowed to be included in the name and address, and will not be calculated as text. However, honorifics such as "Mr." and "Sir" must be included in the telegram's word count.

The Trend of World Economy in 1935

— Ming

In the past year, the world economy has been subjected to much tribulation. What of the coming year? Based on the current situation, it is not difficult to gain a relatively clear understanding by extrapolating into the future. We Chinese people are also caught up in the world's turbulence, and are severely affected by international events. If we can discern the international trends, it will be of considerable help in understanding the movements of our own national economic situation.

Currently, there are three relatively major economic problems in the world.

(1) What is the future of inflation policies?

(2) Will the European gold standard be shaken?

(3) How will future markets be developed?

In the development of our Chinese national economy, inflation policies have only been discussed in theory. We have no actual, overall experience. In the past, things like the "military currency" of the early Republic, the banknotes of Wuhan, the Jin banknotes of Shanxi, and the provincial banknotes of Guangdong cannot be considered inflation policies. The so-called inflation policy today must at least have the following two economic effects:

First, it must raise prices. Since the world panic of 1929, major countries have all experienced falling prices due to overproduction and reduced consumption power. Therefore, they have had to find ways to raise prices so that existing industries do not stagnate. If the value of money is reduced, prices will naturally rise relatively. At the same time, there is another effect: stimulating emerging industries.

Second, it must open up new markets. Before the American stock market crash in the autumn of 1929, countries had all restored the gold standard, stabilizing the value of currency. As a result, wage and salary income was invisibly reduced. Government budgets also shrank. Therefore, the consumption power of general society was reduced along with it. As a result, the digestive capacity of domestic markets was small. In overseas markets, major countries all had some degree of protectionist trade measures. Conversely, countries using silver benefited from being on the upper hand in exports. Importing from them was restricted by high prices. Once an inflation policy is implemented, it can not only increase exports to silver-using countries, but also break through tariff barriers and compete for overseas markets. Domestic markets can also be slightly expanded due to the general increase in wages.

However, in reality, only Britain and Japan have benefited from inflation. One reason is that they abandoned the gold standard relatively early, and the other is that they are both engaged in special markets, such as the development of colonies, which is more convenient than for other countries. The United States only abandoned the gold standard in April 1933 and implemented a reduction in the value of currency in January 1934. Unfortunately, it was too late, so it did not receive any practical benefits. Now there is a new policy following the National Industrial Recovery Act, and for the fiscal year ending in June 1934, the financial deficit was US$3,626 million. Public debt increased by US$4,514 million. It seems that it will be impossible not to continue to implement inflation. Moreover, the implementation of the new policy still requires new expenditures of US$5 billion to US$20 billion.

Currently, all major countries except France and Germany are implementing inflation policies. On the one hand, they are striving to seize overseas markets. On the other hand, they are expanding the power of the national economy as much as possible within the country, wanting their own country to monopolize the domestic market. Unless absolutely necessary, they will never allow foreign goods to be imported. For example, the United States imports raw silk and ore, and Japan imports cotton and iron ore and pig iron. In this way, they can only develop towards countries with relatively backward industries or colonial markets. However, the economies of these markets themselves are also declining. In essence, purchasing power is abnormally reduced. Trying to expand even more than now will almost be impossible, and may even shrink further. The countries of South America have small populations, and there is no outlet for their agricultural products. Expanding this market again is probably impossible. China has a large population and vast land, but in recent years, its people have become poor and its finances exhausted. It is also difficult to increase unilateral imports.

As for their domestic markets, a large country like the United States has as many as 11 million unemployed people. These people have no work, so where will they find the surplus power to consume? Britain is similar to this. Unemployment is usually over 2 million. The economic alliance within the British Empire is only a temporary remedy. Japan has had the best economic situation among capitalist countries in recent years. However, in the autumn of 1934, various industrial sectors showed a downward trend. The reason is a reduction in foreign exports. Future hopes are very slim. Therefore, the future of inflation policies is not optimistic. Moreover, there is still much pessimistic material.

The countries that still maintain the gold standard, such as France, Belgium, Switzerland, and the Netherlands, truly hold the reins of the financial world in Europe. They have also declared that they will not abandon the gold standard. The reason is that they suffered greatly from excessive inflation during the First World War. In particular, Germany still retains the negative effects of that time. However, they have recently been greatly shaken by the devaluation of currency by Britain and the United States. In particular, prices in France are falling more and more, and there is also a tendency for gold reserves to decrease. Income and expenditure other than trade is also decreasing. Overseas trade seems to be falling behind Britain, the United States, and Japan. Recently, the calls for reducing currency value have gradually increased in the industrial sector. It is feared that she will not be able to maintain the gold standard for long. Otherwise, this group of gold standard countries will not be able to compete economically with non-gold standard countries. However, abandoning the gold standard and implementing inflation policies may not have any special benefits.
