Page 18

[H Shen Bao Fifth Sheet]

Bandit Suppression Provinces: County Governments Abolish Bureaus and Establish Departments

Headquarters Issues General Outline of Measures

Revamping the County System to Enhance Efficiency

Implementation Required in All Areas Within Three Months

(Nanchang) The Nanchang Headquarters issued a general outline of measures for bandit suppression provinces regarding the abolition of bureaus and establishment of departments in county governments on the 31st, instructing the provincial governments of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Fujian, and other provinces to comply and implement them within three months. Reports and records are to be submitted for verification. The instruction stated: "Regarding compliance, it has been observed that county administration has deteriorated over the years, and no tangible results have been seen. Many attribute this to the incompetence of county magistrates. While this is a factor, the lack of centralized authority and incomplete organization within county governments are also contributing factors. The current county organizational law provides for only two departments within the county government, with Public Security, Finance, Education, and Construction Bureaus below them. The heads of these bureaus are often appointed by the respective provincial departments, forming their own systems and acting independently. They directly issue bureau orders downwards and report directly to their respective departments upwards. The county magistrate, presiding over them, cannot fully exercise supervisory and commanding powers due to not having personally appointed them and often being concerned about their backgrounds. Even between Bureau A and Bureau B, they only focus on individual development, lacking a unified will. The central focus of work in a county is therefore difficult to determine. Furthermore, with the establishment of these bureaus, the scale expands, inevitably leading to the establishment of sections and divisions and the indiscriminate placement of officials to create an impressive facade. Consequently, local finances are entirely allocated to support these redundant officials in the various bureaus, often proving insufficient, resulting in county budgets allocating only funds for organizational expenses and no funds for projects. Even with virtuous and capable individuals, how can they achieve results? This commissioner is deeply aware of this issue. When commanding troops in Jianghan in previous years, the headquarters of the three provinces stipulated measures for county governments to abolish bureaus and convert them into departments in order to consolidate authority and reduce expenditures, which has already been circulated for implementation. However, it has been observed that some provincial county bureaus have not yet been uniformly abolished. Now that the provincial government has implemented a joint office system, in order to enhance county administrative efficiency and ensure seamless and flexible coordination, the revamping of the county system is an urgent task. Therefore, after extensive consultation and detailed consideration, a general outline of measures for bandit suppression provinces regarding the abolition of bureaus and conversion into departments in county governments has been formulated and promulgated for implementation. All aspects of the county magistrate's authority and responsibilities, county government organization, and the handling of education, construction, public security, and finance have been carefully considered and improved appropriately based on actual circumstances. Summarizing the key points, the following should be clearly stated: Firstly, centralize authority and responsibilities. All existing bureaus under the county government are to be abolished, and their functions are to be incorporated into the management of the various departments within the county government. All county administrative measures are to be overseen by the county magistrate. The administrative personnel of the county government are also to be nominated by the county magistrate and approved by the provincial government to form a cohesive body, achieving effective coordination. Secondly, strengthen the organization. With the abolition of the bureaus, the county government's affairs will become more complex. The original organization should be appropriately expanded, with the addition of departments and personnel, and an increase in administrative expenses to attract talent and assist in governance. Thirdly, integrate education and construction. Education and construction are both priorities for national salvation today. The two are interdependent and closely related. This commissioner has repeatedly emphasized this in proclamations since last year, aiming to ensure that educational facilities meet the needs of local industries. Therefore, this outline stipulates that after the abolition of bureaus, education and construction affairs should be merged into one department to facilitate coordinated management. The administrative personnel of this department must be filled with specialized talent and may include supervisors and technicians to assist in the handling of affairs. Fourthly, strengthen police and defense coordination. Modern police systems are products of industrialized nations. Since their adoption in our country, they have only proven necessary in major cities and trading ports. In the towns and villages of various counties, where rural life prevails and residents have mostly lived in settled communities for generations, the forcible implementation of modern police systems for management is not only incompatible but also faces insufficient funds and personnel, making it impossible to perfect the organization and facilities. As a result, they merely adopt the name of the police while being staffed by disbanded soldiers, vagrants, or local ruffians who are ignorant of their duties, serving as tools to exploit the people and commit crimes. The harm caused is immeasurable. It is not known that since ancient times, our country's police administration has been entrusted to the Baojia system. The Baojia and militia units organized in the bandit suppression provinces are, in fact, the rural police. If their organization can be strengthened, appropriate training provided, and police officers assigned to supervise and guide them, the execution of all police duties can be assisted and promoted. Therefore, the reform of our country's police system cannot blindly imitate the superficial aspects of other countries but must adapt to local conditions to suit the current environment. Therefore, Article 6 of this outline specifically adopts the method of police and defense coordination. The existing public security organs and police in the towns and villages of various counties are to be abolished. Even the political police or judicial police secretly established in various counties should be largely eliminated, with strict limits on the number and appropriate salaries to prevent them from using their positions for extortion. Only police assistants are to be established in county governments, patrol officers in district offices, and police chiefs and officers stationed in key towns and villages, respectively obeying the orders of the district chiefs or joint Bao directors, commanding Baojia officials and militia units on-site to perform general police duties and be responsible for training Baojia members and militia, integrating self-defense organizations with police officer allocation. With only a small number of police officers strategically distributed, the entire county's police network can be constructed. Fifthly, unify tax collection. The numerous national, provincial, and local taxes are collected by various tax bureaus stationed in the same county, each operating independently. This not only wastes significant funds but also leads to extortion by tax collectors, with their unofficial collections often exceeding the government's revenue. Therefore, the more collection agencies, the greater the people's suffering. However, in cases of overdue payments, fines, or other necessary actions, the assistance of the county government is still required for enforcement. The current system's drawbacks are evident and require fundamental improvement. Therefore, Article 7 of this outline specifically stipulates the reform principles for county finances. Except for cases where a particular tax source in the area is exceptionally large and has been approved for the establishment of a special bureau for collection, all other provincial and county taxes are to be collected uniformly by the county government. A collection office may be established to handle this under the direction of the department in charge. The legally entitled collection fees are to be used to supplement county administrative expenses. At the same time, a county treasury is to be established as the agency for receiving, transferring, managing, and allocating funds. The collection office is responsible for collection but does not receive cash, while the county treasury is solely responsible for receiving cash and not for collection. With clear divisions of authority and responsibilities, past abuses such as unclear handover of collection personnel and embezzlement can be gradually eliminated, and the establishment of the county treasury can also effectively regulate local finances. The above five points are the main provisions of this outline and represent good rules for county administrative reform. It is hoped that the respective provincial governments will understand the purpose and strictly comply. In addition to forwarding this outline to the Executive Yuan for submission to the National Government for review and notification to the relevant departments for record-keeping and distribution, the attached measures for abolishing bureaus and converting them into departments in various bandit suppression counties are hereby ordered to the provincial governments for immediate compliance and implementation within three months. Reports and records are to be submitted for verification. This order is given."

General Outline of Measures for Bandit Suppression Provinces Regarding the Abolition of Bureaus and Conversion into Departments in County Governments

Article 1: This headquarters, in order to concentrate the powers and responsibilities of county governments and strengthen their organization to enhance county administrative efficiency, hereby formulates this outline.

Article 2: Documents sent to and from county governments are to be issued in the name of the county magistrate.

Article 3: The existing Public Security, Finance, Education, and Construction Bureaus under the county government are to be abolished, and their functions are to be incorporated into the management of the various departments within the county government.

Article 4: The county government shall have one secretary and three departments, numbered for identification, each with a department head. The functions of each department, except for education and construction affairs, which should be combined into one department to facilitate close cooperation, should be appropriately allocated according to actual needs. The number of personnel in each department shall be determined by the provincial governments of each province based on this outline, and the organizational regulations of the county government shall be submitted to this headquarters for approval and implementation. The increased administrative expenses of each county due to the addition of departments or personnel shall be determined by the provincial governments according to the county's level and approved by this headquarters before being disbursed by the provincial government.

Article 5: County administrative personnel shall be nominated by the county magistrate and submitted to the provincial government for strict review and approval or record-keeping. Administrative personnel responsible for education and construction affairs must possess specialized qualifications or equivalent knowledge and experience and shall not be appointed otherwise. Supervisors and technicians may also be appointed to assist in handling education and construction projects.

Article 6: Except for municipalities and provincial capitals with thriving commerce and dense populations and major trading ports, the existing public security organs and police in the towns and villages of various counties are to be abolished. Instead, one police assistant shall be established in the county government, one patrol officer in each district office, and a number of police chiefs and officers shall be stationed in the joint Bao offices of important towns and villages. Under the command of the county government and the supervision of the district chiefs and joint Bao directors, they shall train Baojia members and militia in their respective areas, handle security, household registration, sanitation, transportation, and all police duties, and assign Baojia officials and militia units to perform local labor and assist in the execution of various police affairs. The training, appointment, and employment of police officers and the methods for assigning labor and assisting police affairs to Baojia units shall be formulated by the respective provincial governments and submitted to this headquarters for approval and implementation. Political police or judicial police established by county governments for collecting taxes, delivering messages, and handling cases shall, to the extent possible, be assigned to assist the district offices and Baojia personnel. The number of existing political police or judicial police shall be determined by the provincial governments according to the county's level and the complexity of affairs, with appropriate salaries and necessary travel expenses provided during official trips. They shall not extort the people, nor shall they establish additional unpaid political police, which would lead to extortion. Violators will be severely punished.

Article 7: County financial affairs shall be reformed in accordance with the following principles: (1) Provincial and county taxes to be collected by each county, except for cases where a particular tax source in the area is exceptionally large and has been approved for the establishment of a special bureau for collection, shall be collected uniformly by the county government. The responsible department may be entrusted with the collection or a collection office may be established under the direction of the department in charge. The legally entitled collection fees shall be used to subsidize county administrative expenses. The methods for unified collection, allocation of collection fees, and the organization of the collection office shall be determined separately. (2) The management of county financial revenues, expenditures, and custody, currently handled by the accounting section of the county financial committee, shall be separated and a county treasury established for independent management. In areas where a county treasury has already been established, the financial committee prescribed in Chapter 3 of the Regulations for Reorganizing County Local Finances in the current bandit suppression area shall be changed to a full-time auditing agency, with separate regulations to be determined. (3) The funds saved by the county government from the abolition of the various bureaus shall be transferred to the county's project expenses and district office establishment expenses. (4) The county's original education funds or construction special funds, under the unified collection and disbursement of the county treasury, shall still be kept separate and maintain their independent nature and shall not be diverted for other purposes.

Article 8: The provincial governments of each province may formulate detailed rules for the implementation of this outline and report them to this headquarters for record-keeping.

Article 9: This outline shall be implemented in the bandit suppression provinces of Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian. This headquarters shall forward it to the Executive Yuan for submission to the relevant departments for record-keeping and distribution. Other provinces that deem it necessary to implement the abolition of bureaus and conversion into departments in various counties in accordance with this outline shall submit a request to the Executive Yuan for approval.

Article 10: Matters not covered by this outline shall be handled in accordance with the current county organizational law and other relevant laws and regulations.

Article 11: This outline shall be uniformly implemented in all counties within three months from the date of its promulgation. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 31st)

(Nanjing) The Salt Company jointly requested the Ministry of Finance to expand sales areas, and the Salt Administration has approved the request and stipulated the following measures: 1. The registered annual sales volume is set at 1.3 million dan. 2. Refined salt is allowed to be sold in the four coastal areas and the five inland counties of Jiangsu Province. However, the sales volume for each coastal area will be based on the average actual sales volume of the most recent three years (1931-1933). 3. Refined salt transported inland in the four coastal areas and the five counties of Jiangsu Province must have the local stamp on each package. Those without the stamp will still be fined as contraband salt by the tax police. 4. Except for the four coastal areas and the five counties of Jiangsu Province, the remaining areas will still be handled in accordance with the general rules for refined salt, i.e., limited to treaty ports. 5. If the sales volume exceeds 1.3 million dan, each coastal area will be required to pay an additional registration fee, and the release of salt will be suspended. (Special dispatch from the 31st)

United States Considers Joining League of Nations with Conditions

Democratic Member Plans to Propose Bill to Congress

State Department Indicates It Can Provide Assistance

(Washington) Senator Pope stated today that when the current Congress convenes, there will be another proposal for the United States to join the League of Nations. Pope also announced that he is drafting a joint proposal that will be submitted when Congress opens. The United States can join the League of Nations with a simple majority vote in both houses, instead of the usual two-thirds majority required in the Senate for treaties. Pope said that there is considerable support for the United States to join the League of Nations, so there is a greater chance of it passing in the current Congress than before. The joint proposal will include a reservation stating that after the United States joins the League of Nations, it will have no obligation to send troops to other countries under any circumstances. Although Pope expressed optimism, it is generally expected that his proposal will encounter fierce opposition, led by Senator Borah, the former chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee from the same state. Other expected opponents include Senators Norris and Johnson. It is recalled that when President Wilson returned to Washington from the Versailles Peace Conference and proposed that the United States join the League of Nations, these three were among those who opposed it. (National News Agency dispatch from the 30th)

(New York) According to a dispatch from the New York Times correspondent in Washington, the State Department is currently studying a bill to enable the United States to join the League of Nations. The reporter stated that Senator Borah, a Democrat from Ohio, will propose a bill at the beginning of the next session of Congress advocating for this matter. Borah's new bill will contain two reservations: (1) Although the United States is a member of the League of Nations, its obligations should be consistent with the provisions of the Kellogg-Briand Pact; (2) Although the United States joins the League of Nations, it cannot send troops to foreign countries under any circumstances. The State Department officially denies that the government is studying this matter but acknowledges that the State Department will provide assistance to Senator Borah in drafting this bill. However, Borah will be personally responsible for its submission to Congress. According to Borah, President Roosevelt believes that once the United States joins the League of Nations, the warmongering factions in various countries will suffer a fatal blow. In addition, Democratic Senator La Follette said that since the United States has already joined the Permanent Court of International Justice at The Hague, a proposal to join the League of Nations will be submitted to the Senate at the beginning of the next session of Congress. (Havas dispatch from the 30th)

US Congress to Reopen Soon; National Defense and Finance are Major Issues

The Navy Department Will Request Increased Funding

Unemployment Requires Urgent Government Relief

(Washington) With Congress about to convene, relief and financial issues loom large in the capital. It is estimated that 15% of the nation's population relies on relief for survival. Other, less significant, foreign matters include the development of naval and Far Eastern issues, and their impact on the US position in the Philippines and Hawaii. Silver and inflationist members of both the House and Senate demand the passage of new currency reform bills to stimulate national commerce. However, they will face resolute opposition from conservatives, who claim that the new currency issued by the government will be used to repay old debts and will soon flow into the coffers of banks. However, they admit that President Roosevelt's difficult problem is veterans' allowances, as two-thirds of the members of both the House and Senate support the immediate payment of adjusted veterans' service certificates. The government acknowledges this matter and hopes to use strategy to seek a compromise (i.e., to pay cash immediately to truly impoverished veterans). It is said that the President has decided to ask Congress to stipulate methods for raising funds to pay veterans' allowances. If there is no such provision, the President will reject any allowance plan. It is said that the invincible naval plan caused by Japan's abandonment of naval treaties will stir up serious discussion. The Navy not only requires a huge increase in funding for shipbuilding, but also seeks increases in funds for fuel equipment and naval personnel. The Navy Department's proposed fuel bill for the 1935 naval maneuvers is said to be the highest expenditure since the European War. (30th National Telegram)

(Washington) The most important thing in US domestic affairs in 1934 is that the American people support the policies implemented by President Roosevelt. The reason why the American people are like this is that Roosevelt's policies have a radical trend, and some even say that they have a tendency to socialize. There is no doubt that the Economic Revival Bureau has lost its power. The method of regulating prices has now been abandoned, and even the industry regulations of various industries are more open than before. Roosevelt, worried about the increase in the budget deficit by the Conservative Party, allowed for budget cuts and indicated that he might stabilize the currency in the future. However, the issue of dollar stability and currency inflation does not seem to be a real issue at present. As for expanding lending, it is no longer mentioned. The prospects for business revival are better than a year ago, but there are two things that must wait a few months to know. One is whether the economic improvement is thorough, and the other is that the unemployment problem still lingers in the minds of the general public, and whether economic reform can solve it. The end of this year is the same as the end of 1933. According to estimates from all parties, there are still 7 million to 12 million unemployed people who need the government to maintain their lives. If their families are included, there are a total of 18 million to 20 million people. (30th Havas Telegram)

US Prepares to Mention Far Eastern Politics at Naval Conference

Japan is Alert and Preparing Countermeasures

Claims Not to Have Violated the Nine-Power Treaty

(Tokyo) The US believes that Japan's notification of the abandonment of the Washington Treaty is a new situation. Therefore, in order to deal with this matter, it may mention political issues in the Far East at the preparatory consultation to be reopened next year. Former US representative Davis once informally told representative Matsudaira that if Japan notified the abandonment, the US would not but mention political issues in the Far East at the same time. The diplomatic authorities are wary of the US attitude on this point. The superficial reason why the US must mention political issues in the Far East is that the Washington Treaty was signed simultaneously with the Nine-Power Treaty at the Washington Conference in the twelfth year of Taisho (1923), so the two are closely related. This is a one-sided view, but the diplomatic authorities decided to oppose the US view for the following reasons: (1) The signatories of the Washington Treaty and the Nine-Power Treaty are different, and judging from the time elapsed since the Washington Conference, the two are not related. (2) Notifying the abandonment of the Washington Treaty aims to achieve a new disarmament agreement. If it is related to political issues, this is because the US suspects Japan. (3) Japan has not only not violated the Nine-Power Treaty in the Far East, but also respects the Nine-Power Treaty and sincerely hopes that China's doors will be opened. It has repeatedly stated this, and it thinks that the US should have understood it. (4) In order to prevent the anxiety caused by the expiration of the Washington Treaty, Japan is also willing to participate in proposals to supplement or reconfirm the Four Treaties. However, it is absolutely opposed to discussing political issues with European and American countries and replaying the foolishness of the Geneva League of Nations General Assembly. (31st Dentsu Telegram)

British and American Newspapers Criticize Japan for Destroying Naval Treaty

(London) The liberal Manchester Guardian wrote an article commenting on Japan's announcement to abolish the Washington Naval Treaty. It sternly criticized the policies adopted by the Japanese government, concluding that "We now have two responsibilities: (1) to formulate a new agreement based on the principle of limiting naval armaments. This principle should be confirmed and not ambiguous in the slightest; (2) to restore an international system in the Pacific that ensures that the stronger has no covetous thoughts and the weaker has no fear of aggression." (31st Havas Telegram)

(London) British morning newspapers commented on Japan's action of abolishing the Washington Treaty, most saying that the treaty still has two years before it expires, and during this period, a way to solve the difficulty of maritime disarmament can be found, so there is no need to worry about naval countries competing to build warships. The Morning Post said that the construction of larger battleships and aircraft carriers will cause the financial burden to exceed the security it provides. The Daily Telegraph said that according to the general opinion of world naval experts, Japan seems to have complete and impregnable security in its own waters, while other countries do not, so they have no choice but to seek complete security. The Times said that Japan's abolition of the treaty can of course be regarded as serious. Although Japanese diplomacy has given its abolition action a kind of conventional form, what cannot be concealed is that the lofty architecture of international coordination established thirteen years ago has been destroyed by this. However, Japan has announced its willingness to conclude a new treaty to replace the old treaty, and the recent negotiations have shown frankness and goodwill, so the establishment of a new treaty does not seem to be without hope. (31st Reuters Telegram)

(New York) The New York Times commented on Japan's announcement to abolish the Washington Naval Treaty in an editorial entitled "Isolation is Not Glory," which mainly stated that "Japan has the right to announce the abolition of the treaty, which is indisputable, but at least Japan's actions have not taken into account other countries, which can be said to be inappropriate." The newspaper believed that the Washington Naval Treaty would expire at the end of 1936. According to Article 23 of the treaty, if the contracting parties do not announce the abolition two years before the expiration, it will continue to be effective until two years after a contracting party announces the abolition, at which time it will be deemed to have been abolished as a whole. Therefore, at most, it will be extended to the end of 1938, and the treaty will automatically announce its abolition. Japan could have waited until 1938. (31st Havas Telegram)

Using New Instruments to Detect Germs in Smallpox and Oral Diseases

Zülich. It is said that there is a new discovery in German medicine recently. If this news is confirmed, it will become the most important invention in modern medicine. The size of some germs, such as the germs of smallpox, oral and foot diseases, etc., is so small that it cannot be seen by a precision microscope, nor can any film cause it to precipitate. Professor Bickelwald has recently invented a new instrument that can be used to determine the size of this microorganism. This instrument is a powerful centrifuge. When it rotates, it has a great force that can separate the smallest organism from the solution (the principle is the same as the centrifuge that separates milk). The size of the microorganism can be calculated by the centrifugal speed at which the microorganism separates. Using this method, Bickelwald proved that the length of the smallpox germ is one two millionth of a millimeter, and the germs of foot and oral diseases are one two hundred thousandth of a millimeter. Many other germs can also be measured by this method. (30th National Telegram)

Tianjin Nankai Japanese-Built Airfield Case

Japanese Celebrate Upon Completion of Construction

Tianjin Court Ruling Ineffective in Reality

Tianjin Dispatch: The negotiation regarding the Japanese airfield in Nankai Bali Tai, Tianjin, involved Zhang Ting'e, who previously dispatched Municipal Government Advisor Sun Runyu to visit the Japanese Consul-General in Tianjin, Kawagoe, and Vice-Consul Tanaka for multiple negotiations. However, no results were achieved. The Japanese side's construction had reached 70-80% completion ten days ago. The land, totaling ten hectares, seventy-five acres, seven fen, and four li, has been elevated, altering the original paddy field terrain. Section A comprises six hectares, and Section B comprises eighty acres. On Section A, three steel-framed, white iron aircraft hangars and two brick-and-mortar houses have been built, along with two gasoline storage depots. The perimeter is enclosed by a low fence with wire mesh. The original earthen road, constructed by our side, leading from the field to Nanguan outside Tianjin, has been directly repaired and filled with cinder by the Japanese side. This extends the road directly to the western end of Fukushima Street in front of the Haiguang Temple Barracks. Electric poles have been buried along the roadside, with electric and telephone lines connecting to the airfield. When the project was completed, the commander of the Japanese garrison in Tianjin, Umezu, and Consul-General Kawagoe, along with Japanese residents, held a celebration inside the field, outwardly claiming it was to celebrate the completion of a new sports field for the Japanese community. However, recent reconnaissance by our military experts all concluded that it was undoubtedly an airfield, with the hangars capable of accommodating at least twenty-four aircraft at a time. The construction of Section B is currently halted due to the cold weather and unsuitable mud conditions this winter, but it will continue when the weather warms up in the spring. The Municipal Government has reported this matter in detail to the Beiping Political Readjustment Committee, the Military Branch Committee, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. It is rumored that a solution may be difficult, or that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs may directly negotiate with the Japanese ambassador. This is the proper procedure in diplomatic protocol, and all possible efforts have been made. Tracing back to the beginning of this case, the landlord, Guang Ren Tang, in order to absolve themselves of the responsibility of illegally selling national territory, filed a complaint with the Tianjin District Court, accusing the tenant, Zhang Shaoqing, of violating the land lease agreement by altering the original terrain (the original terrain being paddy fields). The court ruled last winter to cancel the original agreement, ordering the tenant to return the land. However, the complexity lies in who Zhang Shaoqing is and how the Japanese suddenly emerged as tenants. This issue cannot be effectively resolved by a mere piece of paper from a judicial body without extraterritorial jurisdiction. Therefore, the ruling is just a ruling, and the Japanese side continues construction as before. In the spring, Guang Ren Tang continued the previous lawsuit, still suing the court. After years of delay, the court both issued summons for the tenant Zhang Shaoqing and lacked the power to stop the construction of the Bali Tai project. Until today, a default judgment was issued. The main text of the judgment states, "The lease agreement between the original owner Qian Di and the defendant, concerning ten hectares, seventy-five acres, seven fen, and four li of paddy land in Nankai, is hereby terminated. The defendant shall return the aforementioned land to the plaintiff for management, and the altered land shall be restored to its original condition. Regarding the land return portion, provisional execution is granted. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant." This judgment, apart from not requiring service to the plaintiff, requires service to the defendant, but there is no place to deliver it. At the same time, the so-called provisional execution is also impossible to execute. Guang Ren Tang, before and after leasing the land, employed clever methods to evade responsibility. Beforehand, they strictly stipulated the contract to show that they were unaware that the tenant was Japanese. Afterwards, they repeatedly sued to cancel the original contract to show that they had no other intentions. However, when tracing the culprit, the hall is actually responsible for serious crimes. (December 28th)

League Head Suo Wang of Xilin Gol League Arrives in Beiping to Recuperate

Weighing Over Three Hundred Pounds, Walking with Difficulty

Wu Peifu Has Brief Meeting with Suo Wang

Beiping Dispatch: Inner Mongolia's Xilin Gol League has two league heads, a main and a deputy. The main league head is Suo Wang, and the deputy league head is De Wang, the current Vice-Chairman of the Mongolian Political Council. Suo Wang has deep roots and prestige in Inner Mongolia. In recent years, due to obesity and illness, he has rarely been involved in political affairs. De Wang, a young up-and-comer, has thus come to the fore. During the Mongolian incident, Suo Wang was also a figure of attention from all sides. Recently, his obesity has worsened, with swelling in his limbs, weighing up to three hundred and twenty pounds, and walking with great difficulty. He needs assistance to move, so he came to Beiping from Xilin Gol League to recuperate. When he got off the train, four people supported him as he walked unsteadily. According to his attendants, the king dreamed of Sakyamuni, who told him that the water in Tangshan, fifty miles north of Beiping, is warm and that he must bathe there to cure his obesity. Suo Wang believed it was an indication from the Buddha, so he came from afar. He rested in Beiping for two or three days and then went to Tangshan to bathe. He also consulted famous Chinese medicine practitioners. In recent days, many people have visited his residence, but he has declined to meet most of them due to illness. He only spoke with Wu Peifu for over twenty minutes. The lamas claimed they would not leave without seeing Suo Wang. After much explanation by Suo Wang's secretary and others, which took two hours, they finally dispersed. The authorities have been very courteous to Suo Wang," it is said. (December 29th)

The most important items were the military education program and the restructuring of the political training offices at all levels of the army. On the 12th, the political training restructuring plan was passed and submitted to Chen Jitang for review. The restructuring of the political training offices of each army, division, and brigade will result in the elimination of all section chiefs except for the directors and deputy directors, who will retain their original establishments. The political training office of the army headquarters will have one colonel secretary, one lieutenant colonel staff officer, two major staff officers, and three captain and lieutenant staff officers each, as well as two warrant officer clerks. The division headquarters will have one lieutenant colonel secretary, three lieutenant colonel staff officers each, and three warrant officer clerks. The brigade will have one major political training officer and one sergeant clerk. The company will have one lieutenant political training officer. An order has been issued to all political training offices to downsize according to the new establishment and complete the restructuring by the end of December. (December 26th)

Retrospect of the New Life Movement Last Year

Published by the New Life Movement General Association

Nanchang Dispatch: The year 1934 of the Republic of China has ended. In the historical events of this year, the New Life Movement is truly one of the most precious pages. Looking back at the initiation and progress of the movement this year, it is truly inspiring and hopeful. Therefore, the general situation of the movement in recent years is summarized as follows: (1) The Genesis of the New Life Movement: The evolution of every nation is like sailing against the current; if you don't advance, you retreat. Our Chinese nation has five thousand years of culture, four hundred million people, and thirty-five million square miles of land. It was originally the most ancient civilization in the world. However, in recent times, it was first mistaken due to the incompetence and stagnation of the late Qing Dynasty, and then hindered by the oppression and trampling of various imperialist powers. The national spirit declined, and national affairs became increasingly difficult, leading to "decadent" and "romantic" phenomena. The twilight years deepened, and there was much degeneration. Mr. Sun Yat-sen, the pioneer of our Chinese nation, realized the crisis of our nation. He deeply believed that in order to promote political reconstruction of the country and revive the nation, he advocated revolution for decades, and the Republic of China has been established for more than twenty years. Unfortunately, Mr. Sun died prematurely, and the great cause of the revolution has not yet succeeded. The reason is due to the intensified oppression of various imperialist powers, making it impossible for us to raise our heads, and the decadence and stagnation of our nation, failing to participate in the cause and bear heavy responsibilities, is the greatest reason. Our revolutionary leader, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, based on the principle of "pacifying the interior before resisting foreign aggression" and "reforming the heart before revolution," launched the New Life Movement in February 1934 in Nanchang, the location of the General Headquarters. He sought a life revolution for all our citizens, using the simplest and most urgent methods to eliminate the habits of our people that are incompatible with the times and the environment. He aimed to revitalize the nation and make it a fundamental movement for the revival of our nation. The New Life Movement is an extremely ordinary and practical movement. It does not seek deep textual explanations, nor does it want to sing high-sounding tunes in vain. The initial movement focused only on "propriety" and "cleanliness."

(2) Initial Progress of the New Life Movement: The New Life Movement, inspired by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, began its initial trial in Nanchang. The initial governing body was called the Nanchang New Life Movement Promotion Association. At the end of February, the first meeting of executive officers was held, and various regulations were gradually formulated. The movement proceeded in three stages: first, propaganda; then, guidance; and finally, inspection. Civic rallies and lantern parades were held to attract the attention and awareness of the general public. The "propriety" and "cleanliness" movements were then carried out step by step according to the planned plan.

(3) Subsequent Rise in Various Parts of the Country: After the New Life Movement was implemented in Nanchang, it achieved remarkable results in a short period. The aspects of "propriety" and "cleanliness" were greatly different from the past. All parts of the country, due to the eagerness to revive the nation and the enthusiasm to eliminate the old and establish the new, started the same movement under the leadership of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. The first to follow were the capital and Shanghai. Then came Jiangsu, Hebei, Hubei, Fujian, Anhui, Henan, Zhejiang, Hunan, Shandong, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Gansu, Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Qinghai, Sichuan, Guizhou, Yunnan, Xikang, and Beiping City. This movement developed vigorously in a short period of time, reaching major cities and remote villages, which was beyond initial expectations.

(4) Promulgation of the Outline of the New Life Movement: The New Life Movement swept the country in a few months, which greatly encouraged and comforted the promoters of the New Life Movement in Nanchang. However, the progress was too rapid, and shortcomings and malpractices inevitably arose. In order to clarify the theory of the New Life Movement and guide the methods of the New Life Movement, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek specifically ordered the drafting of the Outline of the New Life Movement and published it to the people of the country as a guideline. The outline included the main purpose of the New Life Movement, the understanding of the New Life Movement, the purpose of the New Life Movement, and the content of the New Life Movement, such as propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, as well as food, clothing, housing, and transportation. In addition to a concise and thorough explanation, the methods of the New Life Movement, the responsibilities of the movement, and the progress of the work were also detailed. As a result, the New Life Movement, which had been developing spontaneously, was brought into line and proceeded in an orderly manner.

(5) Establishment of the New Life Movement General Association and Reorganization of the New Life Movement Associations in Various Cities, Counties, and Railways: Due to the rapid progress of the New Life Movement, the organizations in various places inevitably suffered from the drawbacks of some people acting arbitrarily and unevenly. In order to unify the movement and strengthen the organization, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek established the New Life Movement Promotion General Association in Nanchang on July 1st, and took office as the chairman. He also formulated the organizational outline of the New Life Movement Promotion Associations in various provinces, cities, railways, and counties in Jiangxi (because the movement in various counties in Jiangxi was directly presided over by the General Association), and notified the various provincial, city, county, and railway associations to reorganize accordingly. Those that have completed the reorganization include the capital, Shanghai, Beiping, and the three cities, Hubei, Hunan, Shanxi, Henan, Shandong, Fujian, Anhui, Shaanxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Gansu, Chahar, Suiyuan,

Hebei, Qinghai, and other provinces. The Pinghan, Jiaoji, Longhai, Zhengtai, Jinpu, Nanxun, Beining, and Jinghu-Huhangyong railways, and more than fifty counties in Jiangxi, such as Nanchang, Xinjian, Jiujiang, and Poyang, are all under the guidance of the General Association and are carrying out the movement separately.

(6) The Purpose and Steps of the Work: The New Life Movement is a simple movement to change customs and correct current malpractices. It does not make excessive propaganda, nor does it engage in superficial displays. It does not aim to transform the habits of the entire nation all at once, but seeks gradual progress for each individual. Therefore, it consistently takes a trial attitude, starting from the near and extending to the far, and extending from oneself to others. The work steps focus on Nanchang, followed by the counties in Jiangxi and the capital cities of the country, and are gradually promoted in order to ensure the practical progress of the movement. Based on this purpose, the General Association not only formulated the General Outline of the First Phase of the Work Plan of the General Association, but also formulated the Principles of the First Phase of the Work Plan of the Provincial, City, County, and Railway Associations, and distributed them to the various associations for implementation.

(7) Promotion of the New Life Movement in Nanchang: A. Scope of Promotion: The General Association, based on the principle of establishing prestige from near to far, focuses on Nanchang. The scope of work is initially divided into the following eight items: (1) Promotion of the New Life Movement in various government agencies; (2) Promotion of the New Life Movement in various public places; (3) Promotion of the New Life Movement in various shops; (4) Promotion of the New Life Movement in various public utilities; (5) Improvement of city appearance; (6) Promotion of the New Life Movement in social organizations; (7) Research on the reform of etiquette; (8) Promotion of the New Life Movement in various factories. B. Promotion Cadres: The New Life Movement depends on the ability to be implemented. Therefore, the promotion cadres are extremely important. The promotion cadres used by the General Association include the following: (1) Jiangxi Youth Holiday Service Corps: This corps is organized under the guidance of the General Association. In addition to twelve branch corps in Jiujiang, Linchuan, Pingxiang, Poyang, and other counties, there are more than 1,900 people in Nanchang City who are working hard to serve during the holidays, achieving remarkable results. (2) Shop Service Staff: Each shop with two or more employees appoints a service staff member, who is issued an armband by the General Association and taught separately, totaling more than 1,600 people. (3) Female Civil Servant Service Corps: Women are the backbone of the New Life Movement in the family. Therefore, the General Association organizes a service corps of female civil servants in Nanchang, and their mission is to start from themselves and then from their families, extending the service from a small number of families to the entire society. (4) Constitution and Police Organization Inspection Team: The constitution and police are the most effective cadres in promoting the New Life Movement. Therefore, the Nanchang constitution and police are divided into several groups, led by personnel dispatched by the General Association, to patrol and inspect and advise. (5) Civil Servant Service Corps: Each government agency in Nanchang City organizes a service corps of civil servants, who not only promote the New Life Movement in the agency, but also teach the nearby streets and markets. The organization is currently underway. C. Practical Demonstration: In addition to promoting various movements, the General Association also seeks various practical demonstrations, in order to encourage citizens to emulate and silently transform. Therefore, the following matters are carried out: (1)筹 Establishing Public Canteens: The restaurants in Nanchang are not only expensive, but also do not meet the conditions of simplicity and cleanliness, which is harmful to the health and economy of the general public. Therefore, the Association decided to establish public canteens in five locations in Nanchang City, east, west, south, north, and central. The construction of the houses and the setting of furniture should meet the conditions of simplicity and cleanliness. The food should be of low value and rich in nutrients, and each meal should not cost more than ten cents. After there is a clue, it will be contracted to merchants for operation. The General Association will then select another location to open. This will be promoted in this way, with the aim of completely transforming all the restaurants in the city and achieving the requirements of the New Life. (2)筹 Establishing Male and Female Bathhouses: The bathhouses in Nanchang with slightly better architecture are expensive and cannot be afforded by the general public. Most of the ordinary ponds are dirty and expensive. There are no female bathhouses in the entire city, and it is winter and the weather is cold, so women have no way to bathe. Therefore, the Association decided to establish male and female bathhouses in five locations in Nanchang City, east, west, south, north, and central. The equipment in the bathhouse should be clean and hygienic, and each person will only be charged five copper coins for bathing. (3)筹 Establishing Public Cemeteries and Cremation: Various places in our country have always valued burial, which wastes land and money, and there is a real need for reform. Therefore, the Association stipulates cremation methods and replies to the Jiangxi Provincial Government to designate the forest hills between Nanchang Niuxing Railway Station and Meiling to build public cemeteries as a demonstration. (4) Designated New Life Practice Areas: For demonstration purposes, the General Association designates one or more locations in government agencies, schools, party headquarters, and streets and markets as New Life Practice Areas. (1) Government agency: Nanchang Municipal Committee. (2) Schools: No. 1 Middle School, No. 2 Middle School, Girls' Middle School, No. 2 Vocational School, Girls' Vocational School. (3) Party headquarters: Provincial Party headquarters. (4) Streets and markets: West Main Street. (8) Promotion of the New Life Movement in Jiangxi Province: A. Promotion Steps: Since the movement in various counties in Jiangxi is directly presided over by the General Association, the General Association has decided on three promotion steps: (1) Counties along the Nanxun Railway with convenient transportation; (2) Counties along various highways with convenient transportation; (3) Various counties that have launched the New Life Movement. B. Overview of the Movement: More than fifty counties that have already launched the movement are following the principles of the work plan formulated by the General Association, formulating detailed work plans according to the actual needs of each county, and working hard to carry them out.

(5) Promotion of the New Life Movement in Various Provinces, Cities, Railways, Shipping Lines, and Overseas Chinese: A. Various Provinces and Cities: The General Association formulates work plan principles for all provincial and city associations that have been reorganized and established, in order to ensure consistency in promotion. Detailed promotion items are formulated by each province and city according to actual needs. The work is now progressing consistently. B. Various Railways: Various railways are the national transportation lifeline, which is of great importance to the lives of passengers. After the General Association reorganized the New Life Movement Associations of various railways, it issued work plan principles, and each railway formulated its own detailed items for implementation. Now all railways have made rapid progress. C. Various Shipping Lines: Various domestic shipping lines, especially those operated by foreign merchants, are quite inconsistent with the requirements of the New Life. In order to thoroughly reform, the General Association plans to establish New Life Movement Associations for various shipping lines. However, due to the deep-rooted malpractices of various shipping lines, it is not possible to reform without reforming their system and economic relations. It is currently consulting with its competent authorities. D. New Life Movement of Overseas Chinese: After the New Life Movement was launched in Nanchang, overseas Chinese also wrote to request the establishment of New Life Movement Associations and followed up with promotion. In response to the needs of the facts, the General Association specially formulated the Organizational Outline of the New Life Movement Associations of Overseas Chinese, which was ordered by the Central Organization Committee and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to be responsible for the General Branch and various consulates. (10) Further Movement Preparation: The initial work of the New Life Movement lies in the "propriety" and "cleanliness" that are easiest for the people of the country to implement. However, the highest goal of the New Life Movement is definitely not limited to this. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek said in the outline, "How can the life of the people be noble? It is called the art of life. How can the life of the people be rich? It is called the production of life. How can the life of the people be consolidated? It is called the militarization of life." This art of life, production of life, and militarization of life are the highest requirements of the New Life Movement, and are also the further work of the entire movement. In order to carry out this work, the General Association established a research group for militarization, production, and art, to conduct research and draft implementation plans. The various plans have now been drafted, and the second step will be promoted at the beginning of 1935.

(11) General Review of This Year's Movement: Since the New Life Movement was launched in February of this year, what has been the progress and effectiveness? There are facts that can be consulted, so there is no need to repeat them. However, the course of this year's movement can be clearly divided into several periods, namely (1) from the launch of the New Life Movement in February to the establishment of the General Association on July 1st, it was the period of the launch and free development of the New Life Movement; (2) from the date of the establishment of the General Association on July 1st, it was the period of unifying the national movement and streamlining the work steps, gradually transitioning from propaganda to practical action; (3) Since the beginning of this bottom, the New Life Movement has gradually moved from the initial stage of "propriety" and "cleanliness" to the further promotion of the militarization, production, and art of life. In short, life has no end, and the New Life Movement has no end. In other words, this movement will advance with our nation and our country. Whether our nation can be revived and whether our country can be strong depends entirely on whether we can work hard on this movement. The country has its efforts to go to (Central News Agency)

Qingdao's Difficulty in Eradicating Opium

Japanese Operate About Two Hundred Opium Dens

Over One Thousand Addicts Detained in Rehabilitation Centers

Qingdao Dispatch: Since the Nanchang Headquarters issued the "Provisional Regulations for the Strict Prohibition of Potent Drugs," all provinces and cities have taken swift action to eradicate them within a specified period. However, due to Qingdao's special circumstances, although the authorities have repeatedly issued orders and strictly prohibited opium, the number of opium offenders has not decreased. The Drug Rehabilitation Center established by the Public Security Bureau is overcrowded with drug offenders. According to investigations, there are about two hundred opium dens set up by Japanese and Korean vagrants in Qingdao. If each household has at least twenty addicts, then there should be more than four thousand people in total. The Public Security Bureau has difficulty cracking down, and the rehabilitation center cannot accommodate so many people. Eradicating opium within a specified period is difficult. Therefore, the various difficulties have been reported to the Municipal Government for review. The report states: "Following Instruction No. 7953, it is noted that potent drugs such as morphine are extremely harmful. Repeated orders have been issued to prohibit them. However, due to long-standing complacency, the results are still minimal. If this continues, the harm will be profound. Recently, the Beiping Political Affairs Council forwarded the Nanchang Headquarters' order to issue the 'Provisional Regulations for the Strict Prohibition of Potent Drugs.' Copies of the original documents have been issued for compliance and have been circulated to all on record. Now, from the date of receipt of this document, you must eradicate all opium within one month. You are instructed to direct your subordinates to earnestly investigate and prohibit opium in order to ensure the completion of the task. If there is favoritism or negligence, you will be held accountable for shielding criminals and will not be shown any leniency. You are to comply immediately and instruct your subordinates to be aware of the same." Upon receiving this, we are deeply aware of Your Excellency's emphasis on humanitarianism and the determination to eliminate opium. We dare not fail to comply diligently. We immediately instructed all districts under our jurisdiction to comply. At the same time, we negotiated with the Japanese Consulate to investigate and prohibit the morphine dens set up by Japanese and Korean vagrants so that they can assist each district in conducting thorough searches at any time. Since the implementation, two months have passed. According to the total number of people arrested in each district, since the implementation of the 'Provisional Regulations for the Strict Prohibition of Potent Drugs' on September 12, it has reached more than eight hundred. Except for those who have been discharged from rehabilitation, the total number of people currently detained in the two branches is no less than four hundred. The morphine dens set up by Japanese and Korean vagrants in each district have been searched more than ten times with the cooperation of the Japanese Consulate. As a result of repeated negotiations, eleven fewer dens exist than before. According to the report from the consulate, twelve families of Japanese and Korean vagrants who were engaged in this business have now been sent back to their home countries. The fines collected recently in this regard have also reached more than two thousand two hundred and eighty yuan. This is a general overview of the active opium prohibition in the past two months. However, Your Excellency has set a deadline of one month for eradication. Now, two months have passed. Although there have been considerable results, the eradication period is still far away. The Director is anxious day and night and deeply fearful. However, in tracing the cause, there are things that must be clearly stated to Your Excellency. According to reports from various districts, there are more than two hundred opium dens set up by foreigners in this city. Due to strict prohibition recently, eleven have been reduced, leaving more than one hundred and ninety. If each household has at least twenty addicts per day, then there should be four thousand people, not including those who send people to buy opium. According to the current number of people allowed in the two branches of the Bureau's Drug Rehabilitation Center, which is three hundred, we have already squeezed in up to four hundred, which is already extremely crowded. Even if we can accommodate up to four hundred people according to the previous situation, the average rehabilitation period for each person is two months. Therefore, it will take two years to complete the process. Moreover, the number of addicts in the city is more than this. Relapses and new addictions after rehabilitation are even more unavoidable. Therefore, to achieve temporary clarity, just the current opium offenders in this city who should be arrested at the same time are also more than one thousand. Without planning large-scale housing separately, there is no place to accommodate them. Once the accommodation location can be arranged, then we will seriously negotiate with the Japanese Consulate. All morphine dens set up by Japanese and Korean vagrants that have been discovered must be ordered to return to their home countries. Newcomers must not engage in this business again. If we proceed so strictly, there may be hope for eradication. The Director's ignorant view dares not be silent. If there is anything appropriate, please review and approve." Subsequently, the Municipal Government issued instructions stating, "Noted. Since the number of people is crowded and there is no way to settle them, you should immediately prepare suitable housing and arrest and accommodate as many people as possible. You are still urged to instruct each branch bureau to actively handle the matter and eradicate opium within a short period. If any of your subordinates are perfunctory, they will be held accountable for shielding criminals and will not be shown any leniency. You are to comply immediately and instruct your subordinates to strictly abide by this and not violate it." (December 29)

Giant Snake Discovered in Tangshan

(Tianjin) A giant snake was discovered on the morning of the 29th on the right bank of the Dou River, upstream of the Da Hong Bridge in Tangshan. It was over two zhang long and as thick as a telegraph pole. It moved from east to west, followed by countless small snakes. It stopped after about two hours and entered the water at the Yuehe area. Over a hundred people saw it and were amazed. (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 31st)

The Disaster Situation in Changyuan, Puyang, and Dongming Counties in Southern Hebei is Extremely Serious

A Total of 270,000 Disaster Victims

Dozens of People Freeze to Death and Starve to Death Every Day

Beijing Dispatch: The Yellow River in Hebei Province has breached its banks for years, and disasters have occurred repeatedly. Changyuan, Puyang, and Dongming counties have all suffered a major calamity. The once fertile fields have all become flying sand and vastness. The two-year flood broke out, and clothes and belongings were all washed away. The mulberry fields have become a sea, and there is no hope for sowing. Many villages and houses have become ditches and ruins. The three major elements of clothing, food, and shelter are all unsustainable. At this time of freezing weather, how can they live? Therefore, dozens of people freeze to death and starve to death every day. Even the formerly wealthy families have now become beggars. The tragic situation in the disaster area is no less than a human hell. The disaster victims are begging for relief, like a great drought looking for clouds and rain. Therefore, the three counties recently sent Tian Kongnai as a representative to Beijing to petition for relief in order to save hundreds of thousands of disaster victims who are about to die. The document presented to the Central Government is recorded as follows:

"Reporting that the three counties of Changyuan, Puyang, and Dongming in Southern Hebei have suffered severe Yellow River disasters for years, and the disaster victims are in urgent need of relief. Please quickly allocate a large amount of relief funds to save the people's lives and avoid taking risks. This year, the Yellow River mouth in Changyuan County, Hebei Province, has breached again, and Changyuan, Puyang, and Dongming counties have suffered floods again. It is estimated that the disaster area in Changyuan County reaches more than four hundred villages, with more than 140,000 disaster victims. The disaster area in Puyang is more than two hundred villages, with 100,000 disaster victims. Dongming has fifty-nine villages with more than 27,000 disaster victims. According to statistics, there are more than 270,000 disaster victims in the three counties. The water depth in the disaster area ranges from four or five feet to eight or nine feet, and the area is as wide as more than 300,000 square li. Houses were washed away by the floods, and fields became swamps again. The treasury was empty, and clothes were gone. The disaster situation is more severe than last year, more than doubled. First, the breach of the banks for years has made it impossible for the people to live. Moreover, the disaster victims are still in the floodwaters. Today last year, the Yellow River water in Changyuan had receded, and a lot of autumn wheat was planted. But today, the city is surrounded by floodwaters, which are boundless. Moreover, the Yellow River water has been rising recently, and the floods have not stopped. At this time of severe cold, the disaster victims have lost all hope for clothing, food, shelter, and transportation. The cries for help are overflowing the fields. Recently, dozens of people have been freezing to death and starving to death every day. The situation in the disaster area is no less than a human hell. It is noted that Hebei Province has had many misfortunes for years, and its financial expenses have already fallen short of revenue. In addition, the subsidies for the Eastern War Zone and the assistance to the Beiping Political Committee's expenses are even more stretched every month. According to Hebei Province's financial expenses, maintaining the status quo is still insufficient, let alone providing relief. The relief funds obtained from the Yellow River Disaster Lottery are very few, only a drop in the bucket. There are too many disaster victims, which is really difficult to relieve. Therefore, repeated telegrams have been sent, but no allocation has been received, and we are deeply regretful. Moreover, the folk customs in Southern Hebei are strong. If no relief is provided, hundreds of thousands of disaster victims will inevitably take risks once they are forced by hunger and cold, endangering the political situation. In the spring of this year, various slogans were discovered. Fortunately, the authorities maintained their strength and were not harmed. At this time when the disaster victims are hopeless for survival, if someone uses this opportunity to engage in incitement, future hidden worries must be prevented in advance. Therefore, representatives of the three counties have gone to Beijing to petition, so that the lower-level situation can be reported to the higher levels. It is noted that the Central Government's plan for providing relief to various provinces has been discussed and decided at the Central Political Affairs Conference in November. All service personnel in military, political, and educational institutions in various provinces who earn more than fifty yuan per month will donate 2% of their salary, from November to April 24th. This shows the Central Government's great intention to provide relief to various disaster areas. Hebei Province has not received any allocations for relief in the disaster area since the Yellow River mouth breached again in August of this year, which is inevitably biased. Hebei Province's donation to aid relief has been implemented since November. Can the funds donated by Hebei Province be retained by this province in order to distribute them to various disaster areas in this province? Or should a large amount of relief funds be quickly allocated to save the hundreds of thousands of disaster victims who are about to die? We are extremely fearful and await orders. If what has been reported is appropriate, we respectfully request your review and approval, and quickly allocate funds to benefit the disaster victims. This would be a great act of kindness. Respectfully presented to the President of the Executive Yuan Wang, the Minister of Finance Kong, and the Chairman of the National Government's Yellow River Flood Relief Committee and Relief Affairs Committee Xu."

Qingpu Bandit Song Maorong Executed

The bandit Song Maorong, 22 years old, originally from Fengxian, who committed crimes in this county, was originally a doctor. In June of last year, he colluded with a large group of bandits, carrying guns, and successively kidnapped Ni Lansheng's child in Jinshanwei, looted the Ruanxiang Town in Fengxian and the firearms of the town's public security outpost, opened fire and killed people. In September of this year, he kidnapped Li Shenqi, Anzhuang Huang Shunfu, and others in Youbang, this county. He was escorted to the district headquarters by the First Detachment of the First District of the Provincial Public Security Water Police Team at the end of November and transferred to the county government for handling. Qian, the County Magistrate, signed the order to extract the bandit the day before yesterday, verified his identity, and escorted him to Jinze Town for execution by shooting.

Jiangqing Xiba Salt Merchants Petition

Although the salt business in Xiba, Huaiyin, has declined in recent years, and many lake merchants have switched to trucking, there are still some merchants who still go to the dike to purchase salt and ship it out by boat. Because river-transported salt can be freely sold in Bengbu after arriving there, it is not restricted by the sequential sales of truck transport. Now, the Northern Transport Envoy Qiu Jieli has ordered the dike salt merchants to adopt the same method as truck transport. Therefore, the dike merchants are in great panic. Jiaxing Maoshengtong Pawnshop Reopens

Jiaxing Fengjieqiao Town's Maoshengtong Pawnshop is owned by the town gentry Wu Huichen. Due to business losses, it announced the suspension of operations last month. The farmers near the area had no way to pawn their goods. The town's shops also suffered greatly from the sudden closure of the pawnshop, so they jointly sent a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce to forward to the County Government, urging the pawnshop to reopen immediately. The County Government also advised the pawnshop to find a way to reorganize and continue operating in order to benefit the poor. It is now known that the pawnshop has been officially transferred to Maoshengtong Qiaoji, and will continue operating from today (the 1st).

Special Announcement

Review and Prospects of the Judiciary Over the Past Year

Speaking of the state of the judiciary over the past year, I am truly very sorry. Although various matters concerning judicial organization mostly fall within the scope of judicial administration, which at the time was not under the jurisdiction of the Judicial Yuan, in essence, whether purely judicial or judicial administrative, many shortcomings have been left in our hearts during the past year, which is undeniable. The reasons for this are manifold, perhaps due to the country's many difficulties, or due to financial constraints, and also due to several struggles and efforts to reform, but with limited resources, it has not yet been possible to reach the realm of perfect ideals. However, summarizing these many setbacks and listing them as a review of the past and a lesson for the future is also a way for public servants to exercise self-discipline.

Currently, the judicial phenomena that make us feel most uneasy are roughly three points:

(1) The failure to abolish consular jurisdiction has resulted in the failure to achieve complete judicial sovereignty. This is the first shortcoming in the judiciary. Originally, on December 28, 1929, the National Government had already issued an order announcing the abolition of consular jurisdiction of various countries; on May 4, 1931, it further promulgated twelve articles of the "Regulations for the Implementation of Jurisdiction over Foreigners in China," stipulating that they would be implemented on January 1, 1932. At that time, it seemed that there was a desire to act vigorously, thereby breaking the shackles of unequal treaties and wiping out eighty years of shame. Subsequently, after the September 18th Incident, due to financial difficulties, all preparations for the abolition of consular jurisdiction were unable to be carried out and have been shelved to this day. This year, floods and droughts have occurred frequently, and the government has no time to rescue the dying and heal the wounded. Therefore, although the abolition of consular jurisdiction is highly anticipated, it has to be postponed until next year.

(2) The failure to universally establish new-style courts has resulted in the failure to thoroughly implement the spirit of judicial independence. This is the second shortcoming in the judiciary. According to the Six-Year Plan for Judicial Work during the Tutelage Period in 1929, it was originally planned to establish 1,367 county courts in the first two years, and then convert them into district courts in the third year. During the six years, 1,773 district courts, one high court, 42 high court branches, four supreme court branches, 47 juvenile detention centers, 174 ordinary prisons, 22 recidivist prisons, and 21 tuberculosis and mental illness prisons should be added. This is the plan of our party to complete judicial independence during the Tutelage Period. However, the current situation is also felt to be flawed, mostly because the country's finances are difficult, so many plans cannot be carried out on schedule. As of the end of 1934, there are currently 37 county courts (but established after 1929), 129 district courts (56 established after 1929), 24 high courts (2 established after 1929), 38 high court branches (9 added after 1929), one juvenile detention center, and 92 ordinary prisons (18 added after 1929), which is a huge difference compared to the original plan. However, this belongs to judicial administration, and before the change of affiliation in October, it was not the responsibility of the Judicial Yuan.

(3) Regarding the effectiveness of the judiciary, although efforts have been made in recent years to achieve both "appropriateness" and "speed," there are still some regrets. The Supreme Court is under my direct command, and striving for "appropriateness" and "speed" is naturally my duty. According to statistics, the number of pending cases in the court was 5,518 in 1932, 5,191 in 1933, and 4,554 in 1934, showing a gradual decreasing trend year by year. Our ultimate goal is naturally to have "no backlog of cases," but with the current number of courtrooms and judges, I am afraid that we have exhausted our efforts and can no longer make further progress. In the past, the Supreme Court judges were limited to concluding 15 cases per month per person. Now, the minimum limit has been increased to 18 criminal cases and 20 civil cases per month. Considering the vastness of the case files in the third instance, concluding more than one case per day cannot be compared to those who are perfunctory and afraid of difficulty. As for the handling of cases in courts at all levels, it is difficult to calculate accurately because the statistics for this year have not yet been finalized. Here, we will take the Suzhou High Court, Jiangning District Court, Shanghai District Court, and Wuxian District Court as examples (because their locations are close to the capital and statistical materials are relatively easy to obtain). Table A below compares the number of criminal cases accepted by each court in the second instance with the number of cases in which the original judgment was overturned to see how much the degree of "appropriateness" has been achieved. Table B compares the rate of civil cases accepted by each court with the rate of pending cases to see the degree of "speed":

Table A (Criminal Second Instance)

Year　Number of Cases Accepted　Number of Original Judgments Overturned
