Except for the Jiangning District Court, where the ratio between the two numbers has been slightly "three to one" over the years, the other courts have generally progressed from a "one to one" ratio to a "three to one" ratio, which shows that the handling of cases by courts at all levels has gradually improved in terms of "appropriateness." However, this difference is still very large and should be further improved unremittingly.

Table B (Civil Second Instance)

Number of Cases Accepted　Number of Pending Cases

Jiangsu High Court　1931　1315　252

1932　1727　380

1933　2163　363

Jiangning District Court　1931　280　　48

1932　371　　56

1933　463　　72

Shanghai District Court　1931　912　　131

1932　1144　146

1933　1290　138

Except for the Jiangning District Court, the number of cases accepted by the other two courts in 1933 increased compared to 1932, while the number of pending cases decreased, indicating that there has also been progress in the "speed" of handling cases. However, this only applies to a few major cities, and there are no statistics available for the rest. The fact that Jiangning District Court, located in the capital, lags behind is a major shortcoming.

From the above figures, it can be shown that the effectiveness of the judiciary has improved slightly over the past year, but it is still too far from our ultimate goal.

In addition, there is one more thing worth mentioning in the past year, which is the compilation of the Supreme Court's precedent abstracts. Because our country's laws are incomplete and there are often ambiguities in the provisions of the law, the compilation of precedents is particularly important for increasing judicial efficiency. This article contains 150,000 words, from the establishment of the Nanjing Supreme Court in 1927 to the end of December 1931, and all precedents that can clarify the purpose of the law have been collected as much as possible. In today's judicial situation with many holes and sores, this move is somewhat comforting.

The past situation has been roughly explained. Now, let's move on to expressing our hopes for the future.

The most urgent task is naturally to promptly implement the abolition of consular jurisdiction to realize the completeness of judicial sovereignty. On the one hand, this depends on improving the judiciary and completing various codes to block the excuses of foreigners as a basic step for proceeding, and when implementing it, diplomatic negotiations are also important. The completion of the code belongs to the scope of legislation, and the improvement of the judiciary is based on sufficient financial resources. Therefore, the abolition of consular jurisdiction must be achieved through the joint efforts of diplomacy, finance, judiciary, and legislation. There is no doubt that we must overcome all difficulties this year to reach this goal.

The second is to universally establish new-style courts to eliminate the old practice of combining administration and judiciary. It is planned to urge the Department of Judicial Administration to comprehensively plan and formulate detailed implementation methods in the shortest possible time and submit them to the central government for review and implementation, so that the six years of tutelage will not be in vain, and judicial independence will be gradually realized.

Thirdly, regarding the improvement of judicial efficiency, courts at all levels should also be urged to make the greatest efforts to achieve the extreme of "appropriateness" and "speed," aiming for the number of cases accepted by each court to be close to the number of cases decided, and for the number of pending cases to approach zero. In addition, the third instance should implement the legal review system. According to statistics, approximately 30% of the cases adjudicated by the Supreme Court are overturned. The goal for this year is to reduce this 30% to less than 10%. This will show that the lower courts are capable of handling cases "appropriately."

To achieve the above goals, there are roughly the following guidelines:

(A) Expand the courts and increase the number of courtrooms. Because the number of cases accepted by each court has been increasing in recent years, from the perspective of the entire government policy, various social policies should be adopted at the same time to enrich the national economy and fundamentally reduce the causes of crime and litigation. However, from the perspective of the judiciary itself, expanding the courts is an unavoidable measure to seek speed in handling cases.

(B) Strengthen the training of judges. Expanding the courts is to increase judicial efficiency from the quantitative aspect. At the same time, attention should also be paid to the qualitative aspect. The training of judges is to increase the ability of judges so that they can be sufficient to achieve the principle of "appropriateness" and "speed" in handling cases. The current judge training institute has also added a trial member training class and a clerk training class to assist in this. If the ability of judges is improved, the two meanings of "appropriateness" and "speed" in handling cases can be achieved.

(C) Establish a Legal Profession Research Association. The judge training institute can only gather a certain number of people in one place for a certain period of time to conduct research. The Legal Profession Research Association can allow judges from all over the country to continue their research. Its organization will generally be based on Supreme Court judges and prosecutors from the Procuratorate as basic members. Judges and prosecutors from high and district courts in various provinces can also join as members at any time to conduct joint research, so that judges in the national first, second, and third instances can exchange knowledge. The internal division is divided into civil and criminal groups, and members will raise questions on the articles and case interpretations of domestic and foreign laws, as well as existing cases in various provinces, and answer questions and argue with each other. In this way, those who are in the final trial position can be aware of the experiences of the first and second trials across the country. Those who are in the first and second trial positions can also recognize the original rules and measures of the final trial court. Internal and external communication, consistent spirit, not only can the cases sent back for retrial be gradually reduced, but also the talent and intelligence of judges across the country can be increased.

(D) Convene a National Judicial Conference. The methods of increasing judicial efficiency are naturally multifaceted. The thinking power of one person is limited, so it is necessary to gather legal practitioners and legal scholars from all over the country to conduct in-depth discussions to obtain detailed methods. Our plan is that if there are no other obstacles, this judicial conference will be realized this year.

The above is a small idea, and it is inevitable that there will be omissions. If all sectors are willing to give advice, I will naturally be happy to listen.

Today is the New Year's Day of the 24th Year of the Republic of China and the Anniversary of the Founding of the Republic of China

All Sectors Hold a General Assembly at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce　　All Affiliates of the Municipal Government Hold a Group Worship in the Morning

All Agencies, Factories, and Stores are Closed for Holiday

Today is the New Year's Day of the 24th Year of the Republic of China, and also the anniversary of the founding of the National Government. The Municipal Party Department of this city has decided to convene representatives from all walks of life at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 a.m. to hold a celebration assembly. The Municipal Government convened all its departments and bureau staff to hold a celebration group worship. All fleets of the navy stationed in Shanghai will raise flags to celebrate. The groundbreaking ceremony for the Ministry of Industry's Fishing Market, the Central Machinery Factory, and the Municipal Hospital will be held. The opening of the Workers' Union and Students' National Products Year will be held, and all industries will be closed for holiday. The details are recorded as follows:

General Assembly of All Sectors

The Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, in accordance with the central government's regulations for commemorative activities, has decided to convene representatives from all walks of life at the auditorium of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at Tianshenggong Bridge at 10:00 a.m. to hold a celebration assembly. The preparatory office has ordered workers to build a pine and cypress colored archway at the gate of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, with a bamboo cloth banner in the middle, inscribed with "Celebration Assembly of Representatives from All Sectors of Shanghai Municipality." The entrance passage is full of Party and national flags, and the four walls of the auditorium are pasted with red and green slogans. The portrait of the Premier is hung in the center of the rostrum, flanked by Party and national flags, and decorated with fresh flowers. The layout is extremely magnificent.

Hanging Flags and Decorations All organs, groups, schools, factories, and businesses in the city will hang flags and decorations from New Year's Day to the 3rd to celebrate together. Huashang Tram and public buses also hung national flags and posted various red and green slogans.

Two Routes for Seafarers The Seafarers' Special Party Department has decided to hold a celebration assembly at 10:00 a.m. today at Tairui Lane in Ximen. Standing Committee Member Yang Hu is appointed as chairman, and the Jun'an Seafarers' Elementary School will perform various recreational activities. The special Party departments of the Beijing-Shanghai and Hangzhou-Ningbo railways will also convene district party departments and district branches at 10:00 a.m. to hold a celebration assembly.

Municipal Government Celebration

The Municipal Government held a celebration ceremony at 9:00 a.m. today: (1) Play music, (2) Everyone stands at attention, (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party and national flags and the Premier's portrait, (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will, (5) The mayor's speech, (6) Reports by directors of various departments and bureaus, (7) Speech, (8) Perform group worship, (9) Photography, (10) Adjourn the meeting. The venue of the general assembly is in the Municipal Government Auditorium, which is decorated with pine and cypress flower balls, sky bridges, and stone steps, and decorated with red and green paper flowers, making it extremely solemn and splendid.

Message to the Citizens Mayor Wu Tiecheng's Message to the Citizens on New Year's Day of the 24th Year of the Republic of China states: The giant wheel of the times advances relentlessly along the historical trajectory of human groups. The curtain of the New Year of the 24th Year of the Republic of China is unfolding following the fleeting past year of 1934. Heaven acts vigorously, advancing without ceasing. On the occasion of the New Year, I feel even more inspired. I have been serving as the head of this city for three years. Following my duties and responsibilities, I am deeply concerned about the difficulties of the times. Therefore, I issue this message, hoping to encourage my fellow citizens together. The past three years have been a period of hardship and suffering for this city. Recalling the time when I received my appointment from the Party and the country, it coincided with the time when the Shanghai Incident was in full swing. I tried my best to respond to the difficult situation. At first, I worked hard to restore order and stabilize society, and then I diligently sought to provide disaster relief to the refugees and restore the war zone. Since the Municipal Government moved into its new building last year, it has followed the Premier's will and the plans of previous mayors to seek the gradual development of the city center and the gradual construction of various cultural undertakings. Although limited by time and financial resources, I dare not say that there have been special achievements, but I am deeply grateful for the assistance of wise people from all sides and the joint efforts of my colleagues in the Municipal Government. The image of recovery has gradually emerged, which is a source of comfort for us after the trauma. I quietly observe the current situation of this city. Since it has gradually recovered, we should continue to actively promote construction. The ancient governance of our country combined "education" and "nurturing." The way of construction puts the people's livelihood first. Considering the process of political evolution in various countries, it should be held as the standard for modern governance. Moreover, Shanghai, after its serious injuries, should recuperate and restore its inherent prosperity. At the same time, Shanghai is also the center of national culture, and we should strive to promote the popularization and improvement of education to establish the foundation for the revival and development of national culture. After extensive consideration of the historical principles of political evolution, the principle of "education" and "nurturing" are put forward to determine the direction of this year's governance, and I hope that the following matters will satisfy the urgent expectations of my fellow citizens. 1. Literacy Movement. The large number of illiterate people in our country is the greatest result of cultural decline and national weakness. According to the statistics of the French Confucian Cambo, the rise and fall of politics in various countries is closely related to the number of illiterate people. The municipal scholar Munro also believes that enlightened citizens are the driving force for municipal development. Although Shanghai has the advantage of being at the forefront of trends in various places, the proportion of illiterate people still accounts for the majority. In terms of school-age children, according to the latest statistics, they account for about 49.056%. In terms of adults, according to rough estimates, they also account for about 25%. Therefore, it is planned to use one year from this year to find ways to educate the illiterate people in this city between the ages of 15 and 30 as a basic movement for popularizing education, developing national power, and promoting municipal administration. 2. School Construction. There are many schools in this city, which can be said to be the best in the country. However, for thousands of years, due to the mistakes in the spirit of education and the lack of understanding of the connection between education and production, the more people who are educated, the fewer producers there are. The lack of life and the abundance of food have made the country poor and the people impoverished. The function of education lies first in increasing the knowledge and skills of human beings to cope with the environment and improve life. However, scholars in our country are not only not diligent in their four limbs, but also cannot distinguish the five grains. Therefore, as a result of promoting Confucian scholars for thousands of years, the national culture, whether spiritual or material, has not only made no significant progress, but has also declined day by day. It can be seen that education in our country has failed fundamentally and needs to be thoroughly transformed. Therefore, the future education policy of this city should aim at increasing the national production capacity. It is planned to open a vocational middle school within this year, and expand four agricultural schools, one in the Gaohang District, focusing on gardening experiments, two in the Luhang District, focusing on fruit tree experiments, three in the Zhenru District, focusing on rice cultivation experiments, and four in the Caojing District, focusing on animal husbandry experiments. Other aspects such as primary and secondary education are also the foundation for transforming education and training citizens. Therefore, it is planned to build two complete middle schools in the city center, and add facilities to the Xinlu Normal School, Yangjing Junior High School, and Wusong Junior High School. Model elementary schools will be built in the two districts of Hunan and Zhabei, and fifteen central elementary schools will be set up in various rural areas. 3. Social Construction. Residence is the primary requirement for people's lives, and it is also a serious problem in modern cities around the world, especially in this city. In recent years, the construction industry in this city has been progressing day by day, but with the decline of the national economy, the lives of ordinary people in this city have become increasingly difficult. Thatched houses are lined up, dwellings are simple, dirt and filth are hidden, epidemics are rampant, and the old and weak are in dire straits, which is a terrible sight. It not only damages the appearance of the city, but also hinders hygiene. It is necessary to actively provide relief. Therefore, it is planned to raise millions of dollars within this year to build six model new villages for civilians in the South City, Zhabei, Pudong, Huxi, and Hudong, totaling more than 3,000 rooms, in order to improve the lives of civilians in this city. Furthermore, civilian nurseries are also an important social construction in this city. The industry and commerce of this city are developing, and there are many factories. Civilians, whether men or women, are forced to make a living, so they often cannot take care of the comfort of infants. Therefore, it is planned to build a civilian nursery in the north and south of this city, so that the workers of the civilians can reduce the burden. Other matters such as the construction of public halls, the rectification of slaughterhouses, and the improvement of the lives of rickshaw pullers will also be actively planned according to the financial resources available. 4. Water Conservancy Construction - Water conservancy construction is the key to revitalizing the countryside today. The seawall project in this city has been neglected for many years, and the collapse is getting worse. Every autumn flood, the collapse is worrying. Although funds have been allocated and construction has been carried out over the years, due to the limitations of financial resources, it has been repaired and collapsed from time to time, and it is still a hidden danger. Thinking of this, I am deeply afraid, and it is urgent to coordinate large sums of money to seek a plan that will work once and for all. Even after the Shanghai Incident, when financial resources were scarce, we should also try to inject funds to achieve it. 5. Transportation Construction - Shanghai is the only commercial port in our country and a world-famous city. However, modern transportation facilities such as commercial flight ports are still lacking. The original Longhua Airport covers an area of only 280 acres, which is not enough for application. Therefore, special methods are used to open up and increase it to 970 acres, making it the first water and land flight port in our country. Longhua is located in the upper reaches of the Huangpu River, and the terrain and transportation are very convenient. The completion of this port will surely increase the prosperity of Shanghai. All of the above are only the main points. Politics does not lie in much talk, and I do not want to describe them one by one. Annual plans are in the spring, so I sincerely express my thoughts. Although there may be some delays due to financial constraints, this heart is always held in mind, and I will strive to realize them as scheduled. New Year's Day of the 24th Year of the Republic of China.

The Shanghai Municipal Hygiene Testing Laboratory is also located in the city center. Yesterday's Banks Settle Accounts for Disaster Relief

All Industries Follow Money Shops in Settling Accounts on February 3rd

Three Banks (Central, China, Communications) Continue Lending to Maintain Finance

According to the New Voice Agency, yesterday was the last day of the 23rd year of the Republic according to the solar calendar, and also the date for banks to settle their accounts. All banks worked overnight. The Central Bank and other banks continued to lend money to maintain finance. The details are recorded as follows.

Bank Account Settlement

Shanghai's banks were very busy yesterday settling their accounts and handling receipts. All worked overnight and will be closed for three days on New Year's Day. As for the money shops, it has been decided that February 3rd of the 24th year of the Republic will be the date for the final settlement of accounts for the 23rd year of the Republic. All industries will also take the settlement date of the money shops as the final settlement date. Therefore, they did not settle accounts yesterday but will be closed for two days starting on New Year's Day. Although yesterday morning was the settlement date for banks, the overnight loan interest rate in the money market opened at 55 cents, down 5 cents from the previous day.

Continued Lending

The Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, in order to stabilize Shanghai's financial situation, designated 10 million yuan to be used for mortgage loans to money shops. Yesterday was Monday, and they continued to announce loan interest rates and handle lending matters. All those who requested loans were granted loans. Including the previous loans, a total of more than 4 million yuan has been lent out.

Entering Beijing with Nie Yifu at the Beginning of the Year

According to the Central News Agency, Mr. Coode, the League of Nations expert sent to China for technical cooperation, arrived in Shanghai at 9:00 AM yesterday on the British shipping company's Nerthda, sailing from England. The ship docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf. The National Economic Commission specially sent Guo Dehua, secretary of the commission, and Nie Yifu, an expert sent by the League of Nations to China, to welcome him. After landing, they went to Room 501 of the Cathay Hotel to rest. Then, they went to Qiqi Road to meet with Song Ziwen, a standing committee member of the National Economic Commission. Mr. Coode is a member of the London Institution of Civil Engineers. Considering the fatigue of the journey, he plans to spend the New Year in Shanghai and then go to Beijing with Nie Yifu. Then, they will go together to the Northwest to inspect various water conservancy and highway construction projects. As for Has, the liaison officer for technical cooperation specially sent by the League of Nations to China, he is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai by ship from Geneva at the end of January.

Revenue and Expenditure of Customs Duties in the 23rd Year of the Republic of China

Approved and Announced by the Ministry of Finance

Customs revenue in the 23rd year of the Republic of China (import duty, export duty, transit duty, tonnage dues, disaster relief surtax, and customs surtax) totaled approximately 33,460,000 yuan in national currency, calculated in round numbers. The total tax revenue for the 22nd year was 33,950,000 yuan in national currency.

The numbers for each item of tax revenue in the 23rd year and the 22nd year are compared below:

Customs House Name Tax Revenue for the 23rd Year Increase/Decrease Compared to the 22nd Year

Jianghai Customs 175,400,000 yuan Decrease of 800,000 yuan

Jinhai Customs 41,100,000 yuan Decrease of 700,000 yuan

Jiaohai Customs 20,200,000 yuan Decrease of 2,400,000 yuan

Jianghan Customs 19,400,000 yuan Decrease of 1,000,000 yuan

Yuehai Customs 8,000,000 yuan Decrease of 3,000,000 yuan

Jiulong Customs 7,500,000 yuan Decrease of 800,000 yuan

Chaohai Customs 5,800,000 yuan Decrease of 2,100,000 yuan

Xiamen Customs 5,500,000 yuan Increase of 400,000 yuan

It is verified that the total import duty was 132.7 million gold units, of which 83% was actually collected in customs gold unit notes, and the remainder was converted into national currency for collection according to the daily customs exchange rate for gold units.

The left table details the amount of customs duties collected by each important customs house in the 23rd year, and the comparison of increase or decrease with the tax revenue numbers in the 22nd year (calculated in round numbers).

23rd Year 22nd Year

Import Duty 132.7 million gold units 135,763,000 gold units

Export Duty 24.7 million yuan in national currency 23,245,000 yuan in national currency

Transit Duty 16.9 million yuan in national currency 18,003,000 yuan in national currency

Tonnage Dues 4.3 million yuan in national currency 4,402,000 yuan in national currency

Disaster Relief Surtax

(Import Surtax) 6.6 million gold units 6,586,000 gold units

(Export Surtax) 1.2 million yuan in national currency 1,250,000 yuan in national currency

Customs Surtax

(Import Surtax) 6.6 million gold units 6,583,000 gold units

(Export Surtax) 1.2 million yuan in national currency 1,248,000 yuan in national currency

Foreign Debt Indemnities

The principal and interest of the Anglo-German Supplementary Loan of 1898, the Boxer Indemnity, and the Rehabilitation Loan of 1913, which matured this year, have all been paid in full from customs duties, totaling 75,414,347.81 yuan in national currency. The amount paid last year was 85,742,482.36 yuan in national currency. The principal and interest of the US Wheat and Flour Loan of the 20th year of the Republic of China, which matured this year, totaled 3,439,455.24 US dollars, equivalent to 9,890,615.07 yuan in national currency, and has been paid in full from the disaster relief surtax revenue. In addition, the interest on the US Cotton and Wheat Loan of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, which matured this year, amounting to 1,714,023.75 yuan in national currency, has also been withdrawn from the special funds stored from last year's disaster relief surtax revenue for payment.

Domestic Debt Bonds

Regarding domestic debt bonds guaranteed by customs duties, the fund to be allocated this year has been following the order of the National Government of February 24 of the 21st year of the Republic of China, and 8.6 million yuan in national currency has been allocated monthly from customs duties and transferred to the custody and control of the National Debt Fund Management Committee. In addition, a total of 29,415,000 yuan in national currency has been allocated to the committee as the principal and interest repayment fund for the customs bonds of the 22nd year of the Republic of China and the customs bonds of the 23rd year of the Republic of China.

Customs Houses in the Three Eastern Provinces

What must be stated here is that part of the principal and interest of various debts and indemnities guaranteed by customs duties, which were previously borne by Dalian and the customs houses in the three eastern provinces, have not been remitted since those customs houses were seized in the summer of the 21st year of the Republic of China.

Celebrating the Victory Over the Communists the Day After Tomorrow

Mayor Wu Published a Long Article Last Night

Historical Lessons of the Collapse of the Communists

In order to expand the celebration of the victory over the Communists, the Municipal Government has specifically scheduled a radio broadcast celebration rally at Zhongxi Electric on the 3rd of this month. In addition to speeches by Mayor Wu and Director Pan, people from the entertainment industry will also participate in the broadcast. Radio stations in this city will also broadcast celebration programs at the same time to celebrate. Mayor Wu published two articles last night titled "Historical Lessons of the Collapse of the Communists". They are transcribed below: 1. The way to save and revive the country today should first focus on both the root and the branch, and enrich the people's strength. 2. The rampant Communists are actually the extreme cause of the depletion of the people's strength and the decline of national power. 3. Revolutionary doctrines must have historical and ethnic characteristics and social realism. 4. Otherwise, it will inevitably be rejected by the social "love power" and eliminated by the national "vitality". In recent years, our country has been beset by worries. Externally, strong enemies are pressing on the border, shaking the foundation of the country. Internally, communist bandits are wreaking havoc, causing trouble in the heartland. Those who speak of national affairs either advocate resisting foreign aggression to secure the interior, or advocate securing the interior to resist foreign aggression. Those who advocate resisting foreign aggression believe that only by resisting foreign aggression can the spirit of the nation be revitalized and the turbulent public sentiment be stabilized. Without resisting foreign aggression, there is no way to secure the interior, and without resisting foreign aggression, there is no way to save the country. Those who advocate securing the interior say that only by securing the interior can the constraints of resisting the enemy be removed, the vitality of society be cultivated, and the strength of the country be enriched. Securing the interior is enough to resist foreign aggression, and securing the interior is the same as resisting foreign aggression. At this time, those who bear the heavy responsibility of the country cannot be afraid of difficulties and seek temporary peace, nor can they act rashly. They must not cater to the preferences of the times and bet the country's fate on a single throw. They should first calm their minds, endure their tempers, and deal with the situation calmly. They should look at both internal and external affairs, focus on both the root and the branch, establish a grand plan for saving the country and resisting foreign aggression, and clearly indicate the direction for the whole country to go. In the past, Sun Zhaoxian of the Song Dynasty said, "To resist foreign aggression, one must first govern the interior. To govern the interior, one must first appease the people. If one only knows about military needs and does not care about the suffering of the people, then resisting foreign aggression will not be effective, and internal worries will come first." Zeng Qing (Hu Wenzhonggong) also said, "To resist foreign aggression, one must first pacify the interior." The words of Sun and Zeng do not mean that foreign aggression should not be resisted, but that the way to resist foreign aggression must seek the basics. Things have a root and a branch, and affairs have a beginning and an end. Saving the country and resisting foreign aggression is a difficult and serious task. The modern military forces of various countries are based on the development level of their national science, culture, and all political, economic, educational, and social national power. China's deep weakness and the arrival of national disasters have complex and long-standing historical reasons. Therefore, today's way to save the country, to treat the root, is most important to enrich national power. To treat the branch, there is nothing more urgent than to clear the communist bandits. If national power is not strong, it is because the people's power is insufficient. The people's power is insufficient because of the immaturity of industry and the bankruptcy of the countryside. The rampant communist bandits are the extreme cause of the depletion of the people's power and the decline of national power. If they are not thoroughly eradicated, not only will the people not be able to live and work in peace, but all plans will be constrained by them, and even resisting foreign aggression and defending oneself will not be effectively implemented. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, worried about this, gathered the national army and devoted all efforts to suppress and clear out the red bandits who were consuming the people's power and causing trouble in the heartland, and to save the people who were in deep water and displaced, so as to enrich the people's power, develop national power, and prepare for resisting foreign aggression. All of this is to treat both the root and the branch, and to look at both internal and external affairs. It is not only an easy principle for saving the country and surviving today, but also the spirit that statesmen who endure humiliation, bear heavy burdens, and bury their heads in hard work should have. Today, the communist scourge that has rotted society and caused trouble in the heartland, and the bandit dens that have persecuted the nation for years, have finally been relied upon by the whole nation's cooperation and support, the hard work and sacrifice of the communist-suppression generals, and the hard work of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. The remnants of the bandits are fleeing like wolves and pigs, have lost their dependence, and are terrified and scattered. Their strength is weak and their power is scattered. It is easy to thoroughly eliminate them. Such objective and obvious constructions and reality, and what it shows to our people, is enough to prove that the national policies set by the central government in recent years are absolutely appropriate. This sign and this subtlety should not only be clearly understood by the Chinese people facing a crisis, but also be thoroughly believed by the whole country. Furthermore, a healthy country is based on healthy citizens, and healthy citizens are based on healthy thoughts. Healthy thoughts can nurture healthy vitality. With healthy vitality, one can determine the correct direction, promote the development of society, create a glorious and brilliant culture, and continue the long and great life of the nation. Therefore, revolutionary doctrines must have historical and national characteristics and social realism in order to conform to the objective needs and generate a common belief, thereby creating a great force for saving the world, rescuing the nation, and reviving the country. If one blindly follows doctrines that do not conform to the national conditions, picks up incomplete theories, and cuts one's feet to fit the shoes, one will eventually be rejected by the social "love power" and eliminated by the national "vitality". All of our people should deeply recognize this repeatedly proven historical lesson, and those who are still deluded should deeply regret the serious and difficult times today, turn back as soon as possible, and return to the Three Principles of the People that are suitable for the national conditions, unite as one, and jointly overcome the critical national crisis. The country is fortunate, and the nation is fortunate. (Shanghai, Lunar New Year's Eve, 23rd year of the Republic of China)

Yu Xianglin Talks About Resolving the Postal Communication Issue

Mail from Outside the Customs to Inside the Customs

Postal Stamps Are Divided into Four Types

After the northeastern four provinces were occupied by the Japanese army, the postal communication in that area was blockaded by our country. It has been two years and five months since its implementation in July 1932. Now, as a result of negotiations between the Chinese and Japanese authorities, the issue of postal communication in the Northeast has been resolved through negotiation without involving politics. Various postal items, except for parcels and remittances, will have the blockade lifted starting on January 10 and February 1, respectively. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency inquired with the postal authorities about the details yesterday. According to Zhu Menghou, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Postal Administration, the postal communication matter is still handled according to the method of traffic by private individuals to organize institutions to transport and deliver mail. Therefore, this bureau only received a notice and did not receive an order from the ministry. He also said that he could not disclose any details as he was not directly involved. The reporter then learned from the bureau that Yu Xianglin (former Director of the General Affairs Department of the General Administration), the postmaster of the Taiyuan Provincial Capital who had just arrived in Shanghai from Shanxi, was involved in the postal communication matter. He was found at the New Asia Restaurant and questioned about the details. According to him, the postal communication issue started negotiations shortly after the implementation of traffic. The Chinese side was represented by himself and Gao Zongwu, and the Japanese side was represented by the Kwantung Army, which sent Iga and Shibayama as responsible representatives. They discussed in Pingjin for three months, and recently decided to follow the traffic method by private individuals to organize postal agencies, one in Shanhaiguan and one in Gubeikou, to start delivering mail on January 10. Mail from inside the customs to outside the customs will still use the current postal stamps. Postal stamps from outside the customs to inside the customs will be printed with special postal stamps. The types of postal stamps will be based on the old stamps before September 18, divided into two-cent, four-cent, eight-cent, and twelve-cent denominations. The colors are divided into two types. The two-cent and four-cent stamps will have two ears of wheat drawn in a cross shape. The eight-cent and twelve-cent stamps will have landscapes drawn on them. The words used will only be "Postal Administration", and the words "China" and "Japanese Puppet" will not be added. The expenses of the two institutions will be covered by private individuals in advance as start-up expenses. Thereafter, 1% will be deducted from postal remittances to cover the regular expenses. It is investigated that our country has implemented a postal blockade since July 1932, which has now been two and a half years. Now, forced by the situation and due to the inconvenience of communication for the people, we are seeking a mending remedy, etc. Mr. Yu is still staying in Shanghai for a week and will then go north, first to Peiping, and then return to his original post in Taiyuan once the postal communication is implemented. According to another source, the reporter was told that there were seven decisions made regarding the Kwantung postal communication. As for telegrams, which have the same nature as postal letters, the reporter inquired with the telegraph bureau, which said that at present, the telecommunications in the eastern provinces are relayed through Yantai and Dalian. Telegrams have a fixed line, and the actual reporting is still the same as before. There is no news of any new developments.

Shanghai Grain Merchants' Cash Purchase Detained by Tongshan County

Shanghai Has Sent a Telegram Asking for Release

The Central Government has long had a clear order prohibiting the carrying of cash out of the country. If anyone is found to have exceeded the limited amount, it will be confiscated. A certain grain store in this port sent personnel to the Xuhai area to purchase miscellaneous grains. Because they carried a large amount of cash, they were discovered by the local government and deemed to have violated the ban. The cash was confiscated and the people were detained. Shanghai has received the news and has sent a telegram to rescue them. The details are described as follows.

Huge Sum Taken to Xuhai

A certain grain merchant in this port needed to purchase miscellaneous grains, so they prepared cash of several tens of thousands of yuan, packed in three boxes, and entrusted two staff members, Mr. Lu and Mr. Wang, to carry this amount and personally go to the various ports of Xuhai to directly purchase miscellaneous grains and soybeans for sale in Shanghai. Because the local villagers did not like banknotes, they carried cash. Unexpectedly, this matter happened in Tongshan County.

County Government Detains Cash and People

The county police stated that the limit for carrying cash was 50 yuan per person. Now, these two people were carrying such a large amount of cash, which not only violated the government ban but also had suspicion of smuggling. Therefore, the cash was detained, and Mr. Lu and Mr. Wang were sent to the county government for investigation. Although the two repeatedly stated that they were purchasing miscellaneous grains and were not smuggling, it was to no avail.

Shanghai Receives Telegram

After this matter occurred, Mr. Lu and Mr. Wang requested Tongshan County to allow them to send a telegram to Shanghai to report the matter and to ask Shanghai to send a telegram to prove the facts for their early release. Yesterday, the grain store received a telegram from Xuzhou. Because the matter was of great importance, they immediately reported it to the Municipal Miscellaneous Grain Association, requesting the association to find a way to send a telegram to Tongshan County requesting the release of Mr. Lu and Mr. Wang and the return of the original cash.

Various Parties Send Telegrams of Proof

The grain store originally planned to transport the purchased miscellaneous grains to Shanghai via the Longhai Railway and entrust the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to load them. Therefore, the Miscellaneous Grain Association has requested Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, to send a telegram to Qian Zongze, Director of the Longhai Railway Bureau, to quickly issue a proof and inform Tongshan County to release Mr. Lu and Mr. Wang and return the cash as soon as possible. Liu Hongsheng has complied with the association's request and sent a telegram to Director Qian. Yesterday afternoon, Director Qian had a reply telegram to Shanghai, saying that he had forwarded the original telegram to the Tongshan County Government for investigation.

Private Postal Bureaus File Administrative Appeal

Ministry of Communications' Reply States That the Request is Difficult to Approve

Private Bureaus Present Reasons for Requesting Separate Disposal

According to the East China News Agency, the Ministry of Communications has ordered all private postal bureaus in the country to close down by the end of the 23rd year of the Republic of China. The deadline has now arrived. The private postal bureaus, because more than 100,000 employees will have difficulty making a living after the closure, have requested a five-year extension. The Ministry of Communications, because the matter belongs to the unified postal system, has replied that it cannot be approved. The day before yesterday, the private postal bureaus submitted three reasons to the Ministry of Communications to file an administrative appeal. It seems that the disturbance will continue to expand. The Ministry's reply and the original text of the private bureaus' appeal are recorded separately below.

Ministry of Communications' Reply

The submission has been noted. It is investigated that the banning of private postal bureaus is a necessary move to unify the postal system. The postal system is a state-operated business, which is a common practice in all countries around the world. In the 17th year of the Republic of China, the National Communications Conference resolved that all private postal bureaus should be banned by the 19th year of the Republic of China. It should have been implemented on schedule. Later, because the postal industry repeatedly requested, five temporary registration and licensing measures for private postal bureaus were formulated, allowing them to continue operating temporarily. This temporary measure was originally to give the postal industry workers and others the opportunity to gradually change their livelihood and has been extended on record. The period given has been several years and cannot be said to be ungenerous. Even this time, the order issued by this Ministry limiting the gradual cessation of operations of private postal bureaus to the end of the 23rd year of the Republic of China was issued on November 23 of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, with a period of more than a year. The postal industry can abide by the Ministry's order, gradually close down, and seek another livelihood, which is also more than enough. But they did not do this, and they are only harming themselves. Now that this bureau has clearly defined the deadline for cessation and the Executive Yuan has repeatedly issued orders, the requested extension and the prior cessation are difficult to approve. The representatives are to convey this to the fellow industry members to comply with the order and close down, so as to uphold the rule of law. This is the reply.

Civil Affairs Bureau Appeal

Regarding the appeal against the punishment imposed by the Ministry's No. 4059 decree, according to the law, the appellants, because the private postal bureaus were closing down and the deadline was imminent, requested an extension and suspension of execution, hoping for consideration. On the 24th of this month, the Ministry's No. 4059 decree was received, stating (the decree is omitted as it appeared previously), and so on. The legal principles were not examined, nor was the benefit considered, making it difficult to accept. Therefore, an appeal is filed within the legal deadline. The reasons are listed below. It is noted that the postal service should be exclusively operated by the state, as clearly stipulated in Article 1 of the Postal Law. However, Article 2 clarifies the scope as the collection, sending, and delivery of letters and postcards, while remittances, parcels, and savings can be operated concurrently by the post office, indicating that it is not a postal monopoly. Our private postal bureaus have a long history. In the past, before our country had a postal service, letters, money, and parcels were all delivered through them. After the establishment of the postal service, people in cities with post offices have abandoned these for the postal service regarding letter delivery. Their business is practically limited to money and parcels, merely eking out a living based on past reputation. Furthermore, even in recent years, the collection and sending of letters have been subject to the five restrictions of the "Temporary Measures for Private Postal Bureaus to Register and Obtain Licenses," and they are all sealed into general packages and delivered by the post office. The rise and fall of their business can be easily determined upon verification. Therefore, their existence does not harm the progress of the postal service. On the contrary, banning them would deprive most rural people of their convenience. Even if the Ministry is determined to unify the postal service and believes that private postal bureaus should absolutely not collect and deliver letters, restrictions can be imposed on this letter business. Alternatively, the "Temporary Measures for Private Postal Bureaus to Register and Obtain Licenses" can be abolished, so that private postal bureaus no longer collect and send letters (or postcards), which would be sufficient. It is not appropriate to issue an order to shut down businesses and enforce it, nor to disregard the interests of most rural people nationwide in sending silver and parcel objects when the appellants request an extension of the closure and suspension of execution. The reply states, "The request for an extension and prior suspension of execution is difficult to approve," and so on, implying an imminent and compulsory execution, which has no legal basis, restricts the people's freedom of business, and violates Article 317 of the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China. This is the first illegality of the original decree's disposition. Secondly, from a factual point of view, even if the past contributions of private postal bureaus to the country and society are not considered, the interests of the majority of people in remote rural areas should be considered. People in these areas find it inconvenient to send and deliver letters because post office mailboxes are not yet widely available, and remitting silver and parcels, especially to post offices far from the city, involves complicated procedures, guarantees, and seals, which ignorant villagers find even more difficult. At a time when education is not yet universal and the postal service is not yet perfect, the social needs for private postal bureaus should be taken into account, their existence encouraged, and their improvement urged. Moreover, the premise of national governance is the welfare of society and the majority of the people. All undertakings beneficial to the masses, whether public or private, should be maintained, as is the case in all countries of the world. Now, only paying attention to superficiality, knowing only that the postal service in all countries of the world is a state monopoly, and following suit, without observing the actual situation in the country, orders and decrees are hastily issued to close down businesses within a time limit, and furthermore, compulsory execution is carried out, which is clearly inappropriate in terms of governance principles. This is the second inappropriateness of the original decree's disposition. Furthermore, the private postal bureaus employ more than 100,000 people, scattered across provinces, doing business thousands of miles away, originally relying on salaries for their livelihoods. In recent years, their business has become a spent force, and at a time when the rural economy nationwide is bankrupt, disasters and famines occur frequently in various provinces, industry and commerce are declining, and all industries are withering. It is true, as the original decree states, that "the order has been issued for more than a year, and there is ample time to seek another livelihood." However, it is not known that under today's social circumstances, even if one wants to change careers, there is nothing to do. Once the order to close down businesses is enforced, these more than 100,000 employees and hundreds of thousands of family members will inevitably become starving corpses. If some are strong and resort to violence, social security will also be affected. Therefore, private postal bureaus have even more need for an extension of closure and suspension of execution. Even if the order to close down businesses is to be enforced, the government should find ways to provide relief and properly arrange measures to alleviate suffering and maintain security. However, after the appellants' request, no consideration was given to it. This is the third inappropriateness of the original decree's disposition. In summary, it is requested that the Ministry revoke the No. 4059 decree issued in December of the 23rd year (1934) and make another appropriate disposition to comply with the law and stabilize society. It would be most virtuous and convenient. Respectfully submitted to Zhu, Minister of Transportation, by the representatives of the national private postal bureaus: Hua Yunjin, Yin Yuantong, Wang Dashi, Zhuang Gengtang, Qiu Zhensheng, Ren Shiting, Pan Wentian, Guarantor: Yu Qiaqing.

American Cantonese Man Arrested for Bringing a Woman from the United States to Shanghai

Due to Being Sued in the United States

The Great American Evening News reports that an American Cantonese man, Rin Lem, was recently accused by the Southern California District Court of the United States for bringing a young girl to the United States with the intention of selling her into prostitution and other immoral acts. This morning (31st), when the Cantonese man and the woman arrived in Shanghai from the United States on the Dollar Line Company mail ship, President Harrison, an executive officer of the U.S. Consulate General arrested them at the pier. Both were sitting in first class. According to the Cantonese man, the woman traveling with him is his biological daughter and is also an American citizen. U.S. Consul General Hillmeck has ordered the Cantonese man to post a bail of US$2,500. The woman was not detained because her nationality was unclear. According to a recent report from the Associated Press in Los Angeles, the Cantonese man sold a young girl to a businessman in Los Angeles for US$1,800, and the payment has been made. The girl is about 20 years old, with a beautiful face, and was weeping sadly at the time. She was then separated from her occasional "husband" and demanded a separate living allowance of US$100 from the businessman in the Los Angeles court. Before the case was decided, the woman suddenly disappeared. The businessman then asked the court to investigate. It was then confirmed by the immigration authorities that the woman and the Cantonese man who sold her had taken the President Harrison to Shanghai. The U.S. judicial authorities in Shanghai were immediately notified by telegram to detain him first. The formal evidence needed for his return to the United States for handling will be sent to Shanghai for verification. It is reported that these documents are already on their way. If the Cantonese man cannot pay the full bail, he will be temporarily detained in the Xiamen Road West Prison to await the arrival of the documents. The woman traveling with him was not detained because the U.S. authorities did not prosecute her. Even if she is prosecuted, she cannot be extradited back to the United States unless it is confirmed that she is indeed an American citizen, because there is no extradition treaty between China and the United States.

Manager Loses a Fur Coat from the Shop and It Leads to a Death

Threatened with Investigation, He Couldn't Bear It and Committed Suicide Due to Fear of Humiliation

Zhai Alin, a 27-year-old native of Jiading, was a shop clerk at the Jutai Bingji Tobacco Shop at No. 10 Tong'an Lane, Old Yong'an Street, French Concession, earning eight yuan a month. He had been employed for two or three years. Recently, a fur coat belonging to the manager of the shop, Chen Fucai (a 22-year-old Ningbo native), was placed in a trunk in the reception room. The coat, worth about 30 or 40 yuan, was newly made last year. It suddenly went missing sometime between the 23rd and 25th of last month. Only this one fur coat had disappeared without a trace. He suspected that two old clerks and an apprentice in the shop had stolen it, and declared that he would investigate and recover it, but he had not yet done so. Unexpectedly, Zhai Alin learned that the manager's fur coat had been lost and that he was going to investigate them. Although he had not committed the theft, his conscience was clear. However, he thought that if he was questioned in person, he would be humiliated. In a moment of panic, he suddenly had suicidal thoughts. On the evening of the 27th, he left the shop and bought raw opium. He checked into Room 7 of the Fuxing Hotel at No. 325 Avenue Edward VII. That night, he swallowed the raw opium and committed suicide. The next morning, the poison took effect. The tea boy, Xia Abing (a 24-year-old native of Suzhou), discovered it and reported it to the French police, who sent detectives to investigate. They rushed Zhai to Renji Hospital, where he vomited the poison after treatment. He regained consciousness and could speak. His cousin, Zhai Axing (a 30-year-old senior clerk at the Hengchun Tobacco Shop at No. 2 Fengyu Lane, North Station Boundary Road), received the news and went to the hospital to visit him. Alin told his cousin the details of the suicide. He wanted to wait until he recovered and was discharged from the hospital before dealing with it. Unexpectedly, Alin's internal organs were still poisoned by the opium, and it suddenly recurred. The rescue was ineffective, and he died in the hospital at 6:25 p.m. on the 30th. The hospital notified the police, who sent a detective to the Jutai Tobacco Shop to investigate the cause of the suicide. His body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch to be examined. Yesterday, the police reported to the Second Special Court Procuratorate and appointed Wang Ren to accompany forensic doctor Jiang and clerk Zhao to the morgue at noon to examine the body. They began the official investigation after confirming the body. The detectives first reported the case, and then Zhai Axing, a relative of the deceased, claimed that his cousin Alin had died a wrongful death and requested justice. The deceased had parents, wife, and children at home, and he had sent a letter to notify them that they could arrive today to collect the body. The officials questioned the witnesses Chen Fucai and Xia Abing about the investigation of the lost fur coat and the discovery of the deceased's suicide. The officials then ruled that Zhai Alin had died of opium poisoning and that the family members could claim the body after signing a guarantee.

The Weather in This City Turned Cold Yesterday

The weather in this city has been very warm for the past two weeks. The temperature on the Fahrenheit thermometer is often between 50 and 60 degrees, and it is often sunny and rainy. There is often heavy fog during the day. It continued to rain for three or four days from last Wednesday, which the citizens found very annoying. It was not until the evening before yesterday that the wind suddenly changed, and the north wind was biting. In the dream at midnight, the doors and windows were rattled by the wind. Yesterday morning, it felt especially shivering. The northwest wind roared all day, presenting a severe cold.

Vehicle Licenses Issued as Usual at Noon: For the convenience of those applying for various vehicle licenses, the Vehicle Donation Department of the Donation Bureau will continue to operate from 9:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m. from January 3 to January 17, without any rest at noon.

Bicycle Licenses Issued in Five Locations: From January 3 to January 17, applicants for bicycle licenses can apply at the Gordon Road Police Station, the Rickshaw Inspection Office, the Yulin Road Police Station, and the Yangshupu Police Station, in addition to the Vehicle Donation Department. After the 18th, they will be issued by the Mountain Vehicle Donation Department.

Driver's Licenses Should Be Renewed: It is reported that licenses for drivers of cars and motorized bicycles should be renewed from January 1. The application location is the Traffic Department in the Central Police Station, and the fee is one yuan per license.

Suspect Arrested in Shanghai in the Murder Case of Mr. Shi Liangcai

He is Zhang Wentian, a watchman from Yongyuan Lane on Tianjin Road.

Police Investigation Says the Watchman Never Left Shanghai

After the murder of our newspaper's General Manager, Mr. Shi Liangcai, the Zhejiang provincial military and police authorities immediately launched a strict search for the perpetrators. Although several suspects have been arrested, the true culprit has not yet been apprehended. Recently, the Hangzhou County Local Court Prosecutor's Office sent a document to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court stating that Zhang Wentian, also known as A'er, a native of Nantong, who serves as a watchman in Yongyuan Lane on Tianjin Road in Shanghai, is highly suspected of involvement in the Shi case and should be apprehended by warrant. The First Special Court issued warrant No. 5344 and sent it to the General Inspectorate of Police for execution. Consequently, Chief Constable Zhang Xiaolin was ordered to proceed to the address on the morning of the 29th of this month at 11:00 AM and arrest Zhang. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Criminal Division of the First Special Court, where Criminal Judge Qian Hongye presided over the interrogation. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, explained the background of the case, stating that according to police investigation, Zhang Wentian has been working in Shanghai for over twenty years and has never left the city. He requested the court to verify this information. When questioned, Zhang Wentian denied the facts and hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to defend him, requesting that the Hangzhou County Court Prosecutor's Office be asked to send the confession in which the defendant was named to the court for rebuttal. He argued that since Zhang Wentian has been in Shanghai for over twenty years and has never left, how could he have committed the crime in Hangzhou? He asked the court to take this into consideration.

The court then ordered that the case be adjourned to January 8th for further hearing, pending notification to the Hangzhou County Court Prosecutor's Office to send personnel to escort him.

Children's Year Ceremony Pending

Other Matters Proceed According to the Original Plan

The 24th year of the Republic of China has long been designated as Children's Year by the government. Today is the first day of the 24th year of the Republic of China. The China Child Welfare Association and the Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee originally agreed to hold the opening ceremony of Children's Year and consulted with major daily newspapers to publish special issues on Children's Year to express their enthusiasm for celebration. However, it has been learned by reporters that this matter has encountered difficulties. Although the establishment of Children's Year has been approved by the government, the implementation steps have not yet been officially promulgated nationwide by the government, and the Children's Year Preparatory Committee is

still being organized by the Ministry of Education. Therefore, Shanghai City will not be able to hold the opening ceremony of Children's Year today, and major daily newspapers have also postponed the publication of special issues on Children's Year. Yesterday afternoon, reporters specifically visited the China Child Welfare Association, where Mr. Chen Zhengfan, a member of the Education Group of the association, received them and explained the details of the matter. According to Mr. Chen, the Child Welfare Association received a reply from the Ministry of Education a few days ago, stating that the organizational outline of the Children's Year Preparatory Committee has been approved by the ministry and is in active progress. As Children's Year is a matter of national concern, the government will definitely promulgate it nationwide to ensure that all regions proceed in an orderly and unified manner. Since Shanghai City held an opening ceremony for Children's Year in Shanghai once on New Year's Day in the 23rd year of the Republic of China, it is not appropriate to hold it again separately at this time when the government has not yet issued an order for all regions to hold it. As for the editing of the special issue on Children's Year, the Education Group of the association is still responsible for it. Recently, the association has received inscriptions and articles from President Lin of the National Government, Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, President Sun of the Legislative Yuan, President Dai of the Examination Yuan, President Yu of the Control Yuan, Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education, Minister Huang of the Ministry of Interior, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, Mayor Wu of Shanghai, Cai Yuanpei, Xiong Xiling, Wang Zhengting Zhang Zhijiang, Luo Jialun, and Pan Gongzhan, all of which are exquisitely written and beautiful. Once the government issues an order for all regions to hold Children's Year on a scheduled date, it will be disclosed in Shanghai newspapers. Furthermore, although the opening ceremony of Children's Year will not be held today, the Children's Welfare Association and the Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee will still carry out the children's welfare matters that should be held during Children's Year in an orderly manner in accordance with the original plan.

Cake Shop Oil Pot Catches Fire

Old Woman Unable to Save Neighbor's Child

The Fuxing Fujian Tea Food Cake and Candy Shop, opened by a Fujianese at No. 270 next door in Fukang Lane on Avenue Joffre

, at 0:30 PM yesterday (December 31st), while working on goods in the kitchen, the oil pot became too hot, and in an instant, green smoke billowed straight up, igniting debris. Job Application Status of Chinese People at Japanese Job Placement Center

According to the Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun, although the Shanghai Job Placement Center established by the Japanese on Jiaxing Road has not been open for long, it has been attracting a steady stream of job seekers in this time of economic recession. According to the report handled by the center for the end of 1934, from December 1st to 23rd, the total number of job seekers was 169, of which 48 were Japanese (38 men and 10 women) and 121 were Chinese (102 men and 19 women). The number of Chinese job seekers is approximately three times that of Japanese job seekers. The age of the job seekers, regardless of Chinese or Japanese, is approximately 25 years old. Among the Japanese, more than half are high school graduates, and approximately 3-4 have graduated from specialized schools or have equivalent qualifications. Most of the Chinese are primary school graduates, with 14-15 who have grown up in Japan and received Japanese university education. The hope of most of these job seekers is only to find a place to eat, without any extravagant expectations. Of these job seekers, a total of 28 have been recommended by the center for employment, including 17 Japanese (11 men and 6 women) and

11 Chinese (8 men and 3 women). The types of jobs are: 5 Japanese company employees, 5 shop clerks, 1 cook, 1 maid, 1 broker, and 1 waitress. Among the Chinese who found employment, there were 1 company employee, 1 shop clerk, 1 translator, 2 cooks, 3 waiters, 2 maids, and 1 wet nurse. Although the salary varies depending on the job, even graduates of specialized schools earn only 30-35 yuan. This is enough to show the increasingly difficult social economy.

In the past, by the order of his parents, he was betrothed to Wang Sidai (27 years old) of Wang Zhizhong, a native of Qingjiang, as his wife, and they were scheduled to be married on October 12th of the 21st year of the Republic [1932] at the Dabu Restaurant in Yangjiadu, South Market. However, Xia expressed dissatisfaction with this marriage, so even when the wedding day arrived, he continued to work as usual. After being strongly urged by relatives and friends, he reluctantly agreed to the marriage, but he did not consummate it and immediately left, renting a house at No. 6 Hexing Lane, Xinzha Road. Ms. Wang lives with her parents-in-law at No. 181 Yangjiadu, and it has been more than two years since. Although Xia and Ms. Wang are nominally husband and wife, they have never spent a single night together. Now, Hu Chengkang, a current court bailiff from Suzhou in Wu County, lives where Xia currently resides. Hu has a daughter named Genyuan, 19 years old, who is still unmarried. Hu saw that Xia had good character and believed that he had no family, so he promised his daughter to Xia. After their engagement in January of last year, Xia began cohabiting with Hu's daughter, who unexpectedly became pregnant and visibly large. Therefore, they chose July 6th to hold their wedding at the Fuxingguo Restaurant on Guangdong Road. Not long after, she gave birth to a child, who is now four months old. This matter came to the attention of Xia's wife, Ms. Wang, who, together with her father, Wang Zhizhong, seized Xia on Qingdao Road yesterday and handed him over to Chinese Constable No. 1074, who took him to the Xinzha Police Station and transferred him to the Laozha Police Station. After investigation by Chinese Detective Feng Xiushan yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special Court's Criminal Division One. The police lawyer, Ru Bao, explained the case, and he was charged with bigamy under Article 254 of the Criminal Law. Subsequently, Ms. Xia Wang, Wang Zhizhong, and Ms. Xia Hu submitted petitions outlining the circumstances. When questioned, the defendant denied marrying Ms. Xia Wang, stating that although he was present on that day, he did not bow to Heaven and Earth. He also claimed that his marriage to Ms. Hu was arranged by his father. Judge Qian Hongye then ordered them to attempt an out-of-court settlement but adjourned the hearing for a later date. The defendant was released on his own recognizance.

The Shengxin Lotus Society Continues Giving Lectures on Scripture

The Shengxin Lotus Society at No. 6 Cihui Lane, Ximolu, near the end of Weihaiwei Road in this city, has been inviting the elderly lay Buddhist Jiang Weinong to lecture on the Diamond Sutra every Tuesday and Friday evening from 7:30 PM to 9:30 PM. He has done so more than twenty times. Listeners from all directions have come together in droves, showing great enthusiasm. Previously, Mr. Jiang had to temporarily suspend the lectures due to health issues. Two months have passed since then. Recently, Mr. Jiang's health has improved slightly, and he will resume the lectures from the seventh section of the scripture starting on January 4th. It is believed that the audience, like a long drought hoping for clouds, will be overjoyed upon hearing this news and will participate with hearts eager to listen to the Dharma rain. In addition, the society has recently printed and distributed corrected editions of the Diamond Sutra in Song-style typeface. This edition has been carefully corrected by Mr. Jiang based on Tang Dynasty handwritten scriptures found in the Dunhuang Grottoes and various ancient versions. Therefore, requests have poured in from various provinces. It is said that only a few copies remain. Those who regularly read and wish to request a copy should attach postage of two and a half cents for out-of-town addresses and one cent for local addresses, and it will be sent immediately.

Jisheng Association Reports on Emergency Relief Efforts in Haining

The China Jisheng Association, considering Haining in Zhejiang to be the area most severely affected by the drought, joined forces with the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, the Haining Drought Relief Association, and the Jiasu All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association. They publicly appointed Mr. Li Yunmen as the director and dispatched more than ten relief workers to investigate and provide emergency relief. This has been documented in this newspaper. An investigation found that there were 10,405 disaster-stricken households in two districts of Haining, with 26,734 adults and 18,137 children. Relief efforts included 2,613.1 *shi* of rice and 1,700 sets of clothing (and 180 sets of smaller clothing). In the third district, there were 8,558 disaster-stricken households, with 19,606 adults and 10,114 children. Relief efforts included 25,486 yuan and 1,400 sets of clothing. In the fifth district, there were 12,137 disaster-stricken households, with 29,714 adults and 18,648 children. Relief efforts included 36,258 yuan and 1,700 sets of clothing. In total, there were 31,200 disaster-stricken households, with 76,054 adults and 46,942 children. Relief efforts included 61,744 yuan, 2,613.1 *shi* of rice, 4,400 sets of new cotton clothing, 400 sets of old cotton clothing, and 180 sets of smaller new cotton clothing. In addition, the Shanghai Jiasu All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association entrusted the association with adding relief to the 2nd, 3rd, and 5th districts, adding 1,000 yuan to each district, benefiting 2,000 households in total, with 5,086 adults and 2,798 children, totaling 3,000 silver dollars. Director Li Yunmen reported this to the association. With the relief work in Haining completed, they will proceed to handle emergency relief in Haiyan. Director Li and the relief workers set off immediately. How can we obtain millions of taels of gold, build ten thousand rooms [to house people], and have ten thousand patient and hardworking comrades to rescue all the helpless disaster victims in the world?

The World Book Company Expands Its Storefront

Business as Usual from January 4th

The World Book Company has two main locations in this city. The main factory for production and manufacturing is located at No. 130 Dalian Road, while the main distribution center for sales and distribution of goods is located in the four-story building at No. 390 Fuzhou Road. According to the person in charge of the company, the World Book Company has been publishing one new book per day for the past three years, and the momentum continues unabated. With more and more new books being published and the retail business booming, the original four-story, five-bay building is no longer sufficient. Especially during the school season, customers are like clouds, with no room to stand. Therefore, it has been decided to expand the space to meet actual needs. The two original city-facing buildings on the west side have been taken back for self-use and converted into a seven-bay storefront. The blueprints have been finalized, and construction will begin during the three-day New Year's holiday of the 24th year of the Republic [1935]. At the same time, the scope of the original educational supplies and printing departments will also be greatly expanded to achieve perfection. It is said that the renovation project is already in active production and is scheduled to be completed late on the night of January 3rd. Business will resume as usual from the 4th.

Southeast Daily Compiles the Southeast Grand View

Collecting and Preserving Southeast Political and Educational Development

Hangzhou's *Minguo Daily* has always been a major newspaper in the Southeast. Since its reorganization on June 15th of this year, when it changed its name to *Southeast Daily*, increased its size to four large sheets, and innovated its layout and enriched its content, it has been welcomed by readers nationwide. Its circulation has surged to over 40,000 copies in a short period. Next New Year's Day will be the first New Year's Day after the newspaper's reorganization. To reward the support of hundreds of thousands of readers, the newspaper has specially compiled a New Year's special issue called *Southeast Grand View*. This book is large format, with a total of 180 pages, two-thirds of which are text and one-third of which are pictures. The pictures are printed on high quality paper using photogravure. The cover is printed in three colors. The entire book is rich in content, collecting and preserving various aspects of politics, construction, education, mountains, rivers, and cultural relics of the Southeast provinces and cities. It has already been published and will be distributed to subscribers along with the newspaper on New Year's Day without additional charge. Among domestic newspapers, it is the first time that such a valuable large-format book has been given away to readers. Furthermore, the provinces and cities of the Southeast are the most politically advanced in China. The authors of this book are mostly officials from the Southeast provinces and cities, and what they describe is the most important and outstanding part of their political work. Therefore, this book is not only a grand exhibition of the Southeast's political achievements but also the most excellent section of China's political exhibition. Reading this book will not only provide a thorough understanding of the Southeast Party's political construction but also an essential and insightful understanding of modern Chinese politics as a whole. It is said that the newspaper is now printing hundreds of additional copies of the book for distribution at a low price. Sending one silver dollar and postage to the Distribution Department of the newspaper on Kaiyuan Road in Hangzhou will obtain a copy of the book.

China Bank Inspection Report

82nd Time

The 82nd inspection report of the Shanghai China Bank's Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee states: In accordance with the regulations, this committee inspected the special vault for the issuance of banknotes and the withdrawal of exchange coupons by the Shanghai China Bank headquarters and its affiliated banks on December 30th, 23rd year of the Republic [1934]. The inspection was conducted by Xu Kan, Director of the Monetary Department of the Ministry of Finance, Wang Yansong and Pei Yunqing, representatives of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Zhai Jigang and Hu Xinan, representatives of the Shanghai Banking Association, Wang Huaikang and Qian Yuansheng, representatives of the Shanghai Money Exchange Association, Yu Zuoting and Xia Xialing, representatives of the coupon-receiving banks and firms, Ye Zhuotang, Song Hanzhang, and Zhou Zongliang, representatives of the bank's directors and supervisors, and accountant Wang Zokang. This was the 82nd inspection, and the results are listed below: The total amount of exchange coupons issued was 136,686,853 yuan, including 92,681,417 yuan issued by the headquarters, 28,400,218 yuan withdrawn by affiliated banks, and 15,784,995 yuan withdrawn by various banks and firms. Excluding the portion withdrawn by various banks and firms, which will be inspected separately according to the original reporting method, this inspection covers the portion withdrawn by the headquarters and affiliated banks, as follows: The amount issued by the headquarters and withdrawn by affiliated banks was 121,083,535 yuan. The reserve amount for exchange coupons held by the headquarters and affiliated banks was 121,083,535 yuan, including 72,939,119.87 yuan in cash reserves and 48,144,415.13 yuan in guarantee reserves. The above two items, with the cash reserves accounting for 60% and the guarantee reserves accounting for 40%, were all checked and found to be accurate. In accordance with Article 5 of the regulations, this is a formal report. December 30th, 23rd year of the Republic [1934].

*3S Geometry Detailed Explanation* Will Be Published Soon

The book *3S Geometry* written by the American authors Schultze, Sevenoak, and Schwatt is very popular because of its exquisite content. Many bookstores have translated the original book into Chinese for use as a textbook, such as *3S* by Zhonghua, *Sisaisi* by Nanjing, and *Plane Geometry* by Beiping Culture. Now, Zhang Zhaoyun, a mathematics teacher at Jingye Middle School, has created a detailed explanation of all 1,500+ exercises in the book to facilitate teacher reference and self-study by students. The content and organization are based on sections, so it can be used with various books. The solution methods are new and detailed, with over 1,000 illustrations. It is currently being bound and will be issued in early January. Sample pages can be requested from Shanghai Jingye Middle School and (Piai) Xueyi Society.
