Education News

Ministry of Education Orders the Issuance of Lists of Textbooks for Selection by Primary and Secondary Schools

(Nanjing, 31st Dispatch) The Ministry of Education has ordered each provincial and municipal education bureau, stating: "The methods for primary and secondary schools in each province and city to select textbooks for each subject have already been instructed in previous orders this year. Now, in order to enable each school to better understand which textbooks published by various publishers have been approved, which ones can still be used in the third year of junior high school, and which ones are outdated, we have specially formulated the following lists: one, a list of textbooks for junior high schools; one, a list of textbooks for primary schools; one, an appendix; and two, a total of four lists, each printed in three copies. We order that your bureau investigate and instruct all affiliated primary and secondary schools to no longer adopt textbooks at will but to select and use the books listed in Lists One and Two. If the lists do not include a textbook for a certain subject, teachers may edit and use teaching materials according to the official curriculum standards for each subject, but must still submit all teaching materials to the Ministry for review at the end of each semester. The books listed in the appendix are only allowed to be used in the third year of junior high school. Starting in the 24th year of the Republic [1935], they must be scrapped by the Ministry and may not be used again. This order must be followed."

Ministry of Education's Chief Secretary Lei Will Come to Shanghai Soon to Continue Searching for a Venue for the London Pre-Exhibition

Lei Zhen, the acting director-general and honorary director of the Arts Committee for the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art, recently came to Shanghai to meet with Pan Gongzhan, the honorary director in Shanghai, to find a venue for the pre-exhibition and a resident office in Shanghai. Although several places were looked at, none were suitable. Mr. Lei returned first due to his busy schedule at the Ministry of Education. Mr. Yang remained in Shanghai to handle everything. It is reported that Mr. Lei will come to Shanghai again on January 12th to continue searching for a venue and office with Mr. Yang and Mr. Pan.

Representatives of the Anhui Education Consolidation Conference Petitioned in Nanjing Yesterday

(Nanjing, 31st Dispatch) The Anhui Local Education Consolidation Conference sent representatives Huang Daolin and five others to Nanjing to petition the authorities. They said that the local education funds in Anhui Province were affected by the drought this year, and the total revenue was only 1.2 million yuan. After the government abolishes excessive taxes and surcharges on farmland, the provincial authorities will abolish them in phases. The first phase, which has already been abolished, was 250,000 yuan related to education revenue. The second phase will be implemented soon and will require another 250,000 yuan to be abolished. This means that education funding will be greatly reduced and difficult to maintain in the future, and the future will be on the verge of bankruptcy. This trip to Nanjing is to petition the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Finance and Education. The two main points of the request are: 1. Before a proper replacement method is developed for the abolition of excessive taxes and surcharges related to educational surtaxes, please allow Anhui to continue to collect one tenth of the taxes on tobacco and alcohol and allow educational surcharges to continue to be collected.

Ministry of Education Compiles a Summary of Higher Education Nationwide

The Ministry of Education recently compiled a summary of the state of higher education nationwide in the 21st year of the Republic [1932]. It is summarized as follows:

Number of Schools

28 vocational schools (3 national, 5 provincial, 12 provincial and private, 8 private); 35 independent colleges (5 national, 11 provincial, 19 private); 41 universities (13 national, 9 provincial, 19 private). A total of 104 institutions of higher education nationwide. By province and city: Shanghai 24, Beiping 14, Guangdong 7, Hebei 8, Hubei 6, Shanxi 6, Jiangsu 5, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Beijing 4 each, Jiangxi, Henan, and Shandong 3 each, Hunan and Liaoning 2 each, Guangxi, Yunnan, Anhui, Sichuan, Xinjiang, Gansu, Jilin, Chahar, Shaanxi, and Rehe 1 each.

Financial Aspects

Annual expenditure: Universities totaled 22,682,910 yuan (National universities: 13,002,747 yuan, with National Sun Yat-sen University having the most at 2,036,608 yuan, followed by National Central University, Peking University, and Tsinghua University, each over 1 million yuan, the rest all under 1 million yuan, with Sichuan University the least at 317,000 yuan; Provincial universities: 2,400,244 yuan, with Guangxi University, Henan University, and Donglu University each over 400,000 yuan, and Northeast Jiaotong University only 39,000 yuan; Private universities: 7,279,919 yuan, with Yenching University the most at 1,025,000 yuan, the rest ranging from 780,000 to 160,000 yuan, with Datong University the least at 91,000 yuan). Independent colleges totaled 8,633,342 yuan (National colleges: 965,016 yuan, with Beiyang Institute of Technology at 320,000 yuan, Shanghai Medical College at 210,000 yuan, and the School of Industry and the School of Commerce each over 100,000 yuan, and Guangdong School of Law at 85,000 yuan; Provincial colleges: 1,185,304 yuan, with Hebei Institute of Technology having the most at 207,306 yuan, and Gansu College the least at 45,278 yuan; Private colleges: 6,553,022 yuan, with Peking Union Medical College having the most at 3,995,826 yuan, followed by Fukien Christian University at 400,000 yuan, Soochow University at 210,000 yuan, twelve colleges ranging from 100,000 to 180,000 yuan, and China National College the least at 36,000 yuan). Vocational schools totaled 1,887,569 yuan (National vocational schools: 183,442 yuan, with Hangzhou Art School at 120,000 yuan and the National Music College at 62,000 yuan; Ministry-administered vocational schools: 430,675 yuan, with Peking Tax School at 170,154 yuan, Wusong Merchant Marine School at 130,314 yuan, and Shanghai Veterinary School the least at 8,900 yuan; Provincial vocational schools: 823,017 yuan, with Shanxi and Guangdong Industrial Vocational Schools each over 100,000 yuan, the rest ranging from 20,000 to 90,000 yuan; Private vocational schools: 450,435 yuan, with Wuchang Art School at 46,820 yuan, the rest ranging from 19,000 to 96,000 yuan). The total expenditure for all the above was 33,320,3321 yuan (Teachers' salaries: 11,144,339 yuan; Staff salaries: 3,632,653 yuan; Workers' wages: 1,705,752 yuan; Equipment costs: 6,216,559 yuan; Office expenses: 3,259,999 yuan; Special expenses: 2,407,412 yuan; Expenses for affiliated institutions: 2,137,437 yuan, totaling the above figures).

Number of Teaching and Administrative Staff

Universities had a total of 6,768 staff members, including 4,402 teachers, 2,934 administrative staff, and 586 individuals holding dual positions (National universities: 3,647 staff; Provincial universities: 916 staff; Private universities: 2,205 staff). Independent colleges had a total of 2,312 staff members, including 1,554 teachers, 953 administrative staff, and 195 individuals holding dual positions (National colleges: 261 staff; Provincial colleges: 615 staff; Private colleges: 1,436 staff). Vocational schools had a total of 1,174 staff members, including 735 teachers, 572 administrative staff, and 133 individuals holding dual positions (National vocational schools: 84 staff; Ministry-administered vocational schools: 189 staff; Provincial vocational schools: 572 staff; Private vocational schools: 329 staff). Considering individual schools, Peking University had the most teaching and administrative staff with 846, followed by Central University with 465, and Peking University with 344. Nine other universities had over 200 staff, sixteen had over 100 staff, and thirteen had fewer than 100 staff. Among independent colleges, China College, Minguo College, Peking Union Medical College, Chaoyang University, and Jiangsu Education College each had over 100 teaching and administrative staff, while the rest had fewer than 100, ranging from 19 to 95 staff. Among vocational schools, Guangdong Industrial School had 93 staff, Shanghai Veterinary School had 10 staff, and the rest ranged from 18 to 71 staff. The total number of teaching and administrative staff across all institutions was 10,254. (To be continued)

Thirteen Months of Teacher Salary Arrears in Changshu: The Plight of the Educational Sector

Unclear amount owed, difficult to settle temporarily

Teachers' lives insecure, waves of unrest arise

(Changshu Correspondence) Educational funding in this county has been in arrears for up to thirteen months. The teachers' salaries for this academic year have only been paid up to September. Elementary school teachers, due to financial difficulties, have sparked three waves of salary demands. The educational authorities, besides running to major banks and borrowing here and there to barely cope with the immediate situation, regard the salary issue as a major crisis. Furthermore, due to the many internal factions within the educational sector in this county, the fact of salary arrears is used as the sole target of attack. If the educational authorities do not have a unified method for clearing the salary arrears, especially with the end of the year approaching and the time for summarizing accounts quickly arriving, the disputes over the future of the educational sector are far from over. The situation of salary arrears is investigated as follows:

Situation of Arrears

The educational funding in this county has been in arrears for thirteen months in total, both past and present. How much is owed in total? Most teachers and principals are very unclear. Even the responsible educational authorities cannot provide a definite figure. Some say that the arrears over the years amount to 750,000 yuan, but this figure is based on the budget estimates over the years. The revenue from land taxes is calculated based on the nominal amount, and the actual amount is not verified and deducted based on the autumn harvest, which does not match the actual revenue. According to general estimates from the educational sector, with monthly teacher salaries ranging from 10,000 to 20,000 yuan, the arrears over the years should be around 200,000 yuan. However, these arrears date back to 1922, spanning twelve years. Some schools have cleared their arrears due to changes in management, while others have not yet cleared them. Some have borrowed half or a small portion of the amount. The situation is complex. Whether these arrears are due to uncollected land taxes, misappropriation, or other reasons, the educational authorities are even more unclear. This is truly an unprecedented muddled account.

Teachers' Livelihood

As for the treatment of elementary school teachers, salaries have traditionally been based solely on qualifications, divided into three levels, leading to significant abuses and unfair treatment. Last year, after a special inspection, the three levels were used as base salaries, and increases or decreases were given based on performance. Senior elementary school teachers' salaries ranged from 22 to 30 yuan, specialized teachers ranged from 18 to 26 yuan, and junior elementary school teachers ranged from 18 to 26 yuan. Part-time teachers ranged from 12 to 20 yuan, all divided into three levels, with each level differing by two yuan. Usually, teachers in each school receive the base salary, which is already a very small amount. Moreover, only one month's salary was paid in the first half of this year, and nothing has been received from October onwards, since the salaries were paid from July to September of the second half of this year. Consequently, waves of salary demands have been sparked three times. In one instance, the director of the education bureau was surrounded by the crowd and unable to cope, bursting into tears in public at the county government office. In another instance, he escaped the encirclement through the back door of the education bureau. Although he usually runs to major banks to borrow funds, most of the education bureau's loans are extended, and credit has gradually been lost, leading to no results. After this year's drought, it is difficult to see any improvement in the collection of land taxes. Teachers' salaries have also been ordered by the provincial government to be paid at an 80% rate, reducing income and increasing financial difficulties, making the need for funds even more urgent. The educational authorities regard raising funds as the only difficulty. With no solution to the economic problem, the educational cause has come to a standstill. Furthermore, due to the many factions within the educational sector in this county, the educational authorities' measures regarding salaries lack definite solutions, leading them to be used as the target of attack. With the end of the year approaching and the time for settling accounts quickly arriving, if salaries cannot be paid, the disputes over the future of the educational sector are far from over.

Reasons for the Arrears

Since there is no definite amount of salary arrears and there are no solutions, the fundamental question is what are the reasons for the arrears? According to the reporter's extensive investigations, the reasons for the arrears over the years are no more than the following: (1) The budgeted income for educational funding each year is based on the nominal amount of land tax, without actual reduction based on the autumn harvest, which leads to inflated income and actual expenditure, with the expenditure increasing accordingly. In reality, the tax revenue in the last five years has averaged less than 50%, so the income cannot offset the expenditure. For example, this year's budget still includes the nominal amount of 372,274 yuan in revenue, repeating the same mistake. (2) The education bureau has lacked supervision over the financial aspects over the years, leading to the former head of the land tax collection office, Hua Zhaozeng, embezzling over 16,000 yuan through fraud. He later escaped, and has not been apprehended for several years. Currently, this case has been judged by the Wuxi Court, and only 39.26 mu of his land has been transferred to cover the civil part of the judgment. The magnitude of the loss is evident. (3) The education bureau's school properties are scattered in the countryside, a situation that has persisted for a long time without investigation and organization, leading to unclear boundaries. Who is farming the land? What about the old fallow land that has not matured? What about the new fallow land? The authorities have no knowledge of any of this. (4) The budgeted revenue from the slaughter tax is over 7,500 yuan per year. From September 1931 to the present, the contractor Jin Ji has been in arrears for 7,027 yuan, and Zhu Deshan owes 4,575 yuan. The educational authorities have also been lenient and have not pursued these debts. (Correspondent Yu Bingchen's communication to this newspaper)

Dates… Set for January 7th, 8th, and 9th

Examination Venues… Wuben, Jingye, Wanzhu, Shangwen

The Municipal Education Bureau has stipulated that the fourth municipal high school student graduation joint examination will be held on January 7th, 8th, and 9th. Meetings were convened separately the day before yesterday. The secretaries of each group are currently preparing the work, which is quite busy. The deadline for student registration for this graduation joint examination was December 26th. All graduating students of this year and students of the previous two years who failed three subjects and were held back to repeat a year are participating in this joint examination, as well as students of the previous two joint examinations who failed one or two subjects and are participating in this make-up examination, totaling approximately 700 students. The examination venues have also been determined. High school students participating in the joint examination will be at Shangwen Primary School, junior high school students will be at Jingye Middle School, high school students participating in the make-up examination will be at Wanzhu Primary School, and junior high school students will be at Wuben Girls' Middle School.

However, the subcommittee believes that it is permissible to retain the option of inviting external personnel to supervise special experiments. Shanghai Municipal Council Considers Tuition Fees

Should Fee Reductions for Families with Multiple Students Enrolled Be Maintained?

The Education Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council has recently given detailed consideration to the question of whether families with multiple students enrolled in the Shanghai Municipal Council's schools should continue to receive tuition fee reductions as before. According to a report submitted by the head of the Finance Department, the current regulations provide that, except for primary schools, families with two students enrolled receive an 80% fee reduction, those with three students receive a 70% fee reduction, and those with four or more students receive a one-third reduction. The total amount of these fee reductions each year is approximately 62,500 yuan. The Shanghai Municipal Council's principle has always been that educational expenses are largely paid for by tax revenue. Therefore, it seems problematic to give special benefits to a small number of people simply because they have many children. Moreover, those who receive these benefits do not necessarily need them. Furthermore, this practice is not found in Chinese academic circles. In the Shanghai Municipal Council's middle schools, families with one or more students enrolled are generally quite wealthy and do not necessarily have economic difficulties.

For the above reasons, the Finance Department suggests that, starting in the spring semester, the practice of fee reductions in all Chinese children's schools should be abolished. This would increase tuition revenue by approximately 22,000 yuan, which could be used to expand education, such as establishing scholarships, which would be more appropriate.

The situation in foreign children's schools is slightly different. The head of the Finance Department argues that the fee reduction for families with two students should be changed to 90%, for three students to 85%, and for four or more students to 80%. This would increase tuition revenue by 17,000 yuan, which could also be used for scholarships and subsidies.

After discussion, some argued that this practice of fee reductions is not found elsewhere, and it is difficult to determine whether students come from the same family. Therefore, it is not convenient to implement the change immediately. One committee member suggested that the Chinese girls' middle school should continue to follow the old regulations to promote female education, while the Chinese boys' middle school should follow the example of foreign children's schools. Another committee member said that the parents of students in the Shanghai Municipal Council's Chinese schools, especially the parents of female students, are mostly wealthy. Since the Shanghai Municipal Council already bears two-thirds of the educational expenses, the parents should pay the remaining one-third in full. Moreover, the facilities of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Chinese schools are superior compared to those of other schools, while the facilities of the Shanghai Municipal Council's foreign children's schools are inferior compared to those of other schools, but the tuition fees are much higher. As a result of the discussion, the chairman of the committee suggested that the fee reduction system be abolished altogether, and that special cases be given assistance. The head of the Education Department believed that this proposal was feasible, but was concerned that parents would be unwilling to have their financial situation investigated. Moreover, not all parents are wealthy, so abolishing the fee reduction would inevitably cause some pain. He suggested that scholarships could be increased or the number of free places could be expanded. As a result of the committee's discussion, no decision was reached and it will be discussed again at a later date.

The Tenth Anniversary of the National Language Movement Held Today

Celebration Held at Shanghai Radio Station Yesterday

Lu Yi-yan and Others Report on the Association's Work

National Language Construction Year Opening Ceremony to be Held Today

The National Association for the Promotion of National Language Education, in order to expand the anniversary celebration and complete the first ten-year plan, has designated this year as the National Language Movement Construction Year, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. The proceedings of the meeting are recorded below:

Preliminary Celebrations Yesterday

Starting at 5:00 PM yesterday, the association held a celebration at the Shanghai Broadcasting Station. After the ceremony, (1) Lu Yi-yan delivered an opening speech, stating, "In the summer of 1925, Yi-yan and others, aware that the warlord government was about to implement measures to undermine national language education, immediately traveled north and south, united comrades, and first tentatively held a National Language Movement Conference in Taiyuan, Shanxi on August 20th. On September 5th, another National Language Movement Conference was tentatively held in Beijing. On September 18th and 19th, another National Language Movement Conference was tentatively held in Shanghai. The results of the trials were very good. On October 1st, the General Preparatory Office of the National Language Movement Conference was officially established in Shanghai, and it was resolved that the period from January 1st to 31st, 1926, would be the term of the National Language Movement Conference, and the conference proceedings would be printed, detailing papers and methods of the National Language Movement, and distributed to comrades at home and abroad, and prepared the movement in good faith. Since the 1st day of January of the fifteenth year of the Republic, eighty-six places in all parts of the country, as well as various ports in Japan and Nanyang, have successively held large-scale National Language Movement Conferences in their own localities, united the people, and supervised the government to dispel the motives of the national language, therefore, this conference decided that January 1st of each year is the National Language Movement Memorial Day. After the end of the movement conference, the comrades believed that it was necessary to establish a permanent organ, so the National Association for the Promotion of National Language Education was organized, and after several months of preparation, it was officially established in Shanghai on September 1st, 1926. In 1930, in order to facilitate assistance to the government to promote national language education throughout the country, it moved to Nanjing and set up an office in Shanghai. This is the origin of the National Language Movement Conference and the National Association for the Promotion of National Language Education. On the economic side, the association is extremely short of money, and the comrades use their spare time, sacrifice their own blood and sweat, and work hard for nine years. Although there are no great achievements, there are still memorable facts, so today we are holding a small meeting to celebrate, hoping that the comrades will cheer up, continue to struggle, earnestly build, carry forward the spirit of the association, and complete the ten-year plan, so that the national language education can be popularized as soon as possible," and so on. (2) Ms. Ruan Huijuan and others sang the National Language Movement Song. (3) Zu Yuren reported on the publicity work over the years. (4) Members of the Flying Sound Troupe sang new songs. (5) Pei Weisen reported on the achievements of the promotion over the years. (6) Members of the Flying Sound Troupe sang new songs.

Founding of Enterprises

(7) Ma Guoying reported briefly, "The association's enterprises have not been able to be carried out as much as possible due to economic relations. Now, the enterprises that have been run over the years are reported as follows: (1) In 1928, the Shanghai National Language Speech Contest was founded in Shanghai, divided into four groups, A, B, C, and D, for competition. (2) Starting in 1929, the association's Lexicography Committee founded the National Language Dictionary. In 1934, the entire book was completed. (3) In May 1930, the association organized the Phonetic Notation Committee to replace the phonetic notation documents of all sectors. After the method was published, it was entrusted by party and government organs, schools, and organizations one after another. By the end of August 1934, there were 1,485 phonetic notation documents, and 285 phonetic notations were corrected. (4) In August 1931, the association organized the National Language Machine Film Committee to design and produce twelve sets of standard national language phonograph records in installments, each set consisting of four records, totaling forty-eight records. In 1932, it was decided to first produce four records of "Phonetic Symbols". In July of the same year, the Ministry of Education sent personnel to supervise the production and review. On March 7, 1933, the Ministry of Education approved the review. In April of the same year, the Central Party Department, the National Government, and the Ministry of Education issued orders to all levels of party departments, organs, schools, and organizations throughout the country to adopt them uniformly. Also, in August 1932, four records of the "National Language Amusement Fair" were produced, and a textbook of "Phonetic Symbols" National Language Amusement Fair" was published to facilitate listening and learning. (5) In 1932, the National Language Amusement Competition was founded in Shanghai, with one-act plays as the competition amusement, divided into two groups, A and B, for competition. (6) In 1933, the Phonetic Symbol Competition was first founded in Shanghai and then continued in Fuzhou. (7) In 1934, the National Primary School National Language Competition was founded, and the Ministry of Education ordered the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to instruct the students of national, provincial, city, county, and township primary schools throughout the country to participate. The preliminary essays of primary school students from Hebei, Shanxi, Henan, Guangxi, Zhejiang, Hunan, Shaanxi, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Shandong, Hubei, Yunnan, Gansu, Sichuan, Suiyuan, Chahar, Fujian, Nanjing, Shanghai, Peiping, Qingdao, and Hankou Weihaiwei have now been received by the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, and they are being reviewed in groups by the reviewers of the re-election, and it is decided that the review will be completed before the end of February next year, and the reviewers of the final election will review them, and the process will be completed by the end of March, and the list of winners in each group will be announced on April 4. (8) The Shanghai Municipal Council Chinese Staff Club Ping Opera Group Clear Singing,

Discussion and Suggestions

(9) Li Weiyue reported briefly, "From August 16th to 18th, 1931, the National Language Education Discussion Meeting was convened in Shanghai. Representatives from the Shanghai Municipal Party Department, the Mayor of Shanghai, the Ministry of Education, and the education bureaus of Shanghai and Nanjing, as well as the education departments of Fujian, Hubei, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Hebei, Shandong, and Anhui, and member representatives from Guangdong, Guangxi, Sichuan, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Hebei, and Shandong, and seventy-six people, passed sixty-six proposals. The Proposals Organizing Committee organized and compiled the National Language Promotion Plan, the Phonetic Symbol Promotion Plan, the National Language Romanization Plan, the Dialect Symbol Plan, and the administrative proposals, which were classified and submitted to the association for execution. The executive committee of the association shall follow the executive committee to the board of directors, and the board of directors shall weigh the importance and submit it to the competent authorities for suggestions for implementation. (1) On November 27, 1932, the Ministry of Education, the Ministry of the Interior, and the Film Inspection Committee were requested to order all film companies throughout the country to assist in the promotion of the National Language Program, with three attached measures to ensure its effective implementation. On December 24th, a letter was received from the Film Inspection Committee, informing that all Chinese and foreign film companies throughout the country had been notified separately to comply. (2) On February 6, 1933, the Ministry of Education was requested to order all major bookstores throughout the country to assist in the promotion of the National Language Program, with four attached measures, with a deadline for implementation. On March 21st, the Ministry of Education approved and ordered the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to inform all bookstores within their borders to comply with the implementation from August 1st of this year. (3) On January 10, 1934, the Ministry of Education was requested to order the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to pay close attention to the National Language Program in the promotion of social education, with four attached measures to ensure its effective implementation. On January 25th of the same year, the Ministry of Education approved and ordered that they be enforced in accordance with the regulations. There are still cases that have not been executed, and it is planned to find ways to execute them next year and submit them to the competent authorities for adoption and implementation," and so on. (10) The Shanghai Municipal Council Chinese Staff Club Ping Opera Group Clear Singing. (11) Huang Zuyi, Zheng Muming, Zheng Qingchao, Zhuo Tengzhao, and others sang dialect songs of students. (12) Ms. Dong Ying delivered a speech on My Little Porcelain Doll. (13) Ms. Fu Bin sang The Fisherman's Light. (14) Guo Weixin, Li Bangen, and Zhou Fushan performed three kinds of short plays. (15) Zheng Zhuyuan, Zhuo Tengzhao, Huang Qifeng, and others sang the dialect song Stepping on the Moon. (16) Zhou Fushan, Guo Weixin, and Li Bangen performed the short play Misunderstanding. Municipal Stadium Football Charity Match for Disaster Relief

Match Time: 10 AM on the 3rd

The Committee was allowed to hold receipts for donations collected at the Guangdong vs. Langya A team finals of the Ping-Pong Competition last night to allow people to enter the stadium to watch the match. This was done to appeal to the spirit of sports and to help the victims of the widespread disasters. The stadium director, Wang Zhuangfei, believing that the disaster areas were vast and the disaster victims were numerous, and that a drop in the bucket would not solve the problem, consulted with the Shen Xing team players and outstanding talents from this year's Industry and Commerce Football Association, and agreed to hold a disaster relief match at the stadium's football field at 10:30 AM on the 3rd of this month (Thursday). All the players also put the disaster victims first, generously fulfilling their obligations, and stadium instructor Zhang Longhai will serve as the referee. It is reported that the method of entering the stadium to watch the match is as follows: for every donation of two jiao of small money, the stadium will issue a donation receipt for two jiao. Holding this receipt will allow entry to watch the match. (Receipts from watching the Ping-Pong Competition cannot be used again.) The back of the donation receipt will be stamped with the stadium's seal. Donations and receipt stubs collected will be sent to the Shanghai Municipal Disaster Relief Donation Committee to ensure transparency. Southeast Women's Sports School Basketball Team Achieves Four Wins in Four Games in Suzhou

Women's Division Divided into A and B Groups, Totaling 16 Teams

The Shanghai YMCA's basketball league has been held for six years. Starting this year, a women's division has been added, so the number of participating teams is even more enthusiastic, with a total of 85 teams, exceeding the previous record. There are 69 teams in the men's division, divided into business and school groups (41 business teams, 28 school teams), and 16 teams in the women's division (divided into A and B groups). The association's committee decided to start the competition next Tuesday (the 8th). For the convenience of the men's division competition, the groups will still be divided into departments. The business group will be divided into five departments, the school group into three departments, and the women's group into two groups, A and B. Each department will use a single round-robin system. In the future, the championships of the business and school groups will be decided by a competition between the champions of each department. The men's championship team will receive two silver balls from the Tianjin Chunhe Company, and the women's championship team will receive two silver cups from the Shanghai Brown Olive Company. Compares to a Good Start, Up Three Yuan Three Jiao

The gold market yesterday was characterized by mediocre trading due to the end of the Gregorian year. The volume was narrow. Call Loan Market Slightly Loosens, Settlement Procedures Very Cumbersome

Business conditions in all sectors have been poor this year, and the flow of funds has been difficult. Few have completed the final settlement for yesterday's New Year's Eve, and many have postponed it, resulting in even more difficult settlements. However, settlement procedures will inevitably be numerous. Yesterday, the banks on the Bund and the Chinese banks, money shops, and companies settled with each other, and the amounts were very large. The call loan market opened at 5.5 fen in both the morning and afternoon, slightly less than 0.5 fen from the previous day's market price, and the situation remained firm. However, because some banks made loans by adding water to the draft, there was a small decline. It started at 5.5 fen, then 6 fen, and finally decreased from 2.8 fen to 2 fen at the close. In the Small Clearing House, only 1.45 fen was made. Regarding call loan transactions, more than 1.7 million was transferred in the morning market, more than 300,000 in new transactions, more than 800,000 in the afternoon market, and more than 600,000 in the Small Clearing House. All were call loans to be repaid after three days, because New Year's Day and the 2nd were closing days, so there had to be a three-day term, which is different from the usual one-day term. Regarding foreign secured loan transactions, Chinese banks and money shops made more than 5.2 million in new transactions, foreign banks made more than 4 million, the purchase amount was more than 6.8 million, and the recovery and issuance of banknotes was 1.67 million. The sources and destinations were all stopped. Bank settlements: because there were so many settlements at the end of the year, it was impossible to calculate them all at once, but it was estimated that no less than tens of millions were involved. Money shops and foreign public bills also had a lot of settlements, totaling 70 to 80 million. Foreign draft loans also had more than 20 million in settlements. Remittances from various sources were 600 to 700 thousand. There were no accurate statistics on the settlement of cash, but it was generally said that more than 1 million was settled.

High Call Loan Rate Last Month Leads to Higher Deposit Interest Rates

Yesterday, the Money Trade Association held a regular meeting. Regarding the deposit interest rate proposal, it was generally agreed that the foreign call loan rate was very high in December, reaching a maximum of 6 jiao and a minimum of more than 2 jiao. As such, the total daily statistics amounted to 10.24 yuan. Therefore, the deposit interest rate was bound to increase accordingly. As a result, the rate was set at 9.5 yuan and 95 deductions, which is vastly different from the usual 2 yuan and 95 deductions. Retrospective of Standard Yarn and Cotton in the 23rd Year

The yarn market conditions in the 23rd year of the Republic of China were most pessimistic in the spring months of January, February, March, and April, because of the decline of domestic rural areas, the depression of commerce, and the great lack of purchasing power in all directions. The political situation in North China was clouded, and the exchange experienced a reform trend in standard yarn. In addition, there was a shareholders' association to deal with standard issues. The struggle between the two factions was particularly fierce. As a result, on February 28th of this year, the Ren Zhong standard yarn, which had been established for more than ten years, was suddenly removed, and Jinji yarn was changed to the standard. At that time, the yarn market was extremely weak, and people were panicked. The market price fell in a straight line. Although a certain factory owner proposed to maintain the yarn price, he once convened the leaders of Chinese factories to discuss methods. However, the factory owners only cared about their own immediate interests, and not only were unwilling to cooperate, but also undermined each other. Therefore, Japanese merchants took the opportunity to sell in large quantities, and the pressure was even greater. The tragedy of the fall in the price of standard yarn in April was terrifying, like a dam breaking and pouring down thousands of miles, creating an unprecedented new record. The low peak saw 160.03 yuan, which was only equivalent to 114.6 taels of silver under the old rules, which was 6.7 taels lower than the lowest peak of 121.3 taels in the yarn and cloth market since July of the 10th year (formerly 16-count standard, now 20-count standard, and according to the grading table, it should be 5 taels higher). It is said that in this big decline, foreign merchants made a lot of profit. Later, by May and June, the old goods stored at the bottom of the standard cotton gradually decreased. Tongji Cotton Company purchased in large quantities, manipulated and went long, and cotton prices rose. The market situation was implicitly recovering. Unexpectedly, things must be reversed, which is the normal course of events. Low prices have triggered real demand. Because yarn was cheap and cotton was expensive, the factories' difficulties deepened and business became more difficult. They had to adopt the method of reducing work to maintain the factory base. More and more people stopped work and reduced work, and production decreased. The situation in North China turned safe, and the implementation of mail and train services was resolved. As a result, the spot sales market in the north developed. At this time, the price of Chinese coarse yarn was cheaper than that of Japanese yarn. Tianjin banks came to Shanghai to purchase in large quantities, causing the yarn market, which had been tired and depressed for a long time, to gradually turn around. The Jinji standard yarn rose straight from 168.9 yuan to 180 yuan. In mid-July and August, the US suffered a severe drought, and the trend of US cotton was stable. At the same time, our country was also suffering from drought, and reports of cotton production damage were urgent. Flour and miscellaneous grains rose sharply first, and the financial community profited greatly, changed its plans, and entered the standard yarn market to engage in purchases. In addition, a rumor broke out at the Shenxin Factory, and there was a lot of discussion in the market, saying that the factory's production capacity was quite strong. If it were to stop operating, the impact on the market would be significant. For a time, new buyers poured in like a tide. Tianjin banks searched for coarse yarn, and the factories' yarn was sold out. The market situation became tighter and tighter, and there was a scene of enthusiasm. A further rise in the standard yarn price was realized (on August 9, the highest peak for the January standard yarn in the 23rd year was 192 yuan). By mid-September, Tongcheng Company sold short, and domestic cotton fields increased. Because agricultural products were particularly cheap last year, the villagers were happy to plant cotton. The low peak of the standard cotton price was 33.2 jiao. The yarn market, which was closely related, was slightly hit. Unexpectedly, the United States implemented a policy of buying silver, and the price of silver rose sharply. The price of gold became shorter. The rise of silver and the contraction of gold were very unfavorable to the price of goods in our country. The Shanghai money market became increasingly tight, and the East Exchange soared to 130 yuan. Japanese merchants used their 8-jiao exchange rate to sell as much as possible in the standard yarn market. The actual sales of customers turned stagnant due to the high price, and the pressure from the sellers was even greater. The market price fell faster and faster. On October 6, the lowest peak for the October standard yarn was 168.5 yuan. In mid-October, November, and December, the National Government, in view of the increasing outflow of silver and the apparent panic and anxiety of the Shanghai economy, increased the export tax on silver and added an equalization tax in order to maintain the stability of Shanghai's finance. The price of gold soared, and all prices rose together, causing the depressed yarn market to suddenly experience a violent surge. Tongcheng Company turned from short to long, and the banking community also bought in vigorously. The standard yarn price jumped wildly by 8.5 yuan. The March standard yarn saw 190.05 yuan, and Henan, Zhengzhou, Tianjin, and other places were buying 17-count yarn very actively. The demand in the South, Guangdong, Yunnan, Guizhou, and Fujian was active, so that the stored yarn of more than 100,000 bales gradually decreased to about 60,000 bales. Therefore, the intentions of many parties became more and more intense. In November, Tongcheng Company alone received more than 10,000 bales of standard yarn. Rumors of paper money in the business community rose repeatedly, and the theory of currency inflation was revived. The pull of the long companies became stronger and stronger. In December, Tongcheng Company received only 1,600 bales of goods, but the final price rose wildly by more than 2 yuan to 187 yuan, creating the highest peak for the end of each month this year. It is found that the amount of buyers Tongcheng Company and Tongji Company is about 50,000 bales, and Tongcheng Company has continuously received more than 10,000 bales of spot yarn. The sellers are a Japanese factory and a certain foreign firm with 30,000 bales, and other manufacturers have about 20,000 to 30,000 bales of hedged positions. The positions of both the long and short sides are strong. The highest and lowest prices, delivery prices, delivery numbers, and total transaction numbers for the standard yarn in one year are listed in the table below for reference.

Grain: New Year's Day Has Arrived, Rice Market Closed for Two Days

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources from various banks were particularly scarce, only a total of fifteen or sixteen (goods totaling more than 3,000 shi). And because the market is closed for two days for the New Year's Day, each store added a little inventory. The market prices of each thick japonica rice and late rice saw a return to stability. Du Yang tip is also stable because it follows each other. Only the arrival of Yin Yuan goods is slightly more, and it is still tired. However, Bian Yuan is also not much different.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, the He Xia banks reached ship number 26 and 27. Because it was the end of the Gregorian calendar year, few buyers went to market. The buyers had no intention of selling, so the outflow of goods of various colors was flat. The market price of white japonica rice and various Bian Yin Yuan early rice and other goods did not fluctuate much.

Sesame: Foreign Firm Opens at 9.8 Yuan

Sparse Transactions in Miscellaneous Grains at the End of the Year

Yesterday's miscellaneous grain market was sparse because it was the end of the year and the market was closed for two days next year (on the 1st and 2nd). Only the Dade Xin Oil Factory bought 2,000 bags of Guide beans for 3.615 yuan, which was 0.035 yuan lower than the price of the previous week. Hankou Zha beans were sold for 300 bags on this street, priced at 3.4 yuan and 0.28 yuan. The future of the bean market depends on the trend after the market opens because Anhui's exemption from donations is brewing. On the previous day (Sunday), Sassoon Foreign Firm purchased 300 tons of sesame for 9.8 yuan, which was still quite brisk. Currently, the goods owners are quoting 10 yuan. In the afternoon, it was heard that Jardine Matheson had sent a telegram, and it may be possible to close a deal at this price, and the transaction volume will inevitably be considerable. Spot goods were purchased by a Japanese bank for 212 bags of Bengbu sesame for 6.6 yuan. 60 bags of Jiujiang milk sesame were priced at 6.77 yuan, and the market price also rose by 0.04 to 0.05 yuan.

Canadian Wheat Stockpiles

The Chicago grain market is slack, and Canadian wheat is stockpiled. Argentine, Australian, and French grains are shipped and sold everywhere, and current prices are difficult to raise. Today's market is supported by the lack of snow in the producing areas and the severe cold weather in the southwest.

Tinplate Costly and Difficult to Sell Cheaply

The tinplate market is costly and difficult to sell cheaply. Because the fixed price has soared and the foreign exchange is expensive, the cost has increased. Due to capital relationship, the industry colleagues refuse to sell cheaply, and in the tight credit period of the year, it is not easy to extend credit, so they are unwilling to sell. Most of them are prepared to sell again next spring, so there are very few shipments. The market conditions of various colors are recorded as follows:

British Goods: Out of stock for a long time, the market is quite lonely. Although the industry colleagues still have purchases for forward orders, distant water cannot quench the immediate thirst, so there is still no news to report in Shanghai.

American Goods: The transaction of the egg factory bank is not very developed, so the outlet has been sharply reduced. Although printing plants have some embellishments, the number is very small. Therefore, in terms of market conditions, it can still stand without falling, such as 90-pound single-layer estimated at 16.5 yuan, double-layer at 32.75 yuan, 100-pound single-layer at 17.25 yuan, and double-layer at 35 yuan. It is heard that there are only dozens of boxes of trading in recent days, and large transactions are still unheard of. However, the cost of new goods is very high, so the industry colleagues are unwilling to sell cheaply.

Italian Goods: The only thing popular in this market is double-layer, estimated at 31 yuan, and the relief market price is 31.5 yuan. The transactions of can factories and iron printing plants are particularly good, and the toy companies also have wide production transactions. In addition, customers only ask about the prices. German Goods: The transaction is quite good, and the goods that arrive are not widely available, so the holders have the intention of hoarding. The price is like 90 pounds single-layer estimated at 16 yuan, 100 pounds at 16.5 yuan, double-layer 100 pounds estimated at 33 yuan, 90 pounds estimated at 31.5 yuan. It is heard that only a few have been released in recent days.

French Goods: The transaction of the goods is quite good, but the nature is hard, so it is not suitable for exquisite printing and canning. Therefore, the transaction is only limited to rough and low-end goods. The current market price is 15.5 yuan (90 pounds) and 16 yuan (100 pounds). There are no double-layer goods, so there is no market to report.

Spring and Autumn New Year Special Edition

New Year's Writing Attempt

— Zhou Shoujuan

Oh dear, another year! Today, they say, is New Year's Day, and it is appropriate to offer congratulations, which is called "New Year greetings." However, while people offer New Year greetings, I want to mourn the year!

Someone might say: The new year brings a new age, and all things are renewed. We should offer congratulations. Why mourn? Isn't that too unromantic?

I say: There is nothing to congratulate, but there is much to mourn. For me personally, my age increases year by year, and my vigor decreases year by year. Daily affairs become more complicated, burdens become heavier, opportunities become fewer, and death draws nearer. Moreover, things rarely go as I wish, and I have few people to confide in. I endure countless grievances alone. In such an environment, spending such years, even if the new year arrives, what is there to congratulate? I only feel it is something to mourn. As for society, disasters spread year by year, the people's livelihood declines year by year, thieves and robbers run rampant year by year, and order becomes more chaotic year by year. Moreover, the world is rugged, and people's hearts are treacherous. New morality has not yet been established, and old morality has long gone bankrupt. Although we loudly advocate reforming society, society remains unreformed. Even if the new year arrives, what is there to congratulate? I only feel it is something to mourn. As for the country, the national territory shrinks year by year, the national treasury becomes empty year by year, domestic affairs remain unreformed year by year, foreign affairs are handled inadequately year by year, and the country's international status declines year by year. In such a country, in such a world, even if the new year arrives, what is there to congratulate? I only feel it is something to mourn.

Alas! Wang Xiaoer's New Year gets worse year by year. Even if I force myself to smile and join in the New Year greetings, what meaning is there? Moreover, the Second World War is about to break out. In the great disaster to come, I don't know what will happen. The arrival of this twenty-fourth New Year is like the Buddha making a great lion's roar, warning us in the darkness, saying: "This is the eve of great world turmoil. An ancient country with thousands of years of history may collapse at any time, and striving for strength and prosperity is now or never. Are you prepared?"

Are you prepared? No one can offer an answer. Drawing my sword and striking the ground, the ground remains silent. Scratching my head and asking the sky, the sky is also silent.

Little Predictions for the 24th Year

— Fang'an

Time flies swiftly, and the year ends. Let the old debts be carried away by the east wind! Some predictions, I hope, will come true. A New Year's writing attempt, just to replace the red couplets.

The winter is not severely cold, and the rain and snow are well-distributed. No one will freeze to death on the roads, covering the vermillion gates with the stench of wine and meat to be given to the disaster victims. The river ice will freeze solid, and the rice borers' eggs in the fields will be frozen to death. In the spring and summer, the silkworm silk harvest will be bountiful, and the price will be surprisingly high. Hangzhou silk, Beijing satin, and Huzhou crepe will suddenly increase from several dimes per foot to more than three yuan. Farmers will benefit a little. In July, the epidemic will not spread, and the owner of the Drinking Ice Studio will make a fortune. In the autumn harvest, many double ears of grain will grow in the fields, and the farmers will smile so much that their eyes narrow.

The Fifth National Congress of Representatives will open in the capital, with unity from all sides in sincerity. Important figures will issue a declaration of unity, which will be selected as a textbook for all schools, immortal for thousands of years.

A reporter will win the first prize in the aviation ticket lottery and build tens of millions of houses to shelter the world's scholars.

The Tianzhu incense market will become even more lively. Dozens of scenic spots in various provinces will be discovered, greatly broadening the horizons of tourists. Someone exploring the Zilai Cave on the lake will discover that it can reach Huizhou, providing a shortcut to Anhui.

During the typhoon season, the thirty-three-story building in Shanghai will be unharmed.

The people of the country will revel in both the government and the public, spending the New Year of 1936 peacefully and securely.

New Year's Musings

— Zheng Yimei

New Year's Day is the beginning of a year. Even amidst national hatred, family disasters, wind, and rain, people must still force a smile and celebrate with joy, doing everything possible to decorate and embellish. This is because everyone has hope and deeply desires that everything starts smoothly. However, hope is the same every year, and the results are always the same, merely showing the foolishness of dreams.

In Western customs, turkey is eaten on New Year's Day. The turkey is named for its brilliant brocade-like colors and is also called fire chicken. Westerners consulting a chef must ask if they know how to cook turkey, as it is considered the standard for judging skill.

Japanese women style their hair on New Year's Day, calling it the "first hair." Seru has a poem about it, saying: "Thousands of heavenly maidens compete in gorgeous hair, the palm of the hand holds a new cloud with a moon halo, and she is busy by the mirror, annoyed that the maiden is busy combing her hair." Also, dreams between New Year's Day and the second day are called "first dreams." On the night of the first dream, people buy a picture of the Seven Lucky Gods' Treasure Ship to place under their pillow, praying for a lucky dream. Seru also has a poem about it, saying: "Red rouge dampens the Treasure Ship picture, seven divine sails, a watercolor charm, waking up and smoothing my hair, I smile first, and ask my love if he saw me in his first dream."

Painting Zhong Kui is a Dragon Boat Festival story, but originally it was done on New Year's Day. The "Idle Glimpses of Duncai" says: "Today, people paint Zhong Kui at the beginning of the year to ward off evil spirits, a custom said to have started during the reign of Emperor Ming of Tang." "Seven Repair Class Drafts" also records that Shen Mingde's New Year's Day poem says: "The newly mounted Zhong Kui is hung first, the bright red spring couplets are gilded." Taoist books also call New Year's Day the "Central Heaven Festival," which is the same as the Dragon Boat Festival.

Drinking Tusu wine on New Year's Day is an old custom, and traditionally the youngest should drink first, hence Gu Kuang's poem: "Holding the Tusu, let the young ones drink first." In fact, Tusu is the name of a plant. Painting this plant on the house is how the house got its name. In the past, people lived in Tusu houses to brew wine, so it was called Tusu wine, said to ward off improper influences. According to elders, when the Manchus entered the Pass and engaged in wanton slaughter, people in Suzhou, having seen the horrors of Yangzhou and Jiading, mutually agreed to abolish the custom of drinking Tusu wine on New Year's Day, as the character "屠" (tu, slaughter) was considered unlucky, fearing it would bring disaster to the living. It is also pitiable.

Do Not Lightly Let New Year's Day Pass

— Zhou Xian

Today is New Year's Day of the 24th year of the Republic of China. The plan for the year lies in the spring. The start of the year's great undertakings should naturally begin on New Year's Day, so we should not lightly let New Year's Day pass.

In the past year, our China has been mired in a whole year of natural disasters of floods and droughts, man-made disasters of banditry and unrest, the attacks of foreign powers by aircraft and warships, and the severe oppression of economic aggression. It has been almost impossible to breathe freely. But this unfortunate 23rd year has passed with the passage of time. The bright New Year's Day of the 24th year has broken through the long night and descended upon us. Naturally, what we hope for is that the light and good fortune of the 24th year will also, along with New Year's Day, break through the terrible atmosphere of the 23rd year and descend upon us.

But light and good fortune require people to strive to pursue them. Light and good fortune will not descend naturally like New Year's Day. This point must be clearly understood. The reason why the 23rd year fell into such a dense and terrible atmosphere was not as natural as the decline of the 23rd year. The reason was the mistake in direction. Lying before us, no matter what it is, there are always two roads: one is successful, and the other is a failure. The 23rd year mistakenly embarked on the path of failure. But which path should we take this year?

Today is New Year's Day. Today is the beginning of this year's great undertakings. On this day, we naturally hope that this year will be full of light and full of good fortune. Light and good fortune are spread all over the path of success that lies before us. We only need to be able to clearly recognize our direction at the beginning of this year's great undertakings, to clearly recognize our first step, and to decide which path to take. Should we follow the direction of last year and continue down the path of failure, or should we change direction and take the path to success?

Today is New Year's Day of the 20th year of the Republic of China, how important it is that we do not let it lightly slip away!

Wang Xiaoer's Confession

— Liang

"Crack," here, "crack," there, the women are dressed in bright red and green, attracting attention. The men are also dressed up very nicely, with a smiling expression on their faces. Cars and rickshaws, squeezing out ear-piercing horns, honking, the streets are really more lively than usual, it's the New Year. A group of children madly dart out of the alley, "Whirr, whirr..." Who knows what they're shouting? "Crack, crack," throwing firecrackers.

Wang Xiaoer has no such interest, with such an ashen face, less than half an inch of cigarette butt still stuck to his purple lip, carrying a bit of knife-cut meat in his hand, "It's the New Year," he thought in his heart, look at the happy feasts of others, but alas, I am always struggling in poverty, with no comfortable days to live, "Is there really fate and destiny?" He often asked himself angrily. He walked along the curb, so slowly, like a snail crawling, but suddenly "Crack," a firecracker exploded on his head, and he was startled. Turning his head, "Hahaha..." A group of children darted into the alley.

"Damn it, even the kids want to bully Wang Xiaoer, people just can't be poor." He cursed a few times, but no one sympathized with him, and others "hahaha" ran away laughing. He thought, "Dogs look down on people," and in a fit of anger, even his eyes blurred. He stumbled home, squeezed through the broken gate, ignored everyone, and collapsed on the bed.

Then he thought and thought: "What is fate? What is destiny? It's all useless talk. Didn't I, Wang Xiaoer, live a good life before? A big family, but the brothers insisted on dividing the family, not harmonious, fighting and grabbing. It benefited outsiders and neighbors, stealing and grabbing, and at that time they only knew to fight among themselves, and didn't care when others came to rob them. Lawsuits, one year, two years... dragging on, all the property is gone, and what's the point of saying 'fighting for honor, not wealth,' brothers... Thinking about it, it hurts..." Wang Xiaoer shed tears, he regretted the mistakes of the past, and resolved to reconcile with his brothers again, and start working together.

On this New Year's night, Wang Xiaoer's wife cooked a big bowl of knife-cut meat, and two pieces of salted fish. Wang Xiaoer bought a pound of white liquor, and drank and ate with his eldest brother, little third, and little fourth. They all threw away their old grudges and spoke from the heart. When they were happy, they "burst" out laughing.

Last Page of the Calendar...

— Qingqu

Alas! Time truly passes quickly! A year of three hundred and sixty-five days has fleetingly reached its last day; recalling the past time, it is like flowing water that never returns. A predecessor said: "Those that abandon me, yesterday's days cannot be retained; those that disturb my heart, today's days bring much worry." Reciting these old sayings, one cannot help but think about why time rushes people, and how fast it is. A perfectly round Earth constantly revolves around the sun, and no one has ever stopped the north-south axis of the Earth; therefore, the course of human life follows the time of seconds, minutes, and moments, passing by in an instant, almost in the blink of an eye, and another year has reached its last day.

I take a look at the calendar of the 23rd year of the Republic of China. Wasn't it quite thick when it was hanging on the wall at first? Unexpectedly, today I tear off one sheet, and tomorrow I tear off another sheet, and now it's December 31st. In my heart, I think, if this sheet is torn off again, will there be a head below it! Everyone knows that the days of the 23rd year are over. But the last page of this calendar, is it better to tear it off, or to leave it behind? I hesitate quite a bit. Because this sheet, even if torn off, will be replaced by next year's calendar, but "the year is not the year of the past, the day is not the day of last year," how can I not stare straight at the wall, lingering and reluctant to tear it off, stand it up, solemnly choose a vacant place, re-hang it, and write a few words on it: "You calendar of the 23rd year, you gave us time for meaningful activity, but many, regrettably, people are unwilling to cherish it, and constantly waste it, then: it is like a shuttle passing by and being missed. It is not the calendar that is ungrateful to people, but rather people who are ungrateful to the calendar, so I am ashamed of you, how can I harden my heart and tear you off again?"

New Year's Day Celebration in Disaster Areas

— Yiqian

Talking About New Year's Cards

— Chen Tuigan

The giant wheel of time is constantly moving forward, and New Year's Day of the 24th year of the Republic of China has arrived again. Regardless of the drastic changes in the international situation and the increasing poverty of the rural areas in the interior, people who value etiquette in society always congratulate each other during the New Year. Thus, peach-colored and rose-purple New Year's cards are bundled and tied up and stuffed into every household by green-uniformed postmen. Speaking of New Year's cards, several years ago, a certain newspaper supplement published that a Mr. Wu of Wujin collected more than a hundred kinds of New Year's cards and held a public exhibition in the local people's education hall. The colorfulness was quite a spectacle. In recent years, I have seen in a friend's house that some people sent him several New Year's cards with the words "Sincere Unity, Strive to Save the Country" printed on them. To say that he is seeking novelty and uniqueness is a bit of a violation of conscience. Because communication between friends is the effect of emotion, then why not reveal the enthusiasm of Du Fu's concern for the times and the country to friends on New Year's cards?

This year's New Year's cards have not yet been seen in many kinds, but I imagine that there will definitely be more timely New Year's cards discovered, because the characteristics of the Chinese nation have always been able to adapt to the environment.

Is Possible

— Yaguang

Musings on the Pig

— Zhang Mengzhao

Thoughts on the Year of the Pig

As the old saying goes, "When a bird is about to die, its cry is mournful; when a person is about to die, their words are good." The stupid and lowly pig, usually eating its fill and sleeping greedily, with no intention, will also cry mournfully when facing execution!

When I was about fourteen or fifteen years old, one early morning, I carried my schoolbag to school and passed by a pig farm. I saw a butcher with a hideous appearance, holding a gleaming sharp knife, aiming at the white tip of a pig hanging from a beam, going in with the red tip coming out, the sound was tragic! Blood was flowing continuously! At that time, I thought to myself: a big-bellied, leisurely, and lowly animal! It also has a day of doom! But it doesn't feel what the future of China is like? Since the sounds of the cannons of September 18th and January 28th successively started, I realized that the enemy was taking us as piglets! Without any politeness, they are slaughtering us with knife after knife, but the Chinese people are still living in a drunken dream, and even the tragic cries like those of pigs cannot be heard at all!

Time flies quickly! The Chinese Republic, with its hundred holes and thousands of sores, has reached twenty-four years old! New Year's Day meets the Year of the Pig. If you are not a cold-blooded animal, who would not be chilled! Who would not be startled! Meaningless prayers are not as good as everyone rising up and making a self-defense movement for the struggle of national life! Strive for the final preparations! To deal with the imminent disaster! This is what I encourage myself and others with.

New Year's Day of the 24th Year of the Republic of China—Hoping for a Change in National Fortune

— Huang Jiping

"Writing red on New Year's Day, everything goes smoothly!" This old saying is deeply imprinted in the minds of ordinary people, so no matter the old or new society, on New Year's Day, there are always many superstitious people who, when they meet, say a few "auspicious words." We reporters, every New Year's Day, must have a special issue, publishing a few articles celebrating the whole world, wishing the country's fortune to be prosperous and the people's livelihood to be blessed. But a year passes easily, and it is the New Year again. If you compare these words with reality, they are simply deceiving people, and you feel ashamed yourself! So, from now on, on New Year's Day, I dare not speak big words or harbor extravagant hopes.

For pessimists, when they open the first page of the new calendar of the 24th year, they may be frightened and worried, how will the country's fortune change this year? How will the people's livelihood be bitter or happy? In addition, the world situation is dangerous, and a great war is inevitable. Looking forward to the future, there is more bad luck than good luck! For optimists, knowing that disaster is at hand and the end is not far away, but if everyone has this mentality, they will inevitably accomplish nothing. Instead of sitting and sighing, it is better to roll up your sleeves and take action. My majestic China, the fragmented situation in the past twenty-three years, is indeed unbearable to look back on. Is it possible that the country's fortune will be in a slump from now on? No, absolutely not! I believe that after the 24th year, there will be hope for a change in the country's fortune. Look! The leaders of the central government and various provinces all have an enterprising spirit and a spirit of hard work. Leaders from all sides already have a trend of implementing great unity. The sage said, "In the way of the former kings, harmony is the most valuable." If we can truly have a great and thorough understanding and work together in harmony, it will be an omen of a change in the country's fortune. As for the promotion of education, industry, transportation, water conservancy, land reclamation, and the New Life Movement to restore inherent morality in various provinces, they are all being carried forward and amplified. Isn't this clear evidence?

The people of the whole country have suffered enough in the past, and it is useless to be discouraged, it is useless to be angry, and it is even more useless to blame the heavens and hate the earth; from now on, we must recognize the goal, strive to lift ourselves up, solve our own problems, and serve the society and the country. With unity from top to bottom, we will revive China. Ming Confucian Lu Xinwu said: "Life begins in poverty, followed by repentance and striving, then from repentance and striving, one learns diligence and hardship, from diligence and hardship, one knows thrift and frugality, from thrift and frugality, one can accumulate savings, and from savings, one gradually becomes wealthy. After wealth, pride and complacency arise, one becomes accustomed to extravagance, indulges in lewdness and violence, and will inevitably bring about disaster and return to poverty." Now the situation of my Chinese nation is after poverty, we must repent and strive and be diligent, and combine the strength of 450 million people to change the country's fortune!

The "Imperial Incense缥缈录" outer collection from Mr. Xunling, who was specially allowed to wear glasses by the Empress Dowager Cixi, about Empress Longyu and Consort Jin

— Qin Shouou

In the "Introduction to the Original Author" chapter of my translation of 御香縹緲錄, as well as in the middle of the main text, Mr. Xunling's name has been seen several times, and readers should not be very unfamiliar with him! Recently, through the introduction of my old friend Tang Yunfan, I was able to meet him in person and talked a lot with him. Therefore, I learned that he himself was a French-trained engineering student who once worked as the electrical plant supervisor in the Qing Palace and often took photos for Cixi in his spare time. His eyes were nearsighted, and he wore glasses very early. After returning to China, he saw the Empress Dowager for the first time, and the Empress Dowager asked: "Xunling, isn't there something wrong with your eyes?" He replied: "Yes, I am nearsighted"! The Empress Dowager asked again: "Do you wear glasses?" He replied: "Yes"! The Empress Dowager then said: "Then put them on"! In this way, his wearing glasses was considered a special favor! Whenever he had an audience, he no longer took them off; therefore, the passage in Imperial Incense 缥缈录 where Deling describes his glasses is all true!

Mr. Xunling also told me a few anecdotes about Guangxu's wife, Empress Longyu, and his concubine, Consort Jin, which were very interesting. I am writing them on New Year's Day to make readers laugh.

(1) Longyu Suffered from Bad Breath. According to our imagination, an empress should be very beautiful, but Longyu's appearance was actually very ordinary, and she suffered from severe bad breath. Therefore, she had to constantly smoke cigarettes, trying to cover it up a bit. However, she still could not fully be considerate, and often liked to give the cigarette butts she had smoked to the noble ladies, princesses, district princesses, or palace maids who entered and left the palace. Those who received them were not able to refuse, so they had to try their best to endure it, or quickly rinse their mouths, or throw them away as soon as she could not see them.

(2) Consort Jin's Nickname was Gilded Chamber Pot. According to our imagination, the emperor's concubine should be a charming beauty, but Consort Jin was just the opposite, so ugly that it was indescribable. Her figure was both short and fat. People in the palace secretly gave her a nickname, called gilded chamber pot, which can be said to be unkind! However, Guangxu was indeed not bad to her, which was purely because of her blood sister, Consort Zhen. Consort Zhen, it is said, was indeed a very beautiful woman, but unfortunately, she died too early!
