Summary of the Shanghai Municipal Hospital and Hygiene Laboratory Project, whose groundbreaking ceremony is held today

— Dong Da You

I. Introduction

The Shanghai Municipal Hospital is built in the east of the administrative area in the city center, covering an area of about 80 mu, bordering Funan Left Road to the west, Fudong Outer Road to the north, Huabang Road to the east, and Qiujiang River to the south. The Hygiene Laboratory is located to the east of the Municipal Hospital, covering an area of ten mu, at the intersection of Huayuan Road and Fudong Outer Road. The two are located next to each other, and will form the city's medical center, combining medical treatment, research, and education facilities. The arrangement and planning of the buildings also follows the principle of facilitating the connection and unified management of these two parts.

II. Municipal Hospital

(A) Overall Plan The main buildings of the Municipal Hospital are divided into the following nine parts: (see the overall site plan)

Internal Medicine Hospital Two buildings

Surgical Hospital Two buildings

Obstetrics and Gynecology Hospital One building

Pediatrics Hospital One building

Outpatient Department and Otolaryngology and Ophthalmology Hospital One building

Nursing School and Dormitory One building

Management Office and Medical School One building

The above buildings are arranged with the Management Office and Medical School in the center, facing Fudong Outer Road. The Outpatient Department and Otolaryngology and Ophthalmology Hospital and the Nursing School and Dormitory are located on both sides. The other hospitals are arranged in a "fan-shaped" pattern to the south of the three, with their long sides roughly facing east and west. This arrangement is not only aesthetically pleasing, but also facilitates communication between departments, ensures air circulation, and provides ample light. Trapezoidal open spaces between the buildings are used as gardens for patients to relax during their recovery period. The total capacity of the hospitals is approximately 1,000 beds.

In addition to the above main buildings, there are auxiliary buildings such as staff residences, male and female staff dormitories, kitchens, service rooms, and workshops. The kitchens, service rooms, etc. are located in the southwest corner of the site, next to Funan Left Road and the Qiujiang River, to isolate them and maintain the tranquility of the hospitals. The prevailing winds in Shanghai come from the northeast, northwest, and southeast, so this arrangement ensures that the hospitals are not disturbed by smoke. Staff residences and dormitories are located in the southeast corner of the site, next to Huayuan Road and the Qiujiang River, and are also isolated from the main buildings. (B) Initial Project Considering the grand scale of the Municipal Hospital, the construction cost is naturally enormous, and it is necessary to carry out the project in phases to ease financial pressure. The first phase of the project is limited to meeting the current needs of diagnosis and treatment. The main buildings currently under construction are the Management Office and Medical School in the overall plan, which will be temporarily used for hospital purposes after completion. The building is approximately 80 meters long and 16 meters deep, with a building area of approximately 1,060 square meters. The total area of each floor is approximately 4,500 square meters, with six floors including the basement in the middle and four floors in the two wings.

The exterior adopts a simple and modern style with straight lines, matching the public buildings in the central administrative area. Because Chinese-style architecture is more expensive and the use of the site is difficult to be economical, it is not entirely adopted, but the decoration takes it as the standard, so that the spirit of the national culture is incorporated into modern equipment. This building is a steel-reinforced concrete structure, the outer walls are made of artificial stone, and the partition walls of the internal corridors are made of hollow bricks. Most of the internal partition walls are made of wood, so that they can be easily moved and rebuilt in the future. The floors of the wards are paved with rubber blocks, and the floors of the hall, operating rooms, and workshops are paved with polished stone. (To be continued)

Supplement to the New Year's Day issue of Shen Bao Pictorial

Life of Taiwanese Aborigines

— (Photos by Chen Xiehou, text by Hu Bozhou)

Taiwan is formed by merging Taiwan Island, the Penghu Islands, and affiliated islands, with an area of 2332 square miles. The climate is semi-tropical, the scenery is beautiful, the land is fertile, and it produces timber, tea, camphor, rawhide, sugar, rice, and other items. As early as the first year of Emperor Yang of Sui's Daye reign (605 AD), it had relations with our country. At that time, the area was entirely inhabited by uncivilized natives. During Emperor Xianzong of Tang's Yuanhe era, the Shi family moved to Penghu, and since then, large numbers of Han Chinese began to immigrate to Taiwan. In the early Yuan Dynasty, the post of patrol inspector was officially established in Penghu to manage civil affairs. In the late Ming Dynasty, it was occupied by the Dutch. Zheng Chenggong expelled the Dutch and took over the area, and actively managed it. He resisted the Manchu Qing. After the demise of the Zheng regime, it returned to Qing rule. It was ceded to Japan in the Sino-Japanese War. The Japanese, citing Taiwan's self-organized republic, carried out massacres, staining the entire island with blood. All the governors-general were naval and army generals who adopted a policy of pure military force. Then, they imposed heavy taxes to exploit and extract the blood and sweat of the Taiwanese people to enrich their homeland. Therefore, the Taiwanese people repeatedly rose up in revolution, attempting to overthrow Japanese rule. Up to 1919, there were a total of fourteen recorded uprisings. Last November, the Taiwan Revolutionary Party revolted and hundreds of people were arrested. Of Taiwan's 3.5 million people, apart from more than 100,000 aborigines and 140,000 Japanese, the rest are descendants of our country's Fujian and Guangdong people. Revolutionary ideas are very rich. Although under the rule of power, there will surely be a day of independence and freedom. As for the aboriginal peoples who were the earliest inhabitants of Taiwan, because our people colonized there, they gradually retreated from the plains to the mountains, cut off from the plains people, and unable to accept modern civilization, they still maintain their primitive lives. Only the aborigines on the eastern coast and those close to the plains have evolved slightly and know how to farm. The pictures published here give a glimpse. However, the Japanese government imposes heavy taxes on these evolved aborigines, equivalent to the Taiwanese, reaching more than thirty yuan per person per year.

(1) Distant View of Tianbao Rock

Hualien Port in eastern Taiwan has a mountain called Haishe Mountain, with a huge rock protruding from the deep valley on the summit, named Tianbao Rock. Standing on it, the wind caresses the clothes, as if soaring in the sky. Looking down, the deep ravine is bottomless, making people feel dizzy and afraid to look for long. Three aboriginal women are squatting on the edge of the rock, looking into the distance as if nothing is wrong.

(2) Aboriginal Beauty

Aborigines tattoo patterns on their heads, faces, and all parts of their bodies to be considered beautiful. The central aboriginal woman is the beauty of the aboriginal people. She also has tattoos on her forehead. When pointing straight to her eyebrows, she was weaving cloth outdoors.

(3) Aboriginal Suspension Bridge

The bridge is made of iron wire, with wooden planks laid on top, suspended high above the river valley. Only pedestrians can cross the bridge, no vehicles. It is hundreds of feet long and over a hundred feet high. Standing on it are four aborigines.

(4) Houses of the Hengchun Paiwan Tribe

The Paiwan are a type of uncivilized aborigines. The structure of their houses is quite unique. First, a wide ground cave is dug, and then naturally produced stone plates are densely covered on top as roof tiles, only a few feet above the ground. From a distance, it looks like a flat ground. Many of this tribe who live in the mountains live in mountain caves, making it difficult for aircraft to detect their location, so when there is a rebellion and suppression, they feel extremely difficult.

(5) Dabang Exchange

The Dabang Exchange is located in Alishan, Tainan, and was established by the Japanese. The aborigines bring what they have harvested to the exchange to exchange for what they need. What they like best is wine and matches. There are more than 100 such exchanges throughout Taiwan, operated by the Taiwan Police Association.

(6) Aboriginal Women Grinding Millet

The Alishan forest area is a timber production area, with an annual output value of two million yuan. There are many uncivilized aborigines in the mountains who used to go down the mountain to kill people and take their heads for sacrifice. Later, they were taught by Taiwanese Wu Feng, and this custom ceased. Recently, the Japanese government has carried out educational reforms, and many can speak Japanese. This shows the situation of aboriginal women from remote tribes in the mountains grinding millet.

Page 54

(1) West Peak of Mount Hua

— (Sent by Simao)

West Peak, also known as Lotus Peak, is slightly shorter than South Peak. Black pines grow in the crevices of the rocks. There are many stones that can be counted. There is a large piece of rock that is dozens of feet long floating on the top of the peak, broken into three parts. It is commonly known as the Axe-Split Stone. The bumps and dents on the stone that resemble toe marks are commonly called the Giant's Footprints, and are the same as the Immortal Palm of East Peak, which are commonly admired by people.

(2) Changkong Plank Road at Nantianmen

— (Photo by Yu Pingke)

Going west from Nantianmen, there is a narrow path called Changkong Plank Road. A three or four-inch wide path is built halfway up the cliff wall. Iron stakes are inserted into the wall to support narrow planks to make room for the feet. Horizontal iron chains are strung on the wall to hold onto. In the middle of the path where it is not connected up and down, double chains are hung to connect the people. People walking between them must stretch their arms and climb the chain to move their feet horizontally, which is extremely dangerous.

(3) Mountain Road on West Peak

— (Photo by Zhang Jinde)

Steps are carved out of stone, leaning against the mountain wall on the right and facing the deep valley on the left, which is also quite dangerous.

(4) Middle Peak of Mount Hua

— (Sent by Simao)

Middle Peak, also known as Jade Maiden Peak, is located to the left of East Peak. The house on the top of the peak is the famous Jade Maiden Palace.

(5) Nantianmen

— (Sent by Simao)

Nantianmen is located on the east side of South Peak, facing a deep ravine. Several ancient pine trees arch below, and the scenery is clear and beautiful.

(6) Sea of Clouds on Mount Hua

A peak rises out.

(7)

(8) Lao Jun's Navel

Many place names on Mount Hua are named after Lao Jun, such as Lao Jun's Plow Groove, Lao Jun's Alchemy Furnace, Lao Jun's Hanging Plow Place, and this one makes four.

Mount Hua in Shaanxi is the most majestic and towering mountain in our country's famous mountains. In the past, Han Tuizhi climbed to the top and looked down in horror, even writing a letter to his family to say goodbye. Its danger can be known. From the foot to the top, it was called forty li in ancient times. According to the latest actual measurement, it is about thirteen li. However, climbing is extremely difficult. The most dangerous places have been carved with stone steps or stone railings or wound with iron chains or paved with plank roads since the Tang Dynasty, so that tourists can easily reach its top. However, places such as Climbing Heaven Ladder and One Hundred Foot Gorge have inclination angles of up to 90 degrees, standing vertically against the wall and rising against the chest. Those with weak physical strength will return without success when they reach this point. The highest point is Luoyan Peak, about 8,000 feet above sea level. Standing on it, looking around, the north view of the mountain shade and the peaks are arranged at the foot, and the distant view of the He Luo and Wei plains and the high plains of the three Jin dynasties are vertical and horizontal for thousands of miles are all in sight. Looking south, the mountain faces a deep ravine. The mountains south of the ravine are continuous.

The pavilion is on the side of East Peak, on the top of a small peak. Tourists must climb down with their hands on the iron chain and crawl down before reaching it. It is said to be the place where Emperor Taizu of Song played chess with Chen Xiyi.

Exploring the Zilai Cave

There is an ancient Zilai Cave on Yu Huang Mountain in the south of Hangzhou. Legend has it that it can hold ten thousand people and the bottom of the cave leads directly to Huizhou in Anhui Province. In the past, the entrance of the cave was covered by weeds and smoke, and no one had ever explored it. Recently, the Hangzhou National News Agency and the National Army joined forces to form a Zilai Cave exploration team in order to break various superstitions and inspire the national spirit of adventure. The exploration revealed that the claim of reaching Huizhou was completely unfounded. The cave is approximately 150 yards deep. The path into the cave is rugged, and the cave floor is as flat as a water surface, formed of fine mud. The team placed a pre-prepared commemorative wooden plaque at the deepest point of the cave. Afterwards, it was announced that anyone who independently retrieved the commemorative plaque would be rewarded. The news from the Hangzhou National News Agency spread, and Cantonese athletic experts such as Zhou Zhaohua entered the cave and retrieved the wooden plaque. Subsequently, the number of visitors increased daily. The Military Coordination Committee then cut rocks and erected wooden structures in the cave to facilitate tourists. Since then, another scenic spot has been added between the Three Tianzhu Temples and the Six Bridges.
